Salah — Prayer
beginner
5 min
What is Not Disliked for the Praying Person
Ruling statement on permissible attire and recommended sutra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the actions that are not disliked during prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify when a permissible action becomes disliked.

Core Idea
Wearing a belt or sword in prayer is permissible if it does not distract.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies that certain attire like belts and swords do not make prayer disliked. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the ruling depends on whether the item distracts the person. Additionally, the passage highlights the virtue of having a sutra (screen) in front of the prayer, but its absence does not make the prayer disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and default ruling
Read the Arabic: 'لا يكره له شد الوسط ولا تقلد بسيف..' — list the specific actions: tightening the belt, wearing a sword or similar, and the ambiguous phrase 'ولا عدم إدخال'. Note that the ruling is 'la yukrahu' (not disliked).
The term 'لا يكره' means it is permissible (mubah), not even disliked.
2
Apply the condition
The text adds 'إذا لم يشتغل بحركته' — if he does not become occupied with its movement. So the permissibility is conditional on the absence of distracting movement.
If the item moves and distracts, it becomes disliked (makruh).
3
Distinguish between ruling and recommendation
After stating what is not disliked, the text mentions 'يستحب له' (it is recommended) and quotes hadiths about the sutra. Recognize that having a sutra is recommended (mustahab), not obligatory, and not having it is not disliked.
The hadiths emphasize the virtue, not the necessity.
4
Resolve the ambiguous phrase
'ولا عدم إدخال' is unclear. Some scholars interpret it as 'nor is it disliked not to enter [the prayer with a sutra]' — i.e., praying without a sutra is not disliked, though it is recommended to have one.
This aligns with the later recommendation of the sutra.
5
Conclude the ruling hierarchy
Summarize: The default ruling for wearing belt/sword is mubah; if distracted, it becomes makruh. The sutra is mustahab; its absence is neither obligatory nor disliked.
Know the distinction between mubah and mustahab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما لا يكره للمصلي
لا يكره له شد الوسط ولا تقلد بسيف ونحوه إذا لم يشتغل بحركته، ولا عدم إدخال
يستحب له:
ورد عن عمر رضي الله عنه: لو علم المصلي ما ينقص من صلاته ما صلى إلا إلى شيء يستره من الناس.
وعن ابن مسعود إنه ليقطع نصف صلاة المرء المرور بين يديه.
Chapter on what is not disliked for the praying person. It is not disliked for him to tighten the middle [belt] nor to wear a sword or like it if he does not become occupied with its movement, nor the absence of entering. It is recommended: It is reported from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If the praying person knew what is diminished from his prayer, he would not pray except towards something that screens him from people.' And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Indeed the passing in front of a man cuts half of his prayer.'
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This is a short matn passage listing what is not disliked (makruh) during prayer. The first ruling: wearing a belt or a sword is not disliked as long as one is not preoccupied with their movement. This is because such items are part of normal attire and do not necessarily distract. The second point: it is not disliked not to enter? The text is ambiguous; the phrase 'wa la 'adam idkhal' likely means 'nor is it disliked not to enter', possibly referring to entering a place? However, the commentary might clarify. Then the text says 'it is recommended' and quotes two hadiths about the virtue of having a sutra. From 'Umar: if the praying person knew the loss in his prayer, he would pray only towards something that screens him. From Ibn Mas'ud: passing cuts half of the prayer. These underscore the importance of the sutra but note that not having it is not disliked in the sense that the prayer is valid, though it is recommended to have it.

Key Terms
لا يكره (la yukrahu): Legally, this indicates that an action is permissible and not disliked (makruh tanzihan or tahriman).
سدل (shadd al-wasat): Tightening a belt or sash around the waist.
تقليد (taqlid): Wearing or putting on, especially a sword or similar item.
سترة (sutra): An object placed in front of the praying person to prevent people from passing directly in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a man praying while wearing a sword that is not moving?
A) It is disliked (makruh tanzihan).
B) It is permissible and not disliked.
C) It invalidates the prayer.
D) It is recommended (mustahab).

Key Takeaway
Wearing a belt or sword in prayer is permissible (not makruh) as long as it does not cause distracting movement.

Salah — Prayer

The Sutra and Repelling Passersby in Prayer
Rulings on sutra, drawing a line, and repelling passersby.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah practices regarding sutra, explain the ruling on drawing a line, and apply the correct sequence for repelling a passerby.

Core Idea
The sutra is sunnah; repelling is permitted by gesture but fighting is abrogated.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the recommended practices related to the sutra (screen) for the person praying. It covers the specifications of the sutra, the option of drawing a line when no object is available, and the etiquette of repelling a passerby. The passage also clarifies a common misunderstanding about fighting the passerby, which has been abrogated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling level for sutra and line
Note that both the sutra and drawing a line are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) according to the Hanafi school.
This is derived from the imperative in the hadith, interpreted as recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the physical specifications
The sutra should be about a forearm in length and finger thickness. It should be placed near one's eyebrow, not directly facing it.
Directly facing it (صمداً) is avoided; the sutra is positioned slightly to the side.
3
Analyze the alternative: drawing a line
If no object is available, a line may be drawn lengthwise (or crosswise like a crescent). Early Hanafis disliked it, but later scholars permitted it following the sunnah.
The hadith 'If he does not have a stick, let him draw a line' is the evidence.
4
Learn the repelling hierarchy
First, gesture or say tasbih. If close, gently push once. Do not fight. For women, use gesture or clapping without voice.
If the passerby is far, gesture or tasbih suffices. For animals like cats, push with foot or object.
5
Recognize the abrogation of the fighting hadith
The hadith allowing fighting is interpreted as abrogated by the later principle that prayer occupies one fully, as per the hadith 'There is engagement in prayer.'
This resolves the apparent conflict with the earlier report.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[مراقي الفلاح (٣٦٦] ترك اتخذ سترة أو لم يتخذها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٦٧] التصفيق: صفق فلان يديه ضرب بباطن الراحة على الأخرى، وصفق بيديه صوت بهما ضربا. أقرب الموارد) ولا ترفع لا بالقراءة ولا بالتسبيح. مراقي الفلاح ولا يقاتل إلخ الحاصل أنه إذا قصد المرور بين يديه إن كان قريبا منه يمكنه مدافعته بدون مشي أشار إليه أولاً ليرجع أو يسبح، فإن لم يرجع دفعه مرةً بلطف، فإن لم يرجع تركه ولا يقاتله، وإن كان بعيداً عنه إن شاء أشار إليه، وإن شاء سبح فقط، وإذا مر بين يديه ما لا تؤثر فيه الإشارة كهرة دفعه برجله أو ألصقه إلى السترة، كذا في العيني على البخاري [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٦٨] وما ورد إلخ أي ما ورد به من قوله : "إذا كان أحدكم يصلي فلا يدع أحدا يمر بين يديه، وليدرأ ما استطاع، فإن أبي فليقاتله، إنما هو شيطان فهو مؤول بأنه كان جواز مقاتلته في ابتداء الإسلام والعمل المنافي للصلاة كان مباحا فيها إذ ذاك، وقد نسخ بقوله : " إن في الصلاة لشغلاً". [مراقي الفلاح والطحطاوي: ٣٦٨]
It is recommended for him to fix a sutra the length of a forearm or more, the thickness of a finger, and the sunnah is to get close to it and place it on one of his eyebrows, not facing it directly. If he does not find something to erect, let him draw a line lengthwise, and they said crosswise like a crescent. It is recommended to leave repelling a passerby, and repelling by gesture or tasbih is permitted, and it is disliked to combine both. He repels by raising the voice with recitation, with head or eye or other. She repels by gesture or clapping with the back of the fingers of the right hand on the palm of the left, and she does not raise her voice because it is fitnah. He does not fight the passerby, and what is reported is interpreted as it was permitted and abrogated. The waw is circumstantial. It is recommended for him: narrated from Umar: 'If the worshiper knew what he loses of his prayer, he would not pray except to something that screens him from people.' And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Passing between the hands of a person praying cuts off half of his prayer.' [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 365] 'He does not face it directly': meaning he does not face it straight, but rather inclines from it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 366] 'Let him draw a line': some early scholars disliked it, later scholars permitted it because following the sunnah is better; as it is narrated in the Sunan from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'If he does not have a stick, let him draw a line.' [Maraqi al-Falah: 366] 'Whether he takes a sutra or not.' [Maraqi al-Falah: 367] 'Clapping': a person claps his hands by striking the palm with the back of the other, and he claps by making a sound with them. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) 'She does not raise': not by recitation nor by tasbih. [Maraqi al-Falah] 'He does not fight': the summary is that if someone intends to pass in front of him, if he is close and can repel without walking, he gestures first for him to return or he glorifies; if he does not return, he pushes him once gently; if he does not return, he leaves him and does not fight him. If he is far away, he may gesture or glorify as he wishes. If something that gesture does not affect, like a cat, passes in front of him, he pushes it with his foot or attaches it to the sutra. This is in al-Ayni on al-Bukhari. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 368] 'What is reported': meaning what is reported from him (peace be upon him): 'When one of you prays, do not let anyone pass in front of him, and let him repel as much as he can; if he refuses, let him fight him, for it is a devil.' It is interpreted that the permissibility of fighting was in early Islam, and actions contrary to prayer were permissible then, and it was abrogated by his statement: 'There is engagement in prayer.' [Maraqi al-Falah and al-Tahtawi: 368]
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the etiquette of sutra and dealing with passersby during prayer. The author begins by stating it is recommended (mustahabb) to plant a sutra of a forearm's length or more, about finger thickness. It is sunnah to stand close to it and position it at one's eyebrow, not directly facing it. If no object is available, one should draw a line lengthwise (some say crosswise like a crescent). It is recommended not to repel a passerby, but if needed, repelling by gesture or tasbih is permitted; combining both is disliked. Repelling by raising the voice with recitation or moving the head/eyes is allowed. For women, they repel by gesture or clapping (back of right fingers on left palm) without raising their voice due to fitnah. The person should not fight the passerby; reported hadith about fighting are interpreted as abrogated by the principle that prayer occupies one fully. The commentary expands with evidence from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, and explains the sunnah of the line drawing, citing the hadith: 'If he does not have a stick, let him draw a line.' The commentator clarifies the sequence of repelling: first gesture/tasbih, then gentle push if close, but never fight. For animals like cats, use foot or object. The abrogation of fighting in prayer is supported by a hadith.

Key Terms
سترة (sutra): An object placed in front of the praying person to screen him from passersby.
تصفيق (tasfiq): Clapping the back of the right fingers on the left palm to alert without voice (for women).
مرور (murur): Passing in front of a praying person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a woman do if someone passes in front of her during prayer?
A) She should raise her voice and say 'Subhanallah'
B) She should clap with the back of her right fingers on her left palm
C) She should push the passerby with her hand
D) She should remain silent and not repel

Key Takeaway
The sutra is sunnah; the line is a valid substitute; repelling should be done gently, and fighting is not allowed.

Actions Not Disliked in Prayer: The Hanafi Rulings and Proof
Listing actions not disliked in prayer with proof for contested items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions are not disliked in Hanafi prayer and state the evidence for facing a sword or mushaf.

Core Idea
Facing a sword or mushaf in prayer is not disliked; the Prophet's practice and Quranic command support this.

In this section, the author lists various actions that do not render the prayer disliked (makruh). While some may seem contrary to the spirit of khushu', the Hanafi school considers them permissible based on prophetic practice and explicit proof. We will examine these rulings and the evidence behind the more contested items, particularly facing a sword or Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage begins by stating that certain actions are not disliked for the praying person. Understand that the default in Hanafi fiqh is permissibility unless a clear proof indicates dislike.
The term 'la yukrah' (not disliked) means the act is permissible (mubah) and sometimes recommended if there is a need.
2
List the permissible actions
Go through each item: tightening the waist, wearing a sword if not distracted, not inserting hands into a farjiyyah, facing a mushaf, hanging sword, back of a seated person talking, candle or lamp, prostrating on a rug with images not prostrated on, killing a harmful creature if feared, shaking garment to prevent sticking in ruku', wiping forehead after prayer or before if harmful/distracting, looking with the corner of the eye, praying on carpets, and repeating a surah in nafl.
Some items have conditions, e.g., killing harmful creatures requires fear of harm.
3
Examine the contested items
The commentary focuses on facing a mushaf and sword. Some scholars disliked these acts due to resemblance to the People of the Book (for the mushaf) or because a sword is a weapon (as said by Ibn Umar).
The Hanafi response: the Prophet prayed towards the 'anazah (a short spear), and Allah commands taking weapons in fear prayer (Quran 4:102). Thus it is not disliked.
4
Identify the conditions
For killing harmful creatures, the condition is fear (khawf). If safe, a lot of action becomes disliked. For wiping forehead before prayer, it is only allowed if it harms or distracts.
These conditions prevent the act from being considered disliked.
5
Understand the chosen positions
The author states the chosen view (al-mukhtar) for the farjiyyah: not inserting hands is not disliked. For the other items, the 'correct view' (al-sahih) is given.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) for all listed actions is that they are not disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما لا يكره للمصلي لا يكره له شد الوسط ولا تقلد بسيف ونحوه إذا لم يشتغل بحركته، ولا عدم إدخال يديه في فرجيّه وشقه على المختار ولا التوجه لمصحف أو سيف معلق أو ظهر قاعد يتحدث أو شمع أو سراج على الصحيح، والسجود على بساط فيه تصاوير لم يسجد عليها، وقتل حية وعقرب خاف أذاهما ولو بضربات وانحراف عن القبلة في الأظهر، ولا بأس بنفض ثوبه كيلا يلتصق بجسده في الركوع، ولا بمسح جبهته من التراب أو الحشيش بعد الفراغ من الصلاة ولا قبل الفراغ إذا ضره، أو شغله عن الصلاة، ولا بالنظر بموق عينيه من غير تحويل الوجه، ولا بأس بالصلاة على الفرش والبسط، واللبود، والأفضل الصلاة على الأرض أو على ما تُنبتُه ، ولا بأس بتكرار السورة في الركعتين من النفل. فرجيه هو قباء شق من . خلفه وشقه على المختار: اختلف في هذا اللفظ، وعندي أن المراد به ذيل القباء، وقال بعض المحققين: لعله شقة بالضم من الثياب، وربما قالوه بالكسر، ويؤيده ما في "الصحاح"، وما في "الفتاوى الأنقروية" من أنه إذا لبس شقة أو فرجياً و لم يدخل يديه اختلف المتأخرون فيه، والمختار أنه لا يكره. ولا التوجه إلخ إنما أورد هذه المسألة هكذا؛ لأن من العلماء من كره هذا فقالوا أما السيف فإنه آلة الحرب، وفي الحديد بأس شديد فلا يليق تقديمه في مقام الابتهال، وقيل: هو قول ابن عمر ، وأما في استقبال المصحف فإن فيه تشبها بأهل الكتاب؛ فإنهم كانوا يفعلون ذلك بكتبهم، وقيل: هو قول إبراهيم النخعي له؛ لأنا نقول: لا يفعلون ذلك عبادة، لكن ليقرؤوا منه في صلاتهم، وذلك يكون مكروهاً عندنا، ولأنه لو كان موضوعاً أمام المصلي، فليس به بأس، فكذا إذا كان معلقا، وأما السيف قلنا: نعم إنه آلة الحرب، لكن الموضع موضع الحرب، ولهذا يسمى محرابا فيليق هو فيه، ولأنا أمرنا بأخذ الأسلحة في صلاة الخوف، قال الله تعالى: وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ (النساء: (۱۰۲)، فإذا كان معلقاً بين يديه كان أمكن من أخذه إذا احتاج إليه، يوجب الكراهة، وقد كانت العنزة تحمل أمام رسول الله ، فكانت تركز بين يديه، فيصلي إليها، وهي سلاح، فتبين أنه لا بأس بالسلاح بين يدي المصلي. [الكفاية: ٣٦١/١] أو شمع قال ابن قتيبة في باب ما جاء فيه :لغتان استعمل الناس أضعفهما، الشمع بالسكون والأوجه فتح الميم. (حاشية الطحطاوي) خاف أذاهما إلخ قيد بالخوف؛ لأنه مع الأمن يكره العمل الكثير. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٠] ولا قبل الفراغ الخ: أي ولا بأس بمسح التراب قبل الفراغ من الصلاة إذا ضره أو شغله الصلاة عن خشوع مثل العرق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۰] بالنظر إلخ والأولى تركه بغير حاجة؛ لما فيه من ترك الأدب بالنظر إلى محل . السجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٠]
Section on what is not disliked for the praying person. It is not disliked for him to tighten his waist, nor to put on a sword and the like if he is not occupied by its movement, nor to not insert his hands into his farjiyyah and its slit according to the chosen view, nor to face a mushaf or hanging sword or the back of a sitting person talking, or a candle or lamp according to the correct view, nor to prostrate on a rug containing images that he did not prostrate on, nor to kill a snake or scorpion if he fears their harm even with multiple strikes and deviation from the qibla in the most apparent view. There is no harm in shaking his garment so it does not stick to his body in ruku', nor in wiping his forehead from dust or grass after finishing the prayer, nor before finishing if it harms him or distracts him from the prayer, nor in looking with the corner of his eye without turning his face. There is no harm in praying on beds, carpets, and felts, but it is better to pray on the ground or on what it grows. There is no harm in repeating a surah in the two rak'ahs of nafl. Farjiyyah is a garment slit from behind. And its slit according to the chosen view: there is difference in this wording; I think it means the tail of the garment. Some investigators said: perhaps it is shiqqa (with dammah) from clothing, and sometimes they say it with kasrah, supported by al-Sihah and al-Fatawa al-Anqrawwiyyah that if he wears a shiqqa or farjiyya and does not insert his hands, the later scholars differed, and the chosen view is that it is not disliked. 'Nor to face' etc. He only brought up this issue because some scholars disliked it. They said: as for the sword, it is a tool of war, and iron has severe danger, so it is not fitting to present it in a place of supplication. It is said that this is the view of Ibn Umar. As for facing the mushaf, it is resembling the People of the Book, for they used to face their books. It is said that this is the view of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. But we say: they do not do it as worship, but to recite from it in prayer, and that would be disliked with us, because if it is placed in front of the worshiper, there is no harm, so also if it is hanging. As for the sword, we say: yes, it is a tool of war, but the place is a place of war, therefore it is called a mihrab, so it fits. We are commanded to take weapons in the prayer of fear, Allah says: 'And let them take their arms' (4:102). So if it is hanging before him, it is more possible to take it when needed, this does not cause dislike. The 'anazah (short spear) was carried before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and it was planted before him, and he prayed towards it, and it is a weapon. So it is clear that there is no harm in having a weapon in front of the worshiper. [al-Kifayah: 361/1] 'Or a candle': Ibn Qutaybah said in the chapter on what came: two forms, people use the weaker one, 'sham' with sukun, and the more correct is with fatha on the meem. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) 'He fears their harm' etc.: it is conditioned by fear, because with safety, a lot of action is disliked. [Maraqi al-Falah: 370] 'Nor before finishing': meaning there is no harm in wiping dust before finishing the prayer if it harms him or distracts him from humility like sweat. [Maraqi al-Falah: 370] 'Looking' etc.: it is better to leave it without need because it is abandoning the etiquette of looking at the place of prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah: 370]
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a section on actions that are not disliked (makruh) for the praying person. The author lists several: tightening the waist, wearing a sword if not distracted by its movement, not inserting hands into a farjiyyah garment (the chosen view), facing a mushaf (Quran), hanging sword, the back of a seated person talking, a candle or lamp (correct view), prostrating on a rug with images not prostrated on, killing a snake or scorpion if feared (even with multiple strikes and turning from qibla in the most apparent view). It is permissible to shake one's garment to prevent sticking in ruku', wipe forehead from dust after prayer (or before if it harms or distracts), look with the corner of the eye without turning the head. Praying on carpets is allowed, but ground is better. Repeating a surah in nafl is allowed. The commentary then discusses the definition of farjiyyah and settles on the chosen view. It defends facing the mushaf or sword by citing the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) with the 'anazah and the verse on arms in fear prayer. It also notes the condition of fear for killing harmful creatures, and clarifies that looking around without turning the face is permissible but better left.

Key Terms
فرجيه (farjiyyah): A garment with a slit at the back, worn like a cloak.
عنزة (anazah): A short spear used as a sutra for the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should a person handle a scorpion crawling near him during prayer?
A) He must ignore it and continue praying
B) He may kill it with multiple strikes even if he turns away from the qibla
C) He can only kill it if he remains facing the qibla
D) He should seek help from someone else

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, many actions that might seem disruptive are not disliked, especially when based on prophetic practice or necessity; knowing these rulings helps maintain focus and avoid unnecessary scrupulosity.

Facing a Mushaf or Sword During Prayer: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on actions not disliked with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing a mushaf or hanging sword during prayer, identify the opposing view, and explain the Hanafi evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Praying toward a weapon or mushaf is not disliked; the Prophet prayed toward a spear.

Many Muslims wonder if it is permissible to pray facing a copy of the Quran or a weapon hanging on the wall. Some scholars consider this disliked, but the Hanafi school takes a clear position: it is not disliked, based on the Prophet's practice and a Quranic command. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the reasoning behind the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify from the passage which actions are declared 'not disliked' (la yukrah). Focus on the specific case of facing a mushaf or a hanging sword.
The term 'la yukrah' in Hanafi fiqh means the action falls under mubah (permissible) or better.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Find the views of Ibn Umar and Ibrahim al-Nakhai. What reasoning did they use to consider these actions disliked?
Opponents argue the sword is a tool of war and iron is harmful; the mushaf imitation of People of the Book.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Trace how the Hanafis counter each objection. For the sword: cite the Prophet's 'anazah and the concept of mihrab. For the mushaf: distinguish between using it for recitation (which is disliked) and simply facing it.
The Hanafi response uses both dalil naqli (Quran, Sunnah) and rational argument.
4
Examine the specific evidence
Look at the Quranic verse (4:102) and the hadith of the 'anazah. Understand how these prove permissibility.
The verse commands taking weapons in the prayer of fear, indicating weapons are not inherently incompatible with prayer.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Contrast the Hanafi position with the opposing view. What practical ruling changes?
A Hanafi may pray facing a mushaf or sword without dislike; followers of the other view would avoid it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما لا يكره المصلي يديه في فرجيّه وشقه على المختار ولا التوجه لمصحف أو سيف معلق أو ظهر قاعد يتحدث أو شمع أو سراج على الصحيح، والسجود على بساط فيه تصاوير لم يسجد عليها، وقتل حية وعقرب خاف أذاهما ولو بضربات وانحراف عن القبلة في الأظهر، ولا بأس بنفض ثوبه كيلا يلتصق بجسده في الركوع، ولا بمسح جبهته من التراب أو الحشيش بعد الفراغ من الصلاة ولا قبل الفراغ إذا ضره، أو شغله عن الصلاة، ولا بالنظر بموق عينيه من غير تحويل الوجه، ولا بأس بالصلاة على الفرش والبسط، واللبود، والأفضل الصلاة على الأرض أو على ما تُنبتُه، ولا بأس بتكرار السورة في الركعتين من النفل. فرجيه هو قباء شق من خلفه وشقه على المختار: اختلف في هذا اللفظ، وعندي أن المراد به ذيل القباء، وقال بعض المحققين: لعله شقة بالضم من الثياب، وربما قالوه بالكسر، ويؤيده ما في "الصحاح"، وما في "الفتاوى الأنقروية" من أنه إذا لبس شقة أو فرجياً و لم يدخل يديه اختلف المتأخرون فيه، والمختار أنه لا يكره. ولا التوجه إلخ إنما أورد هذه المسألة هكذا؛ لأن من العلماء من كره هذا فقالوا أما السيف فإنه آلة الحرب، وفي الحديد بأس شديد فلا يليق تقديمه في مقام الابتهال، وقيل: هو قول ابن عمر، وأما في استقبال المصحف فإن فيه تشبها بأهل الكتاب؛ فإنهم كانوا يفعلون ذلك بكتبهم، وقيل: هو قول إبراهيم النخعي له؛ لأنا نقول: لا يفعلون ذلك عبادة، لكن ليقرؤوا منه في صلاتهم، وذلك يكون مكروهاً عندنا، ولأنه لو كان موضوعاً أمام المصلي، فليس به بأس، فكذا إذا كان معلقا، وأما السيف قلنا: نعم إنه آلة الحرب، لكن الموضع موضع الحرب، ولهذا يسمى محرابا فيليق هو فيه، ولأنا أمرنا بأخذ الأسلحة في صلاة الخوف، قال الله تعالى: وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ (النساء: ١٠٢)، فإذا كان معلقاً بين يديه كان أمكن من أخذه إذا احتاج إليه، يوجب الكراهة، وقد كانت العنزة تحمل أمام رسول الله، فكانت تركز بين يديه، فيصلي إليها، وهي سلاح، فتبين أنه لا بأس بالسلاح بين يدي المصلي. [الكفاية: ٣٦١/١] أو شمع قال ابن قتيبة في باب ما جاء فيه :لغتان استعمل الناس أضعفهما، الشمع بالسكون والأوجه فتح الميم. (حاشية الطحطاوي) خاف أذاهما إلخ قيد بالخوف؛ لأنه مع الأمن يكره العمل الكثير. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٠] ولا قبل الفراغ الخ: أي ولا بأس بمسح التراب قبل الفراغ من الصلاة إذا ضره أو شغله الصلاة عن خشوع مثل العرق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۰] بالنظر إلخ والأولى تركه بغير حاجة؛ لما فيه من ترك الأدب بالنظر إلى محل السجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٠] فلا
There is no dislike for the praying person placing his hands in the openings of his garment (farjiyya) and its shiqq (side slit) according to the chosen view, nor for facing a mushaf, a hanging sword, the back of a seated person talking, a candle, or a lamp according to the sound view; nor for prostrating on a mat with images (pictures of animate beings) as long as he did not prostrate directly on them; nor for killing a snake or scorpion if he fears harm from them, even with multiple blows or turning away from the qibla according to the most apparent view; there is no harm in shaking his garment so it does not stick to his body during ruku; nor in wiping his forehead of dust or grass after finishing prayer, and not before finishing if it harms him or distracts him from prayer; nor in looking toward the edge of his eyes without turning his face; there is no harm in praying on carpets, spreads, and felts, but praying on the ground or on what grows from it is better; there is no harm in repeating a surah in the two rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer. Commentary: 'Farjiyya' is a robe slit at the back, and 'shiqq' according to the chosen view — there is disagreement over this word; in my view it means the tail of the robe, and some researchers said it is 'shiqqa' (with dammah on shin) meaning a garment, and sometimes they say it with kasrah, supported by what is in 'al-Sihah' and 'al-Fatawa al-Anqrawiyya': that when one wears a shiqq or farjiyya and does not insert his hands, later scholars differed, and the chosen view is that it is not disliked. 'Nor for facing' etc. — he only brought this issue because some scholars disliked it, saying of the sword that it is a weapon, and iron is severely harmful, so it is not proper to present it in a place of supplication; it is said this is the view of Ibn Umar. As for facing the mushaf, it involves imitating the People of the Book, as they did that with their books; it is said this is the view of Ibrahim al-Nakhai. We (Hanafis) say: they do not do that as worship, but to recite from it during prayer, and that would be disliked according to us; and if it were placed in front of the worshiper, there is no harm, so likewise if it is hanging. As for the sword, we say: yes, it is a weapon, but the place is a place of warfare; for this reason it is called 'mihrab' (from harb, war), so it befits it; and we are commanded to take weapons in the prayer of fear; Allah said: 'And let them take their weapons' (4:102); so if it is hanging before him, it is more accessible for him to take it if needed; this does not necessitate dislike. The 'anazah (short spear) used to be carried before the Prophet, then planted before him, and he prayed toward it, and it was a weapon, so it shows that there is no harm in having a weapon in front of the worshiper. [al-Kifaya: 361/1] 'or a candle' — Ibn Qutayba said in the chapter on what has come: there are two pronunciations, people use the weaker one: 'sham' with sukun, and the more correct is with fatha on the mim. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) 'Fears their harm' etc. — conditioned by fear; because if secure, much action is disliked. [Maraqi al-Falah: 370] 'And not before finishing' etc. — meaning there is no harm in wiping dust before finishing prayer if it harms him or distracts him from humility like sweat. [Maraqi al-Falah: 370] 'Looking' etc. — it is better to leave it without need, because it involves abandoning proper conduct by looking toward the place of prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah: 370] (rest is unclear)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from various sources, addresses actions often thought to be disliked (makruh) during prayer. The author first lists actions that are not disliked, based on the chosen view or the sound view. The commentary expands on each, particularly focusing on the garment issue (farjiyya and shiqq) and the direction toward a mushaf or sword. For the garment, there is a debate about the meaning of 'shiqq', but the chosen view is that not inserting hands into the sleeves of such a garment is not disliked. The major dispute is over facing a mushaf (Quranic manuscript) or a hanging sword during prayer. Some scholars, including Ibn Umar and Ibrahim al-Nakhai, considered this disliked, either because it imitates the People of the Book or because a sword is a tool of war unfitting for prayer. The Hanafi response counters both points: facing the mushaf is permissible because one may read from it in prayer (though that specific act would be disliked, but simply facing it is not); as for the sword, they cite the practice of the Prophet who prayed toward a spear ('anazah) and the Quranic command to take weapons in the prayer of fear (4:102). Thus, the Hanafi position is that these are not disliked. The passage also clarifies other permissible actions like prostrating on a mat with images (as long as not directly on the images), killing a harmful snake/scorpion, shaking clothes, wiping forehead after prayer, etc. Emphasis is on avoiding excessive movement (amal kathir) only if secure; otherwise, small movements are allowed.

Key Terms
فرجيه (farjiyya): A type of garment with a slit at the back or front; the text defines it as a robe slit from behind (qaba shaq min khalfihi).
شقة (shiqqa): A piece of cloth or garment, possibly a garment without sleeves; the text discusses whether the term is with dammah or kasrah on the shin.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action whose avoidance is rewarded but commission is not punished unless it approaches haram (makruh tahrimi).
عنزة (anazah): A short spear, similar to a staff, used by the Prophet as a sutra during prayer.
محراب (mihrab): Prayer niche; derived from 'harb' (war), indicating a place of struggle against the ego or enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is sunnah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, facing a mushaf or hanging sword during prayer is not disliked, due to the Prophet's practice and the Quranic allowance of weapons in prayer.

When Cutting the Prayer is Obligatory or Permissible
Enumeration of cases where cutting the prayer is obligatory or permissible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify scenarios where cutting the prayer is wajib or ja'iz, and apply the condition of ghalabat al-zann to distinguish between permissible and obligatory cutting.

Core Idea
Cutting prayer to save a life is wajib; to prevent loss of property or harm is ja'iz, but becomes wajib if harm is certain.

This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah, details the Hanafi rulings on cutting the prayer (qat' al-salah). It distinguishes between obligatory cutting for emergencies like a distressed person's cry for help, and permissible cutting for lesser harms like theft or fear of an animal. Understanding these cases protects against both sinful abandonment and negligent inaction in the face of real danger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling categories
The passage classifies cutting prayer into obligatory (wajib) and permissible (ja'iz). Also notes when cutting is not required (e.g., parental call).
2
Examine istighatha (distress call)
The first case: a distressed person (malhuf) calls for help. Cutting is wajib even for obligatory prayer. This is based on necessity (darura).
Commentary clarifies examples: seized by oppressor, drowning, animal attack.
3
Analyze theft and fear scenarios
Cutting is permissible for theft of at least one dirham, even if from someone else. Also for fear of a wolf among sheep, or fear of a blind person falling into a well. The ruling becomes wajib if there is dominant presumption (ghalabat al-zann) of harm.
Ghalabat al-zann is a key threshold: it upgrades ja'iz to wajib.
4
Review midwife and traveler cases
A midwife may delay or cut prayer if she fears for the child's life, and must do so if ghalabat al-zann applies. A traveler fearing thieves may delay the time-bound prayer.
The midwife must prioritize saving life over prayer timing.
5
Differentiate parental call
A call from parents without distress does not make cutting obligatory. Al-Tahawi adds: in supererogatory prayer, if parent knows you're praying, do not respond; if ignorant, you may respond.
This is an intra-Hanafi nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب قطع الصلاة باستغاثة ملهوف بالمصلي لا بنداء أحد أبويه، ويجوز قطعها بسرقة ولو كانت فرضاً ما يساوي درهما ولو لغيره، وخوف ذئب على غنم أو خوف تردّي أعمى في بئر ونحوه، وإذا خافت القابلة موت الولد وإلا فلا بأس بتأخيرها الصلاة، وتقبل على الولد، وكذا المسافر إذا خاف من اللصوص أو قطاع الطريق، جاز له تأخير الوقتية، وتارك الصلاة عمدا كسلا يضرب ضربا شديدا حتى يسيل منه الدم، ويحبس حتى يصليها، وكذا تارك صوم رمضان ولا يقتل إلا إذا جحد أو استخف بأحدهما. باستغاثة ملهوف إلخ كما لو تعلق به ظالم، أو وقع في ماء، أو صال عليه حيوان فاستغاث بالمصلي. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۱] لا بنداء إلخ أي لا يجب قطع الصلاة بنداء أحد أبويه من غير استغاثة؛ لأن قطع الصلاة لا يجوز إلا لضرورة، وقال الطحاوي هذا في الفرض وإن كان في نافلة إن علم أحد أبويه أنه في وناداه لا يجيبه وإن لم يعلم يجيبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۱] ولو لغيره: أي ولو كان المسروق لغير المصلي. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۲] خوف تردي الخ: [مصدر تفعل بمعنى سقوط] أي إذا خاف المصلي أن أعمى من العميان يتردى في بئر ونحوها جاز له قطع الصلاة، وهذا إذا لم يغلب على ظنه سقوطه، وإذا غلب على ظنه سقوطه وجب قطع الصلاة ولو كانت فرضاً. وإذا خافت إلخ [أي يجوز قطعها الصلاة إذا خافت والوجوب عند غلبة الظن بموت الولد كالوجوب عند غلبة السقوط وهو كما إذا خافت القابلة - وهي المرأة التي يقال لها وايه - تتلقى الولد حال خروجه من بطن أمه إن غلب على ظنها موت الولد، أو تلف عضو منه، أو أمه بتركها وجب عليها تأخير الصلاة عن وقتها، وقطعها لو كانت فيها، وإن لم يغلب على ظنها فلا بأس بتأخيرها الصلاة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٣] وإلا فلا بأس أي وإن لم تخف القابلة موت الولد، بل غلب على ظنها موته فلا بأس إن أخرت الصلاة عن وقتها وتركتها رأساً، وقضاها بعده ولا يقتل إلخ أي ولا يقتل بمجرد ترك الصلاة والصوم مع الإقرار بفرضيتهما إلا إذا جحد افتراض الصلاة أو الصوم؛ لإنكاره ما كان معلوماً من الدين إجماعاً، أو استخف بأحدهما كما لو أظهر الإفطار في نهار رمضان بلا عذر تهاوناً، أو نطق بما يدل عليه، فيكون حكمه حكم المرتد، فتكشف شبهته ويحبس، ثم يقتل إن أصر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٣]
It is obligatory to cut the prayer due to a distressed person's cry for help directed at the praying person, but not due to a call from one of his parents (without distress). It is permissible to cut it for theft, even if the prayer is obligatory, of something worth one dirham, even if belonging to someone else; fear of a wolf for sheep, or fear that a blind person may fall into a well and the like; and if the midwife fears the death of the child, otherwise there is no harm in her delaying the prayer and attending to the child; likewise a traveler, if he fears thieves or highway robbers, it is permissible for him to delay the time-bound prayer. The one who deliberately leaves prayer out of laziness is severely beaten until blood flows, and imprisoned until he performs it; likewise the one who leaves the fast of Ramadan, but he is not killed unless he denies (the obligation) or shows contempt for either. Commentary: 'Due to a distressed person's cry for help' etc. — like if an oppressor seizes him, or he falls into water, or an animal attacks him and he seeks the help of the praying person. [Maraqi al-Falah: 371] 'Not due to a call' etc. — meaning it is not obligatory to cut the prayer due to a call from one of his parents without a cry for help; because cutting prayer is only allowed for necessity. Al-Tahawi said: this is in obligatory prayer; if it is supererogatory, if one of his parents knows he is in it and calls him, he should not respond; if they do not know, he should respond. [Maraqi al-Falah: 371] 'Even if belonging to someone else' — meaning even if the stolen property belongs to someone other than the praying person. [Maraqi al-Falah: 372] 'Fear of falling' etc. — [masdar tafa'ala meaning falling] — meaning if the praying person fears that a blind person will fall into a well and the like, it is permissible for him to cut the prayer; this is if he does not think it likely that he will fall; if he thinks it likely that he will fall, it becomes obligatory to cut the prayer, even if it is obligatory. 'And if the midwife fears' etc. — meaning it is permissible to cut the prayer if she fears, and obligation when there is a dominant presumption of the child's death, like the obligation when falling is dominant. That is: if the midwife (who is called wageh) receives the child at the time of its birth from its mother's womb, if it is dominant in her presumption that the child will die, or a limb will be lost, or the mother will die by leaving it, it becomes obligatory upon her to delay the prayer from its time, and to cut it if she is in it. If it is not dominant in her presumption, there is no harm in her delaying the prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 373] 'Otherwise there is no harm' — meaning if the midwife does not fear the child's death, but it is dominant in her presumption that it will die, there is no harm if she delays the prayer from its time and leaves it entirely, then makes it up afterward. 'And he is not killed' etc. — meaning he is not killed merely for leaving prayer and fasting while acknowledging their obligation, unless he denies the obligation of prayer or fasting, because of his denial of what is known of the religion by consensus, or shows contempt for either, such as openly breaking the fast in Ramadan without excuse out of carelessness, or speaks something that indicates that; then his ruling is like that of an apostate: his doubts are cleared, he is imprisoned, then killed if he persists. [Maraqi al-Falah: 373]
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqui al-Falah and others, outlines the rulings on cutting the prayer (qat' al-salah) and the punishment for abandoning it. The main rulings: 1) Cutting the prayer is obligatory (wajib) when a distressed person calls for help; but if only parents call without distress, it is not obligatory. 2) Cutting is permissible (ja'iz) when there is a theft of something worth a dirham, fear of a wolf for sheep, fear of a blind person falling, or when a midwife fears the child's death. In such cases, if the fear reaches a level of dominant presumption (ghalabat al-zann), it becomes obligatory to cut or delay the prayer. 3) A traveler fearing thieves may delay the time-bound prayer. 4) As for the one who deliberately leaves prayer or fasting out of laziness, he is severely beaten and imprisoned until he performs it; he is not killed unless he denies the obligation (juhud) or shows contempt (istikhfaf). The commentary clarifies conditions: e.g., for the midwife, the ruling depends on the level of fear. The Hanafi school emphasizes that necessity (darura) permits cutting prayer; otherwise, it is not allowed. The punishment for leaving prayer deliberately is severe but not death unless the obligation is denied, which is akin to apostasy.

Key Terms
استغاثة (istighatha): A cry for help; seeking assistance from a praying person in a dangerous situation.
ملهوف (malhuf): A distressed person in real danger (e.g., seized by a tyrant, drowning, attacked by an animal).
قطع الصلاة (qat' al-salah): Abandoning or terminating the prayer before completion; either obligatory or permissible depending on the situation.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Dominant presumption; a level of certainty that upgrades a permissible act to obligatory in these rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following makes cutting the prayer wajib?
A) A parent calls you for dinner
B) A distressed person cries for help
C) A thief steals something worth half a dirham
D) You fear it might rain on your laundry

Key Takeaway
Cutting prayer is wajib for emergencies, ja'iz for lesser harms, and becomes wajib when harm is certain; parental calls do not justify cutting.

Punishment for Deliberately Abandoning Prayer and Fasting
Ruling on punishment for deliberate abandonment of prayer and fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the punishment for deliberately abandoning prayer or fasting, distinguishing between mere laziness (beating and imprisonment) and denial or contempt (apostasy and execution).

Core Idea
Leaving prayer out of laziness is punished by beating and imprisonment, but denial of its obligation leads to apostasy and death.

This passage from the same source addresses the serious matter of one who deliberately abandons prayer or the fast of Ramadan. The Hanafi school prescribes severe physical punishment and imprisonment for the negligent, but reserves the ultimate penalty for those who reject the obligation outright or show contempt, treating them as apostates. This distinction underscores the importance of intention and belief in Islamic penal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for leaving prayer/fasting out of laziness
The text states: the one who deliberately leaves prayer out of laziness is beaten severely until blood flows and imprisoned until he prays. Similarly for fasting.
Beating is meant to be corrective, not arbitrary; it must be severe but not killing.
2
Note the exception: no death penalty for mere laziness
The text specifies that such a person is not killed merely for leaving prayer/fasting, because they acknowledge the obligation. The punishment is limited to beating and imprisonment.
Death is only for denial (juhud) or contempt (istikhfaf).
3
Understand juhud (denial) as apostasy
If a person denies that prayer or fasting is obligatory, they commit juhud. Since these are known by necessity from the religion, denial constitutes riddah (apostasy). The procedure: clear doubts, imprison, then kill if persists.
This is based on consensus (ijma).
4
Recognize istikhfaf (contempt) as equivalent to denial
Showing contempt, such as openly breaking the fast in Ramadan without excuse or speaking in a way that indicates disdain, is treated as evidence of denial. The same penalty applies.
Contempt is seen as a manifestation of juhud.
5
Contrast with the earlier cutting rulings
The previous rulings dealt with cutting prayer for valid reasons; here the focus is on abandoning prayer entirely without excuse. The gravity of the latter is addressed with severe correction.

يجب قطع الصلاة باستغاثة ملهوف بالمصلي لا بنداء أحد أبويه، ويجوز قطعها بسرقة ولو كانت فرضاً ما يساوي درهما ولو لغيره، وخوف ذئب على غنم أو خوف تردّي أعمى في بئر ونحوه، وإذا خافت القابلة موت الولد وإلا فلا بأس بتأخيرها الصلاة، وتقبل على الولد، وكذا المسافر إذا خاف من اللصوص أو قطاع الطريق، جاز له تأخير الوقتية، وتارك الصلاة عمدا كسلا يضرب ضربا شديدا حتى يسيل منه الدم، ويحبس حتى يصليها، وكذا تارك صوم رمضان ولا يقتل إلا إذا جحد أو استخف بأحدهما. باستغاثة ملهوف إلخ كما لو تعلق به ظالم، أو وقع في ماء، أو صال عليه حيوان فاستغاث بالمصلي. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۱] لا بنداء إلخ أي لا يجب قطع الصلاة بنداء أحد أبويه من غير استغاثة؛ لأن قطع الصلاة لا يجوز إلا لضرورة، وقال الطحاوي هذا في الفرض وإن كان في نافلة إن علم أحد أبويه أنه في وناداه لا يجيبه وإن لم يعلم يجيبه. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۱] ولو لغيره: أي ولو كان المسروق لغير المصلي. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۲] خوف تردي الخ: [مصدر تفعل بمعنى سقوط] أي إذا خاف المصلي أن أعمى من العميان يتردى في بئر ونحوها جاز له قطع الصلاة، وهذا إذا لم يغلب على ظنه سقوطه، وإذا غلب على ظنه سقوطه وجب قطع الصلاة ولو كانت فرضاً. وإذا خافت إلخ [أي يجوز قطعها الصلاة إذا خافت والوجوب عند غلبة الظن بموت الولد كالوجوب عند غلبة السقوط وهو كما إذا خافت القابلة - وهي المرأة التي يقال لها وايه - تتلقى الولد حال خروجه من بطن أمه إن غلب على ظنها موت الولد، أو تلف عضو منه، أو أمه بتركها وجب عليها تأخير الصلاة عن وقتها، وقطعها لو كانت فيها، وإن لم يغلب على ظنها فلا بأس بتأخيرها الصلاة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٣] وإلا فلا بأس أي وإن لم تخف القابلة موت الولد، بل غلب على ظنها موته فلا بأس إن أخرت الصلاة عن وقتها وتركتها رأساً، وقضاها بعده ولا يقتل إلخ أي ولا يقتل بمجرد ترك الصلاة والصوم مع الإقرار بفرضيتهما إلا إذا جحد افتراض الصلاة أو الصوم؛ لإنكاره ما كان معلوماً من الدين إجماعاً، أو استخف بأحدهما كما لو أظهر الإفطار في نهار رمضان بلا عذر تهاوناً، أو نطق بما يدل عليه، فيكون حكمه حكم المرتد، فتكشف شبهته ويحبس، ثم يقتل إن أصر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٧٣]
It is obligatory to cut the prayer due to a distressed person's cry for help directed at the praying person, but not due to a call from one of his parents (without distress). It is permissible to cut it for theft, even if the prayer is obligatory, of something worth one dirham, even if belonging to someone else; fear of a wolf for sheep, or fear that a blind person may fall into a well and the like; and if the midwife fears the death of the child, otherwise there is no harm in her delaying the prayer and attending to the child; likewise a traveler, if he fears thieves or highway robbers, it is permissible for him to delay the time-bound prayer. The one who deliberately leaves prayer out of laziness is severely beaten until blood flows, and imprisoned until he performs it; likewise the one who leaves the fast of Ramadan, but he is not killed unless he denies (the obligation) or shows contempt for either. Commentary: 'Due to a distressed person's cry for help' etc. — like if an oppressor seizes him, or he falls into water, or an animal attacks him and he seeks the help of the praying person. [Maraqi al-Falah: 371] 'Not due to a call' etc. — meaning it is not obligatory to cut the prayer due to a call from one of his parents without a cry for help; because cutting prayer is only allowed for necessity. Al-Tahawi said: this is in obligatory prayer; if it is supererogatory, if one of his parents knows he is in it and calls him, he should not respond; if they do not know, he should respond. [Maraqi al-Falah: 371] 'Even if belonging to someone else' — meaning even if the stolen property belongs to someone other than the praying person. [Maraqi al-Falah: 372] 'Fear of falling' etc. — [masdar tafa'ala meaning falling] — meaning if the praying person fears that a blind person will fall into a well and the like, it is permissible for him to cut the prayer; this is if he does not think it likely that he will fall; if he thinks it likely that he will fall, it becomes obligatory to cut the prayer, even if it is obligatory. 'And if the midwife fears' etc. — meaning it is permissible to cut the prayer if she fears, and obligation when there is a dominant presumption of the child's death, like the obligation when falling is dominant. That is: if the midwife (who is called wageh) receives the child at the time of its birth from its mother's womb, if it is dominant in her presumption that the child will die, or a limb will be lost, or the mother will die by leaving it, it becomes obligatory upon her to delay the prayer from its time, and to cut it if she is in it. If it is not dominant in her presumption, there is no harm in her delaying the prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 373] 'Otherwise there is no harm' — meaning if the midwife does not fear the child's death, but it is dominant in her presumption that it will die, there is no harm if she delays the prayer from its time and leaves it entirely, then makes it up afterward. 'And he is not killed' etc. — meaning he is not killed merely for leaving prayer and fasting while acknowledging their obligation, unless he denies the obligation of prayer or fasting, because of his denial of what is known of the religion by consensus, or shows contempt for either, such as openly breaking the fast in Ramadan without excuse out of carelessness, or speaks something that indicates that; then his ruling is like that of an apostate: his doubts are cleared, he is imprisoned, then killed if he persists. [Maraqi al-Falah: 373]
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqui al-Falah and others, outlines the rulings on cutting the prayer (qat' al-salah) and the punishment for abandoning it. The main rulings: 1) Cutting the prayer is obligatory (wajib) when a distressed person calls for help; but if only parents call without distress, it is not obligatory. 2) Cutting is permissible (ja'iz) when there is a theft of something worth a dirham, fear of a wolf for sheep, fear of a blind person falling, or when a midwife fears the child's death. In such cases, if the fear reaches a level of dominant presumption (ghalabat al-zann), it becomes obligatory to cut or delay the prayer. 3) A traveler fearing thieves may delay the time-bound prayer. 4) As for the one who deliberately leaves prayer or fasting out of laziness, he is severely beaten and imprisoned until he performs it; he is not killed unless he denies the obligation (juhud) or shows contempt (istikhfaf). The commentary clarifies conditions: e.g., for the midwife, the ruling depends on the level of fear. The Hanafi school emphasizes that necessity (darura) permits cutting prayer; otherwise, it is not allowed. The punishment for leaving prayer deliberately is severe but not death unless the obligation is denied, which is akin to apostasy.

Key Terms
جحد (juhud): Denial of the obligation (e.g., denying that prayer is fard), which can lead to apostasy and execution if persisted in.
استخف (istikhfaf): Showing contempt or disdain, e.g., openly breaking the fast in Ramadan without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is a person executed for leaving prayer?
A) When they miss two consecutive prayers
B) When they deny the obligation of prayer or show contempt
C) When they pray but miss the congregation
D) When they leave prayer while traveling

Key Takeaway
The lazy abandoner of prayer is beaten and imprisoned, but execution is only for those who deny the obligation or show contempt.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Rulings of Witr Prayer in the Hanafi School
Rules of Witr prayer: status, structure, recitation, qunut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Witr prayer according to the Hanafi school, including its wajib status, structure (three rak'ahs, one taslim), recitation rules, and the place and wording of qunut.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib: three rak'ahs, one taslim, qunut before ruku' every night.

Witr prayer holds a unique position in Hanafi fiqh: it is wajib, a category between fard and sunnah. This lesson unpacks its rulings from the classical text Nur al-Idah with Maraqi al-Falah commentary. You will learn the precise structure of Witr, the required recitations, and the sunnah of qunut—its timing, wording, and meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hukm of Witr
Determine whether Witr is fard, wajib, or sunnah in the Hanafi school. The passage states 'al-witr wajib'.
Wajib is a distinct level: omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
List the Structural Requirements
Note that Witr consists of three rak'ahs with one taslim (final salam). There is a sitting after two rak'ahs for tashahhud, but no opening supplication when standing for the third.
This differs from the practice of some other schools that pray Witr as one or five rak'ahs.
3
Examine the Recitation Rules
In each rak'ah, recite al-Fatihah and a surah. The passage considers this the most correct view (al-asahh).
Some early Hanafi views allowed surah only in some rak'ahs, but the relied-upon position is recitation in all three.
4
Locate the Qunut Placement and Wording
After reciting the surah in the third rak'ah, raise hands, say takbir, and recite qunut before ruku'. The qunut text is provided with detailed commentary on each phrase.
Hanafi qunut is recited all year, unlike Shafi'i who restrict it to the second half of Ramadan.
5
Understand the Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Hanafi view of Witr as wajib contrasts with Shafi'i and Maliki who consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. This difference affects whether one must make up a missed Witr prayer.
The practical consequence (thamarah): Hanafi requires qada' for missed Witr; Shafi'i does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر
أحكام الوتر
الوتر واجب وهو ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة، ويقرأ في كل ركعة منه الفاتحة وسورة، على الأصح ويجلس على رأس الأوليين منه، ويقتصر على التشهد ولا يستفتح عند قيامه للثالثة، لا يقرأ دعاء الاستفتاح
وإذا فرغ من قراءة السورة فيها رفع يديه حذاء أذنيه، ثم كبر، وقنت قائما قبل الركوع في جميع السنة، ولا يقنت في غير الوتر والقنوت: معناه الدعاء، وهو أن يقول: "اللهم إنا نستعينك ونستهديك، ونستغفرك ونتوب إليك، ونؤمن بك و نتوكل عليك، ونثني عليك الخير كله نشكرك ولا نكفرك، ونخلع ونترك من يفجرك،
اللهم إلخ أي يا الله ! "إنا نستعينك" أي نطلب منك الإعانة على طاعتك، "ونستهديك" أي نطلب منك الهداية لما يرضيك، ونستغفرك نطلب منك ستر عيوبنا، فلا تفضحنا بها، ونتوب إليك" التوبة: الرجوع عن الذنب، وشرعاً: الندم على ما مضى من الذنب، والإقلاع عنه في الحال، والعزم على ترك العود في المستقبل؛ تعظيماً لأمر الله تعالى، فإن تعلق به حق الآدمي فلابد من مسامحته وإرضائه، ونؤمن" أي نصدق معتقدين بقلوبنا، ناطقين بلساننا فقلنا آمنا، "بك" وبما جاء من عندك، وبملائكتك وكتبك ورُسُلك، وباليوم الآخر، وبالقدر خيره وشره، "ونتوكل" أي نعتمد "عليك" بتفويض أمورنا إليك لعجزنا، ونثني عليك الخير كله" أي نمدحك بكل خير مقرّين بجميع آلائك إفضالاً منك، "نشكرك" بصرف جميع ما أنعمت به من الجوارح إلى ما خلقته لأجله ولا نكفرك أي لا نجحد نعمة لك علينا ولا نضيفها إلى غيرك.
" ونخلع" بثبوت حرف العطف أي نلقي ونطرح ونزيل رقبة الكفر من أعناقنا ورقبة كل ما لا يرضيك، ونترك" أي نفارق "من" يفجرك" بجحده نعمتك، وعبادته غيرك، اللهم إياك نعبد عود للثناء، وتخصيص لذاته بالعبادة، ولك" "نصلي" أفردت الصلاة بالذكر ؛ لشرفها بتضمنها جميع العبادات "ونسجد" تخصيص بعد تخصيص؛ إذ هو أقرب حالات العبد من الرب المعبود، وإليك نسعى" وهو إشارة إلى قوله في الحديث حكاية عنه تعالى: "من أتاني سعياً أتيته هرولة"، والمعنى: نجهد في العمل لتحصيل ما يقربنا إليك، "ونحفد" نشرع في تحصيل عبادتك بنشاط، نرجو" أي نؤمل رحمتك أي دوامها، ونخشى عذابك" مع اجتنابنا ما نهيتنا عنه، فلا نأمن مكرك، فنحن بين الرجاء والخوف، "إن عذابك الجد" أي الحق بالكفار" ملحق" أي لا حق بهم. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۸]
Chapter of Witr. Rulings of Witr. Witr is wajib, and it is three rak'ahs with one taslim. And in each rak'ah he recites al-Fatihah and a surah, according to the most correct view. And he sits after the first two rak'ahs, and restricts to the tashahhud, and does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third. And when he finishes reciting the surah in it, he raises his hands to his ears, then says takbir, and makes qunut standing before ruku' in all the year, and he does not make qunut in other than witr. And qunut: its meaning is supplication. And it is that he says: "O Allah, we seek Your help and we seek Your guidance, and we seek Your forgiveness and we repent to You, and we believe in You and we rely on You, and we praise You with all goodness, we thank You and we are not ungrateful to You, and we renounce and leave whoever disobeys You." ... Commentary: "O Allah" i.e., O Allah! "We seek Your help" i.e., we ask for Your assistance in obeying You. "And we seek Your guidance" i.e., we ask You for guidance to what pleases You. "And we seek Your forgiveness" we ask You to conceal our faults. "And we repent to You" repentance: return from sin; legally: regret for past sin, abandoning it immediately, and resolving not to return in the future out of reverence for Allah's command; if it involves a right of a human, there must be reconciliation and satisfaction. "And we believe" i.e., we affirm with conviction in our hearts, speaking with our tongues, so we say we believe, "in You" and in what has come from You, and in Your angels, Your books, Your messengers, the Last Day, and in destiny, its good and evil. "And we rely" i.e., we depend "on You" by entrusting our affairs to You due to our incapacity. "And we praise You with all goodness" i.e., we commend You with every good, acknowledging all Your favors as a bounty from You. "We thank You" by using all the limbs You have bestowed for the purpose for which You created them, and we are not ungrateful to You i.e., we do not deny any favor of Yours upon us nor attribute it to other than You. "And we renounce" with the conjunction, i.e., we throw off and remove the yoke of disbelief from our necks and the yoke of everything that displeases You, "and we leave" i.e., we separate from "whoever disobeys You" by denying Your blessings and worshipping other than You. O Allah, You alone we worship—return to praise and specification of His essence for worship—and to You we pray—prayer is singled out for mention due to its honor in encompassing all acts of worship—and to You we prostrate—specification after specification, for it is the closest state of the servant to the worshipped Lord—and to You we strive—this refers to the saying in the hadith narrated from Him: 'Whoever comes to Me walking, I come to him running.' The meaning: we exert effort in action to attain what draws us near to You—and we earnestly seek—we set out to attain Your worship with energy—we hope—i.e., we hope for Your mercy, meaning its continuity—and we fear Your chastisement—while avoiding what You have forbidden us, so we do not feel secure from Your plan. Thus we are between hope and fear. Indeed Your chastisement, the severe—i.e., deserved by the disbelievers—will overtake—i.e., will reach them. [Maraqi al-Falah: 378]
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah, establishes the rulings of Witr prayer in the Hanafi school. Witr is wajib (obligatory, between fard and sunnah) consisting of three rak'ahs with one taslim. In each rak'ah, one recites al-Fatihah and a surah. After the first two rak'ahs, one sits for tashahhud but does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third. In the final rak'ah, after reciting the surah, one raises the hands, says takbir, and performs qunut (supplication) before ruku' in all seasons of the year (contrary to Shafi'i who limit it to the second half of Ramadan). The passage then provides the full text of the qunut supplication used in the Hanafi school, along with a detailed explanation of each phrase, covering the meaning of tawbah (repentance), iman (faith), tawakkul (reliance), shukr (gratitude), and the renunciation of disbelief. The supplication expresses hope in Allah's mercy and fear of His punishment. The commentary references a hadith qudsi about drawing near to Allah.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): A prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs (three in Hanafi school), considered wajib.
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited after takbir in the last rak'ah of Witr before ruku', or in other prayers during calamities (qunut al-nazila).
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in prayer (at-tahiyyat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) After the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school; its structure is three rak'ahs with one taslim, and qunut is a sunnah recited before ruku' in the last rak'ah every night.

Salah — Prayer

Basic Rulings of Witr Prayer
Declares Witr wajib and details its three-rak'ah format with Qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Witr prayer, describe its format (3 rak'ahs, one taslim), and explain the rules of Qunut.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school—an odd prayer with specific Qunut rules distinct from other prayers.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the essential rulings of Witr prayer. It clarifies that Witr is wajib (not merely sunnah), outlines its three-rak'ah structure with one taslim, and specifies the recitation and Qunut procedures. Understanding these details is crucial because the Hanafi position on Witr's obligation differs from other schools and affects daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of Witr
The text begins with 'al-witr wajib'. Recognize that this is the Hanafi position: Witr is wajib (obligatory) based on ahad hadith, not fard.
In Hanafi usul, wajib is a level below fard, requiring compensation if missed but not invalidating faith for denial.
2
Determine the rak'ah count and structure
The text says three rak'ahs with one taslim. This means Witr is performed as a single unit of three cycles ending with one salam.
Some schools perform Witr as separate units or with two taslims; Hanafis insist on three rak'ahs, one taslim.
3
Analyze the recitation rule
In each rak'ah, recite al-Fatihah and a surah. This is the 'most correct view' (ala al-asahh).
The phrase 'ala al-asahh' indicates there is a weaker opinion, but the relied-upon view is recitation in every rak'ah.
4
Recognize the post-first-two-rak'ahs sitting
After the first two rak'ahs, sit and recite only the tashahhud (al-tahiyyat), without sending salawat or performing any additional acts. Upon standing for the third, do not recite the opening supplication (istiftah).
This is a distinct rule: no opening du'a in the third rak'ah, unlike the first.
5
Apply the Qunut rules
After finishing the surah recitation in the third rak'ah, raise the hands to ear level, say takbir, and recite Qunut while standing before going into ruku'. This is done throughout the entire year (all year), and Qunut is only performed in Witr, not in any other prayer.
The Hanafi school maintains Qunut al-Witr before ruku' year-round, contrary to some schools that limit it to Ramadan or Fajr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر
أحكام الوتر
الوتر واجب وهو ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة، ويقرأ في كل ركعة منه الفاتحة وسورة، على الأصح ويجلس على رأس الأوليين منه، ويقتصر على التشهد ولا يستفتح عند قيامه للثالثة، لا يقرأ دعاء الاستفتاح وإذا فرغ من قراءة السورة فيها رفع يديه حذاء أذنيه، ثم كبر، وقنت قائما قبل الركوع في جميع السنة، ولا يقنت في غير الوتر
Chapter of Witr. Rulings of Witr. Witr is obligatory, and it is three rak'ahs with one taslim. He recites in every rak'ah the Fatiha and a surah, according to the most correct view. He sits after the first two, and confines himself to the tashahhud. He does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third, i.e., he does not recite the istiftah du'a. When he finishes reciting the surah in it, he raises his hands to the level of his ears, then says takbir, and performs Qunut standing before the bowing for the entire year. And he does not perform Qunut in other than Witr.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement passage from Nur al-Idah, establishing the basic legal framework of Witr prayer according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by declaring that Witr is wajib (obligatory but of a lower degree than fard). It consists of three rak'ahs with a single taslim (saying salam once at the end). In each rak'ah, the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah is required, followed by another surah. The worshipper sits after the first two rak'ahs for tashahhud only, without sending salawat or other supplications, and upon standing for the third rak'ah, he does not recite the opening supplication (du'a al-istiftah). After completing the surah recitation in the third rak'ah, he raises his hands to the ears, says takbir (Allahu Akbar), and then recites the Qunut while standing, before going into ruku'. The author emphasizes that Qunut is performed throughout the entire year in Witr, and only in Witr—not in any other prayer. This clarifies that Qunut al-Witr is a distinctive act of the Witr prayer, and it is performed before ruku' [al-mu'tamad]. Note that the Hanafi school considers Witr wajib, not sunnah mu'akkadah as some other schools hold, and the Qunut is an integral part of it.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): A prayer consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs (here three) performed after the night prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited standing before ruku' in the third rak'ah of Witr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling (hukm) of Witr prayer?
A) Fard ayn
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, performed as three rak'ahs with one taslim, and includes Qunut before ruku' in the third rak'ah throughout the year.

The Qunut Supplication: Text and Commentary
Presents the full text of Qunut and its line-by-line commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of each phrase in the Hanafi Qunut supplication and state its legal status as wajib.

Core Idea
Qunut in Witr is wajib, and its prescribed text is a comprehensive du'a of praise, repentance, and hope.

The Qunut supplication recited in Witr is a profound expression of devotion. This lesson presents the exact text as prescribed in the Hanafi school, followed by a detailed line-by-line commentary from Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the meanings of each phrase and the legal definitions of key terms like tawbah. Understanding these meanings deepens the spiritual connection of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Qunut text
Read the entire supplication in Arabic and its literal translation to get an overall sense of the du'a.
The text is divided into two parts: the first part includes praise and repentance, the second part includes exclusive worship and hope/fear.
2
Analyze each phrase with the commentary
For each phrase, read the accompanying commentary from Maraqi al-Falah that explains the linguistic and legal meaning.
Pay special attention to the definitions of 'tawbah' (repentance) and the explanation of 'nakhsha adhabak' (fear of punishment).
3
Identify the key definitions
From the commentary, extract the legal definition of tawbah as given, noting its four components.
The definition includes regret, immediate abstention, resolve not to return, and restitution of human rights if applicable.
4
Determine the legal status
Review the hanafi_position_box to confirm that reciting Qunut in Witr is wajib, not sunnah or fard.
The wording of the supplication is sunnah, but the act of reciting Qunut is wajib.
5
Apply: Follower's role
Note the final ruling that the follower (mu'tam) recites the Qunut along with the imam.
This ensures the follower also fulfills the wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقنوت: معناه الدعاء، وهو أن يقول: "اللهم إنا نستعينك ونستهديك، ونستغفرك ونتوب إليك، ونؤمن بك و نتوكل عليك، ونثني عليك الخير كله نشكرك ولا نكفرك، ونخلع ونترك من يفجرك،
اللهم إلخ أي يا الله ! "إنا نستعينك" أي نطلب منك الإعانة على طاعتك، "ونستهديك" أي نطلب منك الهداية لما يرضيك، ونستغفرك نطلب منك ستر عيوبنا، فلا تفضحنا بها، ونتوب إليك" التوبة: الرجوع عن الذنب، وشرعاً: الندم على ما مضى من الذنب، والإقلاع عنه في الحال، والعزم على ترك العود في المستقبل؛ تعظيماً لأمر الله تعالى، فإن تعلق به حق الآدمي فلابد من مسامحته وإرضائه، ونؤمن" أي نصدق معتقدين بقلوبنا، ناطقين بلساننا فقلنا آمنا، "بك" وبما جاء من عندك، وبملائكتك وكتبك ورُسُلك، وباليوم الآخر، وبالقدر خيره وشره، "ونتوكل" أي نعتمد "عليك" بتفويض أمورنا إليك لعجزنا، ونثني عليك الخير كله" أي نمدحك بكل خير مقرّين بجميع آلائك إفضالاً منك، "نشكرك" بصرف جميع ما أنعمت به من الجوارح إلى ما خلقته لأجله ولا نكفرك أي لا نجحد نعمة لك علينا ولا نضيفها إلى غيرك.
" ونخلع" بثبوت حرف العطف أي نلقي ونطرح ونزيل رقبة الكفر من أعناقنا ورقبة كل ما لا يرضيك، ونترك" أي نفارق "من" يفجرك" بجحده نعمتك، وعبادته غيرك، اللهم إياك نعبد عود للثناء، وتخصيص لذاته بالعبادة، ولك" "نصلي" أفردت الصلاة بالذكر ؛ لشرفها بتضمنها جميع العبادات "ونسجد" تخصيص بعد تخصيص؛ إذ هو أقرب حالات العبد من الرب المعبود، وإليك نسعى" وهو إشارة إلى قوله في الحديث حكاية عنه تعالى: "من أتاني سعياً أتيته هرولة"، والمعنى: نجهد في العمل لتحصيل ما يقربنا إليك، "ونحفد" نشرع في تحصيل عبادتك بنشاط، نرجو" أي نؤمل رحمتك أي دوامها، ونخشى عذابك" مع اجتنابنا ما نهيتنا عنه، فلا نأمن مكرك، فنحن بين الرجاء والخوف، "إن عذابك الجد" أي الحق بالكفار" ملحق" أي لا حق بهم. [مراقي الفلاح: ۳۷۸]
اللهم إياك نعبد ولك نصلي ونسجد، وإليك نسعى ونحفد، نرجو رحمتك، ونخشى عذابك، إن عذابك الجد بالكفار ملحق، وصلى الله على النبي وآله وسلم، والمؤتم يقرأ القنوت كالإمام
And Qunut: its meaning is supplication, and it is that one says: 'O Allah, we seek Your help and we seek Your guidance, and we seek Your forgiveness and we repent to You, and we believe in You and we rely on You, and we praise You with all goodness; we thank You and we do not disbelieve in You, and we forsake and abandon whoever disobeys You. O Allah, You alone we worship, and to You we pray and prostrate, and to You we strive and hasten; we hope for Your mercy and we fear Your punishment; indeed Your severe punishment is joined to the disbelievers.' And may Allah send blessings upon the Prophet and his family and peace. [Explanation continues with line-by-line commentary.] O Allah, You alone we worship, and to You we pray and prostrate, and to You we strive and hasten; we hope for Your mercy and we fear Your punishment; indeed Your severe punishment is joined to the disbelievers. And may Allah send blessings upon the Prophet and his family and peace. And the follower recites the Qunut like the imam.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage serves as a definition_ruling, presenting the full text of the Qunut supplication for Witr with an extensive line-by-line commentary. The author first states that Qunut linguistically means supplication, and then provides the exact wording. The commentary, derived from Maraqi al-Falah, explains each phrase: 'We seek Your help' means we ask for assistance in obeying You; 'we seek Your guidance' means we ask to be guided to what pleases You; 'we seek Your forgiveness' means we ask You to conceal our faults; 'we repent to You' is defined as regret for past sins, immediate abstention, and resolve not to return, with the condition of satisfying any related human rights. 'We believe in You' implies sincere conviction, verbal declaration, and acceptance of all that comes from You including angels, scriptures, messengers, the Last Day, and destiny. 'We rely on You' means we depend on You by delegating our matters due to our incapacity. 'We praise You with all goodness' means we extol You for every good, acknowledging all Your favors. 'We thank You' means we use the limbs You bestowed for their intended purpose, and 'we do not disbelieve in You' means we do not deny Your grace nor attribute it to others. 'We forsake' means we cast off the neck of disbelief from ourselves and anything that displeases You, and 'we abandon whoever disobeys You' by denying Your blessings and worshipping other than You. The second part begins with 'O Allah, You alone we worship' (reaffirming exclusive devotion), 'to You we pray' (specifically mentioning prayer because it encompasses all acts of worship), 'to You we prostrate' (the closest state of the servant to the Lord), 'to You we strive and hasten' (referring to the hadith: 'Whoever comes to Me walking, I come to him running'), meaning we exert ourselves to draw near to You. 'We hope for Your mercy' (for its continuity) and 'we fear Your punishment' (even while avoiding what is prohibited), thus we are between hope and fear. The last line: 'Indeed Your severe punishment is joined to the disbelievers.' This is followed by the salawat. The text adds: 'And the follower recites the Qunut like the imam'—this is a separate ruling that the follower should recite the Qunut along with the imam, matching the imam's recitation.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in Witr before ruku', as given in this passage.
التوبة (al-tawbah): Repentance: linguistic return from sin; legal: regret for past sin, immediate abstention, resolve not to return, with restitution of human rights if applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Saying 'Astaghfirullah'
B) Regret for past sin, immediate abstention, resolve not to return, and satisfying any related human rights
C) Crying in prayer
D) Making du'a for forgiveness

Key Takeaway
Qunut in Witr is a wajib supplication with a rich meaning; Hanafis use a specific text that includes praise, repentance, hope, and fear.
