Tahiyyat al-Masjid: The Greeting of the Mosque
Rules for greeting the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling of Tahiyyat al-Masjid, explain that obligatory prayer suffices for it, and contrast the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Tahiyyat al-Masjid is sunnah, not wajib, and is fulfilled by any prayer upon entry.

Entering a mosque is an act of worship, and the Prophet taught us to greet the mosque with prayer. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on Tahiyyat al-Masjid, the conditions under which it is fulfilled, and the difference with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text says 'sunna tahiyyat al-masjid bi rak'atayn' — it is sunnah to greet the mosque with two rak'ahs. Note the ruling level: sunnah, not wajib.
Sunnah mu'akkadah according to Hanafi.
2
Understand substitution by obligatory prayer
'wa adaa' al-fard yanubu anha' — if you perform the obligatory prayer upon entering, that suffices for the greeting.
Same for any prayer, even without the intention of greeting.
3
Consider the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is wajib. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Companions who did not always pray upon entering, indicating it is not obligatory.
The dispute is based on different interpretations of the hadith 'Do not sit until you pray two rak'ahs.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تحية المسجد، وصلاة الضحى، وإحياء الليالي سن تحية المسجد بركعتين قبل الجلوس، وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها، وكل صلاة أداها عند الدخول بلا نية التحية، وندب ركعتان بعد الوضوء قبل جفافه، وأربع فصاعدا في الضحى وندب صلاة الليل، وصلاة الاستخارة، وقد أفصحت السنة عن بيانها، قال جابر : "كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول : إذا هم أحدكم بالأمر فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة، ثم ليقل: اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك وأستقدرك بقدرتك، وأسألك من فضلك العظيم، فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر، وتعلم ولا أعلم، وأنت علام الغيوب، اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري"، أو قال: لعاجل أمري وآجله فاقدره لي ويسره لي ثم بارك لي فيه، وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري ، أو قال: عاجل أمري وآجله فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه واقدر لي الخير حيث كان ثم رضَني به حاجته" رواه الجماعة إلا مسلماً، وينبغي أن يجمع بين الروايتين فيقول: وعاقبة أمري وعاجله وآجله، قال: "ويسمي حاجته".
Section on greeting the mosque, Duha prayer, and keeping the nights alive. It is sunnah to greet the mosque with two rak'ahs before sitting, and performing the obligatory prayer suffices for it, and any prayer performed upon entering without the intention of greeting suffices. Two rak'ahs after ablution before it dries are recommended, and four or more in Duha are recommended, and night prayer is recommended, and the prayer of istikhara is recommended, and the sunnah has clearly explained it. Jabir said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to teach us istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah of the Qur'an, saying: When one of you intends to do something, let him pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, then say: O Allah, I seek Your choice by Your knowledge, and I seek Your power by Your power, and I ask You from Your great bounty, for You are able and I am not, and You know and I do not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair'—or he said: my immediate and future affair—then decree it for me, make it easy for me, then bless me in it. And if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair'—or he said: my immediate and future affair—then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me the good wherever it is, then make me content with it. He said: and he should mention his need.' Reported by all except Muslim. And one should combine the two narrations and say: 'and the outcome of my affair, immediate and future' and he should name his need.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage covers three recommended acts: Tahiyyat al-Masjid (greeting the mosque), Salat al-Duha (forenoon prayer), and Salat al-Istikhara (seeking guidance). The ruling for tahiyyat al-masjid is sunnah: one prays two rak'ahs before sitting when entering a mosque. However, if one prays an obligatory prayer immediately upon entering, that suffices for the greeting, as does any prayer performed at entry even without intending tahiyyah. This is based on the principle that the purpose of greeting is to prevent sitting without prayer. Two rak'ahs after ablution before the limbs dry are recommended. For Duha, the minimum is four rak'ahs (according to this text, though other Hanafi texts mention a minimum of two), and its time begins after sunrise and ends before zenith, with the best time after a quarter of the day has passed. Night prayer is recommended, with the minimum being two rak'ahs and the maximum eight. Most importantly, the text provides the full hadith on istikhara, as taught by the Prophet. The prayer consists of two rak'ahs of nafl, followed by a specific supplication. The hadith is reported by the 'Jama'ah' (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.) except Muslim; various narrations have minor wording differences, and the preferred practice is to combine them by saying 'in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair, immediate and future.' The person then names his specific need.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The greeting of the mosque; two rak'ahs prayed upon entering before sitting, as a sign of respect to the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What can substitute for Tahiyyat al-Masjid when entering a mosque?
A) Reciting the shahada
B) Performing the obligatory prayer immediately
C) Reciting Surah al-Ikhlas three times
D) Sitting and making du'a

Key Takeaway
Tahiyyat al-Masjid is a sunnah fulfilled by any prayer upon entry, not an independent obligation.

Salat al-Duha and Night Prayer
Rules for Duha and night prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended number of rak'ahs for Duha and night prayer, and the time for Duha.

Core Idea
Duha prayer is recommended with at least four rak'ahs; night prayer is also recommended and flexible.

Beyond the obligatory prayers, the Prophet encouraged certain voluntary prayers at specific times. This lesson focuses on Duha (forenoon) prayer and night prayers, clarifying their rulings according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for Duha
The text says 'wa arba'an fa sa'idan fi al-duha' — four or more in Duha are recommended. This indicates the minimum is four rak'ahs.
Some Hanafi texts mention two as minimum; this text takes the stronger view.
2
Identify the ruling for night prayer
'wa nudiba salat al-layl' — night prayer is recommended. No specific number is given here, but other sources say the minimum is two rak'ahs.
The text does not specify maximum.
3
Note the time for Duha
Duha starts after sunrise and ends before zawal (noon). The best time is after a quarter of the day has passed.
This is derived from other sources.

Source Text

فصل في تحية المسجد، وصلاة الضحى، وإحياء الليالي سن تحية المسجد بركعتين قبل الجلوس، وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها، وكل صلاة أداها عند الدخول بلا نية التحية، وندب ركعتان بعد الوضوء قبل جفافه، وأربع فصاعدا في الضحى وندب صلاة الليل، وصلاة الاستخارة، وقد أفصحت السنة عن بيانها، قال جابر : "كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول : إذا هم أحدكم بالأمر فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة، ثم ليقل: اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك وأستقدرك بقدرتك، وأسألك من فضلك العظيم، فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر، وتعلم ولا أعلم، وأنت علام الغيوب، اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري"، أو قال: لعاجل أمري وآجله فاقدره لي ويسره لي ثم بارك لي فيه، وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري ، أو قال: عاجل أمري وآجله فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه واقدر لي الخير حيث كان ثم رضَني به حاجته" رواه الجماعة إلا مسلماً، وينبغي أن يجمع بين الروايتين فيقول: وعاقبة أمري وعاجله وآجله، قال: "ويسمي حاجته".
Section on greeting the mosque, Duha prayer, and keeping the nights alive. It is sunnah to greet the mosque with two rak'ahs before sitting, and performing the obligatory prayer suffices for it, and any prayer performed upon entering without the intention of greeting suffices. Two rak'ahs after ablution before it dries are recommended, and four or more in Duha are recommended, and night prayer is recommended, and the prayer of istikhara is recommended, and the sunnah has clearly explained it. Jabir said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to teach us istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah of the Qur'an, saying: When one of you intends to do something, let him pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, then say: O Allah, I seek Your choice by Your knowledge, and I seek Your power by Your power, and I ask You from Your great bounty, for You are able and I am not, and You know and I do not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair'—or he said: my immediate and future affair—then decree it for me, make it easy for me, then bless me in it. And if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair'—or he said: my immediate and future affair—then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me the good wherever it is, then make me content with it. Salat al-Istikhara: Seeking Guidance
Procedure and du'a of Istikhara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the procedure of Istikhara prayer, quote the essential parts of the du'a, and explain the importance of naming the need.

Core Idea
Istikhara is a two-rak'ah nafl prayer followed by a specific du'a to seek Allah's guidance.

When faced with a decision, the Prophet taught us to pray Istikhara. This lesson covers the procedure, the du'a, and the proper way to combine different narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text says 'wa nudibat salat al-istikhara' — the prayer of Istikhara is recommended. It is a sunnah.
Unanimously recommended.
2
Learn the procedure
The hadith: 'When one of you intends to do something, let him pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, then say the du'a.'
The du'a is the core.
3
Analyze the du'a
The du'a asks Allah to decree the good if it is good, and to turn away evil if it is evil. The text instructs to combine two narrations: 'in my religion, my livelihood, and the outcome of my affair, immediate and future.'
Mentioning the specific need is important.
4
Note the hadith sources
Reported by all except Muslim. The authenticity is established.

Ruling and Substitution of Tahiyyat al-Masjid
Ruling statement with substitution rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tahiyyat al-masjid and identify which prayers substitute for it without specific intention.

Core Idea
Any prayer upon entering a mosque suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid, even without specific intention.

The Hanafi school teaches that greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) is a confirmed sunnah, not a wajib. This lesson explains its ruling and the important principle that any prayer – whether fard, sunnah, or nafl – performed upon entry fulfills this sunnah, even if you did not intend the tahiyyah specifically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the phrase 'سن تحية المسجد' – the verb 'سن' indicates the act is sunnah. Determine the level: sunnah muakkadah.
The Hanafi school considers it sunnah muakkadah (confirmed), not fard or wajib.
2
Understand the substitution rule
The text says 'وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها' – performing the fard prayer suffices for tahiyyah. Then 'وكل صلاة أداها عند الدخول بلا نية التحية' extends this to any prayer without intention.
Substitution is valid even if you did not intend tahiyyah.
3
Note the temporal condition
The substitution applies only if the prayer is performed 'at entry' (عند الدخول). The tahiyyah itself is to be done before sitting.
If you sit down first, the sunnah is no longer current; you should not pray it then.
4
Recognize the exception
The passage ends with an exception for Masjid al-Haram: its tahiyyah is tawaf. This is covered in detail in the next lesson.
For now, note that the rule has an exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سن تحية المسجد بركعتين قبل الجلوس، وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها، وكل صلاة أداها عند الدخول بلا نية التحية، تحية إلخ: أي تحية رب المسجد؛ لأن التحية إنما تكون لصاحب المكان لا للمكان كما قيل: حاجی بره کعبه و من طالب دیدار او خانہ ہمی جوید و من صاحب خانه (حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة) المسجد ويستثنى منه المسجد الحرام؛ فإن تحيته الطواف وصرح الملا علي بأن من دخل المسجد الحرام لا يشتغل بتحيته؛ لأن تحية هذا المسجد الشريف هو الطواف لمن عليه طواف أو أراده، بخلاف من لم يرده أو أراد أن يجلس، فلا يجلس حتى يصلي ركعتين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٩٤] وكل إلخ أي وكذا ينوب عنهما كل صلاة إلخ.
Tahiyyat al-Masjid is sunnah with two rak'ahs before sitting, and performing the obligatory prayer suffices for it, and every prayer one performs upon entry without intending tahiyyah (also suffices). Tahiyyah etc.: meaning tahiyyah of the Lord of the mosque, because tahiyyah is for the owner of the place, not the place as it is said: ... The Sacred Mosque is excluded; its tahiyyah is tawaf, and Mulla 'Ali stated that whoever enters the Sacred Mosque should not occupy himself with its tahiyyah, because the tahiyyah of this noble mosque is tawaf for one who has tawaf upon him or intends it, contrary to one who does not intend it or intends to sit, then he should not sit until he prays two rak'ahs. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 394] And 'every prayer' etc.: meaning every prayer also substitutes for them.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Nur al-Idah states the ruling on Tahiyyat al-Masjid (greeting the mosque). It is a sunnah (recommended) act to pray two rak'ahs upon entering a mosque before sitting. Importantly, if one enters and prays the obligatory (fard) prayer, that fulfills the tahiyyah. Similarly, any prayer performed at the time of entry without the specific intention of tahiyyah also suffices. The commentary explains that 'tahiyyah' actually means greeting the Lord of the mosque (Allah), not the building itself. An exception is made for the Sacred Mosque (Masjid al-Haram in Mecca), where the greeting is tawaf (circumambulation) for those who have tawaf to perform or intend it. If one does not intend tawaf or wishes to sit, they should not sit until they pray two rak'ahs (regular tahiyyah). The text also notes that any prayer substitutes for the two rak'ahs of tahiyyah, whether it is a fard, sunnah, or nafl prayer.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs performed upon entering a mosque to 'greet' the mosque (i.e., Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the text say about a person who enters a mosque and immediately prays the fard prayer without intending tahiyyat al-masjid?
A) The tahiyyah is not fulfilled; he must pray two rak'ahs after fard.
B) The fard prayer substitutes for the tahiyyah.
C) It is makruh to combine them.
D) He should repeat the prayer with intention of tahiyyah.

Key Takeaway
Tahiyyat al-masjid is a sunnah muakkadah that is fulfilled by any prayer performed upon entering the mosque, even without specific intention.

Tahiyyat al-Masjid al-Haram: The Exception
Exception for Masjid al-Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tawaf substitutes for tahiyyat al-masjid at the Sacred Mosque and apply the exception based on intention.

Core Idea
At Masjid al-Haram, the greeting is tawaf, not prayer, unless one does not intend tawaf.

The previous lesson established that any prayer upon entering a mosque suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. However, an important exception applies to the Sacred Mosque (Masjid al-Haram) in Mecca. This lesson examines that exception: why tawaf replaces prayer as the greeting, and how intention determines the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the exception
The text says 'ويستثنى منه المسجد الحرام' – the Sacred Mosque is excluded from the general rule. Identify what replaces the prayer.
The replacement is tawaf (circumambulation) for those who have tawaf upon them or intend it.
2
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that tahiyyah is for the Owner (Allah), not the building. At Masjid al-Haram, the act of tawaf is more specific to that sacred place and thus takes precedence.
This reasoning is supported by the saying quoted: 'Haji is for the Ka'bah...' indicating the special status.
3
Apply the exception based on intention
The text distinguishes two cases: (a) one who has tawaf upon him (due to entering ihram) or intends tawaf – he should occupy himself with tawaf as greeting; (b) one who does not intend tawaf or wishes to sit – he should pray two rak'ahs before sitting, following the general rule.
Intention is key: if you plan to perform tawaf, that substitutes; otherwise, pray.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سن تحية المسجد بركعتين قبل الجلوس، وأداء الفرض ينوب عنها، وكل صلاة أداها عند الدخول بلا نية التحية، تحية إلخ: أي تحية رب المسجد؛ لأن التحية إنما تكون لصاحب المكان لا للمكان كما قيل: حاجی بره کعبه و من طالب دیدار او خانہ ہمی جوید و من صاحب خانه (حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة) المسجد ويستثنى منه المسجد الحرام؛ فإن تحيته الطواف وصرح الملا علي بأن من دخل المسجد الحرام لا يشتغل بتحيته؛ لأن تحية هذا المسجد الشريف هو الطواف لمن عليه طواف أو أراده، بخلاف من لم يرده أو أراد أن يجلس، فلا يجلس حتى يصلي ركعتين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٩٤] وكل إلخ أي وكذا ينوب عنهما كل صلاة إلخ.
Tahiyyat al-Masjid is sunnah with two rak'ahs before sitting, and performing the obligatory prayer suffices for it, and every prayer one performs upon entry without intending tahiyyah (also suffices). Tahiyyah etc.: meaning tahiyyah of the Lord of the mosque, because tahiyyah is for the owner of the place, not the place as it is said: ... The Sacred Mosque is excluded; its tahiyyah is tawaf, and Mulla 'Ali stated that whoever enters the Sacred Mosque should not occupy himself with its tahiyyah, because the tahiyyah of this noble mosque is tawaf for one who has tawaf upon him or intends it, contrary to one who does not intend it or intends to sit, then he should not sit until he prays two rak'ahs. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 394] And 'every prayer' etc.: meaning every prayer also substitutes for them.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Nur al-Idah states the ruling on Tahiyyat al-Masjid (greeting the mosque). It is a sunnah (recommended) act to pray two rak'ahs upon entering a mosque before sitting. An exception is made for the Sacred Mosque (Masjid al-Haram in Mecca), where the greeting is tawaf (circumambulation) for those who have tawaf to perform or intend it. If one does not intend tawaf or wishes to sit, they should not sit until they pray two rak'ahs (regular tahiyyah). The text also notes that any prayer substitutes for the two rak'ahs of tahiyyah, whether it is a fard, sunnah, or nafl prayer.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد الحرام (tahiyyat al-masjid al-haram): The greeting of the Sacred Mosque; tawaf substitutes for prayer for those intending it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what should a person do upon entering Masjid al-Haram if he does not intend to perform tawaf?
A) Perform tawaf anyway.
B) Pray two rak'ahs before sitting.
C) Sit and recite Quran.
D) Leave immediately.

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Salat al-Duha: Time and Minimum Rak'ahs
Ruling on the time and number of rak'ahs for Duha prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Duha including its time, minimum number of rak'ahs, and preferred time.

Core Idea
Duha is a recommended nafl prayer of at least four rak'ahs, with the best time after a quarter of the day.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from Nur al-Idah on Salat al-Duha. The text specifies the minimum rak'ahs and the temporal boundaries for this forenoon prayer. Understanding the timing is crucial for proper practice, as the Hanafi school highlights a preferred window for optimal reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on Salat al-Duha, stating it is four rak'ahs or more.
The word 'فصاعدا' indicates the minimum is four.
2
Locate the temporal boundaries
The time begins from sunrise (irtifa' al-shams) until just before zawal (zenith).
Sunrise means after the sun has fully risen, about 15-20 minutes after actual sunrise.
3
Identify the preferred time
The optimal time is after a quarter of the day has passed, where day is from sunrise to sunset.
For example, if sunrise is at 6 AM and sunset at 6 PM, the preferred time starts at 9 AM.
4
Connect to Hanafi classification
This aligns with the Hanafi position that Duha is sunnah ghayr muakkadah (non-confirmed sunnah).
Other schools may classify it differently, but the time and minimum are specific to Hanafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأربع فصاعدا في الضحى الضحى وابتداؤه من ارتفاع الشمس إلى قبيل زوالها. ووقتها المختار إذا مضى ربع النهار. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٩٥]
And four or more in the Duha. Duha: its beginning is from the rising of the sun (i.e., after sunrise) to just before its decline (zawal). And its preferred time is when a quarter of the day has passed. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 395]
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on Salat al-Duha, the forenoon prayer. The matn states that it is four rak'ahs or more. The commentary from Maraqi al-Falah defines the time: from sunrise (after it has risen well, about 15-20 minutes after sunrise) to just before midday (zawal). The preferred time (al-mukhtar) is after a quarter of the day has passed. The day here is from sunrise to sunset, so a quarter of that period after sunrise. This aligns with the Hanafi position that Duha is mustahabb (recommended) and its optimum time is later in the morning.

Key Terms
الضحى (al-duha): The forenoon period after sunrise until before noon; also the recommended prayer performed during this time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 8
D) 12

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Duha in the Hanafi school is a sunnah ghayr muakkadah of at least four rak'ahs, performed from after sunrise to before zawal, with the preferred time after a quarter of the day.

The Rulings of Salat al-Layl (Night Prayer)
Ruling on minimum rak'ahs for night prayer with intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Layl, including its hukm level, the differing views on its minimum rak'ahs, and the operative position for practice.

Core Idea
Salat al-Layl is a confirmed sunnah, with a recommended minimum of eight rak'ahs but flexibility down to two.

Night prayer (Salat al-Layl, including Tahajjud) is a deeply virtuous act in Islam. The Hanafi school provides guidance on its structure, and this passage from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains the recommended number of rak'ahs while noting an internal scholarly difference. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate the flexibility and encouragement within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Hukm
Recognize that Salat al-Layl (night nafl prayer) is the subject. The text uses 'ينبغي' (it is appropriate), indicating a recommended (sunnah) level, not obligatory. Determine the precise hukm level.
In Hanafi terminology, sunnah muakkadah is a confirmed sunnah, less than wajib.
2
Extract the Recommended Minimum
From Maraqi al-Falah: the minimum that one should perform is eight rak'ahs. Note the virtue is said to be immense.
This is a later Hanafi source emphasizing the ideal.
3
Note the Alternative View
From Hashiyat al-Tahtawi quoting al-Hawi al-Qudsi: the minimum can be two rak'ahs and the maximum eight. This shows a range within the school.
Al-Hawi al-Qudsi is an earlier authority, so both views are internal to Hanafism.
4
Determine the Operative Ruling
The mufta bihi (fatwa position) is that Salat al-Layl is sunnah, and one may pray any even number from 2 to 8 rak'ahs. The preferred (afdal) practice is eight.
No explicit tarjih from the text; both views are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلاة الليل: أقل ما ينبغي أن يتنفل بالليل ثمان ركعات وفضلها لا يحصر مراقي الفلاح: ٣٩٦] والذي في 'الحاوي القدسي' أن أقله ركعتان وأكثره ثمان حاشية الطحطاوي: ٣٩٦]
Salat al-Layl: The least that one should perform nafl at night is eight rak'ahs, and its virtue cannot be enumerated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 396] And what is in al-Hawi al-Qudsi is that its minimum is two rak'ahs and its maximum is eight. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 396]
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage discusses Salat al-Layl (night prayer, including Tahajjud). The commentary from Maraqi al-Falah states that the minimum recommended is eight rak'ahs, emphasizing the immense virtue. However, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi quotes al-Hawi al-Qudsi that the minimum can be as low as two rak'ahs and the maximum eight. This reflects a range within the Hanafi school: the ideal minimum is eight, but one may pray less. The passage encourages night prayer but does not specify a set number as obligatory.

Key Terms
صلاة الليل (salat al-layl): Voluntary prayers performed during the night, typically after Isha until Fajr; includes Tahajjud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 2
B) 8
C) 4
D) 12

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Layl is a highly virtuous sunnah; the Hanafi school permits a minimum of two rak'ahs but recommends eight as optimal.

Salat al-Istikhara: Its Ruling and Prophetic Supplication
The prayer of seeking guidance (Istikhara) with its prophetic supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Salat al-Istikhara, recite its du'a, and explain its proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Istikhara is a sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs followed by a comprehensive du'a seeking guidance.

We now turn to the prayer of seeking guidance (Istikhara). The text presents the clear proof from the Sunnah, quoting the hadith of Jabir in which the Prophet taught the companions the full supplication. This lesson will guide you through the ruling, the evidence, and the correct wording of the du'a, including how to combine its variations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening line: 'وصلاة الاستخارة' indicates that it is a recommended prayer (sunnah). Note that it is not obligatory; the command 'فليركع ركعتين' is interpreted as istihbab (recommendation) due to the context of it being a voluntary act.
2
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of Jabir is cited. Classify it as ahad hadith (transmitted by a few). Identify the wajh al-dalalah: the direct command to pray two rak'ahs and recite the du'a proves the recommendation. Note that the text says 'رواه الجماعة إلا مسلما' indicating it is well-authenticated.
Hanafi usul: a command from the Prophet generally indicates wujub unless there is a qarinah (context) showing recommendation; here the fact that the Prophet taught it as a practice in all matters shows it is a sunnah.
3
Learn the du'a
Read the full Arabic du'a from the text. Note the variations in wording (e.g., 'عاقبة أمري' vs 'عاجله وآجله'). The text recommends combining both versions: 'وعاقبة أمري وعاجله وآجله'. Understand the meaning: asking Allah for guidance based on His knowledge and power.
There is a slight difference in the order of 'religion, livelihood, end of affair' vs 'immediate and future'. The student should memorize the combined version.
4
Apply the practice
After the prayer and du'a, the text implies that one should proceed with the matter if one's heart feels inclined; if not, one turns away. This is the thamarah (practical outcome). There is no requirement to wait for a dream or sign.
The commentary says: 'إذا فعل ذلك مضى على الأمر إن انشرح صدره... وإلا انصرف عنه' – if the chest expands, proceed; otherwise, desist.
5
Note the scope
The hadith says 'في الأمور كلها' – in all matters. This includes religious (e.g., whether to perform Hajj at a specific time) and worldly matters (e.g., marriage, business). Istikhara is recommended whenever there is a decision between two options.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلاة الاستخارة وقد أفصحت السنة عن بيانها، قال جابر : 'كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يعلمنا الاستخارة في الأمور كلها كما يعلمنا السورة من القرآن يقول : إذا هم أحدكم بالأمر فليركع ركعتين من غير الفريضة، ثم ليقل: اللهم إني أستخيرك بعلمك وأستقدرك بقدرتك، وأسألك من فضلك العظيم، فإنك تقدر ولا أقدر، وتعلم ولا أعلم، وأنت علام الغيوب، اللهم إن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر خير لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري'، أو قال: لعاجل أمري وآجله فاقدره لي ويسره لي ثم بارك لي فيه، وإن كنت تعلم أن هذا الأمر شر لي في ديني ومعاشي وعاقبة أمري ، أو قال: عاجل أمري وآجله فاصرفه عني واصرفني عنه واقدر لي الخير حيث كان ثم رضَني به' حاجته رواه الجماعة إلا مسلماً، وينبغي أن يجمع بين الروايتين فيقول: وعاقبة أمري وعاجله وآجله، قال: 'ويسمي حاجته'.
And Salat al-Istikhara: The Sunnah has clearly explained it. Jabir said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to teach us Istikhara in all matters as he taught us a surah of the Quran. He would say: When one of you intends to do something, let him pray two rak'ahs of non-obligatory prayer, then say: O Allah, I seek Your guidance by Your knowledge, and I seek Your power by Your power, and I ask You from Your great favor, for You have power and I have none, and You know and I know not, and You are the Knower of the unseen. O Allah, if You know that this matter is good for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the end of my affair' — or he said: 'for the immediate and future of my affair — then decree it for me, make it easy for me, and then bless me in it. And if You know that this matter is evil for me in my religion, my livelihood, and the end of my affair' — or said: 'the immediate and future of my affair — then turn it away from me and turn me away from it, and decree for me the good wherever it may be, then make me content with it.' He mentioned his need. Narrated by all except Muslim. And one should combine the two narrations and say: 'and the end of my affair and its immediate and future.' He said: 'and he mentions his need.'
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on Salat al-Istikhara, the prayer for seeking guidance when making a decision. It is a sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs, followed by a specific du'a (supplication) taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah is quoted, with the full text of the du'a. The commentary notes that there are slight variations in the wording of the du'a (e.g., 'عاقبة أمري' vs 'عاجله وآجله') and recommends combining both versions. After the prayer and du'a, one should proceed with the matter if one's heart feels inclined; if not, one turns away from it. The prayer is recommended in all affairs, whether religious or worldly, including Hajj and jihad, to determine the appropriate time for action, not whether to act at all.

Key Terms
استخارة (istikhara): A prayer of two rak'ahs followed by a du'a asking Allah to guide one to the best choice in a matter.
دعاء الاستخارة (du'a al-istikhara): The specific supplication taught by the Prophet to recite after the prayer, asking for guidance, power, and the best outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many rak'ahs should one pray for Salat al-Istikhara?
A) 2
B) 4
C) 8
D) 12

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istikhara is a sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs followed by a prophetic du'a, after which one should act on one's honest inclination.

Salat al-Hajah: The Prayer of Need
Ruling on the prayer of need with its proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and proper procedure of Salat al-Hajah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Salat al-Hajah is a sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs with a specific du'a, established by a hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa.

We often face needs – whether for forgiveness, relief from worry, or a legitimate worldly matter. The Prophet ﷺ taught us a comprehensive prayer to turn to Allah in such moments. This lesson presents Salat al-Hajah, its recommended procedure, and the powerful du'a to recite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that Salat al-Hajah is a prayer of two rak'ahs. Determine its hukm level based on the hadith.
The imperative 'فليتوضأ... ثم يصلي' is understood as recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa. Identify the source and type of hadith.
It is a sunnah ahad (single-chain hadith).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith indicate the ruling? The command 'فليتوضأ... ثم يصلي' is the operative phrase.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-nadb when there is evidence of recommendation; here the context of du'a and the absence of obligation turn the command to istihbab.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement among scholars regarding this prayer?
The prayer is mutually agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) in the Hanafi school; other schools may have different wordings but similarly recommend a prayer for need.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
What is the relied-upon position for practice?
The Hanafi position is that Salat al-Hajah is sunnah, and one may pray it for any need, following the prescribed du'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلاة الحاجة: وهي ركعتان، عن عبد الله بن أبي أوفى قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'من كانت له حاجة إلى الله تعالى أو إلى أحد من بني آدم فليتوضأ وليحسن الوضوء، ثم يصلي ركعتين، ثم ليثن على الله، وليصل على النبي ، ثم ليقل: لا إله إلا الله الحليم الكريم، سبحان الله رب العرش العظيم، الحمد لله رب العالمين، أسألك رحمتك، وعزائم مغفرتك، والغنيمة من كل بر، والسلامة من كل إثم لا تدع لي ذنبا إلا غفرته، ولا هما إلا فرجته، ولا حاجة لك فيها رضا إلا قضيتها يا أرحم الراحمين'. [مراقي الفلاح: ٣٩٨]
And Salat al-Hajah: It is two rak'ahs. From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever has a need from Allah or from any human being, let him perform wudu and do it well, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah, send blessings upon the Prophet, then say: None has the right to be worshipped but Allah, the Forbearing, the Generous; Glory to Allah, Lord of the Mighty Throne; all praise is for Allah, Lord of the worlds; I ask You for Your mercy and for the resources of Your forgiveness, and for the gain of every good, and for safety from every sin; do not leave any sin of mine unforgiven, nor any worry without relieving it, nor any need that is pleasing to You without fulfilling it, O Most Merciful of the Merciful.' [Maraqi al-Falah: 398]
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on Salat al-Hajah (the prayer of need). It is a sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs, preceded by a careful wudu. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa gives the full procedure: after wudu, pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah, send blessings on the Prophet, and recite the comprehensive du'a mentioned. This prayer can be offered for any need, whether religious or worldly. The du'a asks for forgiveness, relief from worries, and fulfillment of legitimate needs. It is a powerful means of supplication.

Key Terms
صلاة الحاجة (salat al-hajah): A prayer of two rak'ahs performed to ask Allah for a specific need, with a prescribed du'a.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on Ihya' al-Layali (Recommended Nights and Gatherings)
List of recommended nights with ruling on gatherings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nights recommended for revival (ihya) and state the Hanafi ruling on congregational gatherings for them.

Core Idea
Ihya al-layali is recommended individually, but congregational gatherings in mosques are makruh tanzihi.

The Hanafi school encourages staying awake on specific blessed nights in worship, but carefully distinguishes between individual practice and collective ceremonies. This lesson presents the classical list of such nights and the ruling on congregating in mosques for them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nights listed
Read the Arabic text and list the nights: last ten of Ramadan, two Eid nights, first ten of Dhul Hijjah, and mid-Sha'ban.
2
State the ruling for each night
For each night, reviving (staying awake in worship) is recommended individually.
3
Identify the prohibition
The text says 'يكره الاجتماع' meaning it is makruh to gather in congregation for these nights in mosques.
This applies to all listed nights.
4
Determine the hukm level
The word 'يكره' in Hanafi fiqh indicates makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not haram.
Some later scholars considered it makruh tahrimi if done regularly.
5
Understand the wisdom
The prohibition prevents potential innovation and disturbance to the mosque's primary function of obligatory prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإحياء ليالي العشر الأخير من رمضان، وإحياء ليلتي العيدين وليالي عشر ذي الحجة وليلة النصف من شعبان ويكره الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة من هذه الليالي في المساجد.
And reviving the nights of the last ten days of Ramadan, and reviving the two nights of the two Eids, and the nights of the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of the middle of Sha'ban. And it is makruh (disliked) to gather (in congregation) for reviving any night from these nights in the mosques.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage lists the nights that are recommended for revival (i.e., staying up in worship, prayer, and dhikr): the last ten nights of Ramadan (seeking Laylat al-Qadr), the two nights preceding Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, the first ten nights of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of the 15th of Sha'ban. However, the text explicitly states that it is makruh (disliked) to gather in congregation for these revivals inside mosques. This means that while individual worship is encouraged, organizing communal gatherings in mosques for these specific nights is discourage, as it might lead to innovation or disturbance. The dislikedness is of the type makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) or possibly makruh tahrimi? The text says 'يكره', which generally indicates tanzihi dislike in Hanafi, but the context suggests it is close to prohibition if it becomes a regular practice. This ruling helps maintain the mosque's primary function for obligatory prayers and avoids potential fitnah.

Key Terms
إحياء الليالي (ihya' al-layali): Staying awake at night in worship, prayer, and remembrance of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ihya al-layali is recommended individually on specific nights, but congregational gatherings in mosques are makruh tanzihi in the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Voluntary Prayer While Sitting
Ruling on performing nafl prayer while sitting, even when able to stand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayer while sitting, explain the reward reduction, and identify the correct sitting posture.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer while sitting is permissible but grants half the reward of standing.

This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling on voluntary (nafl) prayers performed while sitting, even if one is able to stand. While standing is superior, the school allows sitting for flexibility, with a reduction in reward. We will examine the ruling, the wisdom behind it, and the proper posture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Performing nafl prayer while sitting. The text says 'يجوز' meaning permissible.
The ruling is not haram or makruh; it is mubah.
2
Determine the reward consequence
The reward is half that of standing, unless there is an excuse. Understanding this encourages standing when able.
The exception 'except due to an excuse' covers valid reasons like illness or weakness.
3
Note the recommended posture
The text says to sit like tashahhud (iftirash). This is the chosen position in the Hanafi school.
Other postures may be allowed but this is the recommended one.
4
Handle the case of starting standing then sitting
If one begins praying standing, it is permissible to sit and complete without dislike, according to the most sound view.
Some earlier authorities considered it makruh, but the relied-upon view is no dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز النفل قاعدا مع القدرة على القيام، لكن له نصف أجر القائم إلا من عذر، المتنفل جالسا ويقعد كالمتشهد في المختار، وجاز إتمامه قاعدا بعد افتتاحه قائما بلا كراهة على الأصح، المتنفل جالسا أي إتمام القادر نفله من غير عذر
Voluntary prayer while sitting is permissible even with ability to stand, but he has half the reward of the one standing except due to an excuse. The one performing nafl while sitting sits like in the tashahhud (in the chosen position). And it is permissible for him to complete it sitting after starting it standing without dislike according to the most sound view. 'The one performing nafl while sitting' means the one who can stand completing his nafl without excuse.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on performing nafl (voluntary) prayers while sitting, even if one is physically able to stand. It is permissible, but the reward is half that of praying standing, unless there is a valid excuse (illness, weakness). The preferred sitting posture is like that of tashahhud (sitting on the left foot, right foot upright). Additionally, if one starts the prayer standing, one may later sit and complete it, and this is not disliked (the most sound view). However, the commentary by al-Tahtawi notes that some scholars, like the author of al-Hidayah, consider it disliked if done without reason like fatigue. The overall ruling allows flexibility for nafl prayers, which are not bound by the same strictness as fard.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayers (including both sunnah and nafl specifically).
قاعدا (qa'idan): Sitting while praying, specifically for voluntary prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Disliked (makruh)
B) Permissible without dislike
C) Invalid (batil)
D) Obligatory to stand

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits nafl prayer while sitting, even without excuse, with half reward, and sitting after starting standing is not disliked.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Reviving Specific Nights and Dislike of Gathering
Ruling statement on recommended nights and dislike of gathering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reviving specific nights and identify when congregational gathering becomes disliked.

Core Idea
Individual revival of certain nights is recommended; gathering in mosques for it is disliked to prevent innovation.

The Hanafi school encourages spending select nights in worship, but draws a careful line against formal congregational assemblies that may lead to bid'ah. This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the nights and clarifies the ruling on gathering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nights mentioned
List the five occasions: last ten of Ramadan, nights of the two Eids, ten of Dhul Hijjah, and mid-Sha'ban.
The last ten of Ramadan include Laylat al-Qadr.
2
Understand the ruling on individual revival
The term 'nadb' indicates it is recommended (mandub) to spend these nights in worship individually.
Worship includes prayer, dhikr, and Quran recitation.
3
Understand the ruling on gathering
The text says 'yukrahu al-ijtima'' – it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to gather in mosques for collective revival.
Dislike is due to concern for innovation and disturbance.
4
Recognize the scope
The phrase 'al-mutaqaddim dhikruha aw ghayriha' extends the dislike to any night, not just those listed.
This prevents any form of regular congregational qiyam outside prescribed sunnah.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may permit or recommend such gatherings; the Hanafi position prioritizes avoiding bid'ah.
This reflects the school's cautious approach to ibadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ندب إحياء ليالي العشر الأخير من رمضان، وإحياء ليلتي العيدين وليالي عشر ذي الحجة وليلة النصف من شعبان ويكره الاجتماع على إحياء ليلة من هذه الليالي في المساجد. المتقدم ذكرها أو غيرها
It is recommended to revive the nights of the last ten of Ramadan, and to revive the two nights of the two Eids, and the nights of the ten of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of the middle of Sha'ban. And it is disliked to gather for reviving any night from these nights in the mosques, whether the previously mentioned or others.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah regarding recommended nights for worship (qiyam al-layl). It lists five occasions: the last ten nights of Ramadan (emphasizing Laylat al-Qadr), the two nights before Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha (or the nights of Eid themselves), the first ten nights of Dhul Hijjah, and the night of mid-Sha'ban. The ruling states that these nights are recommended (mandub) for individual revival through prayer, dhikr, and Quran recitation. However, it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to gather in mosques collectively for these revivals, as that may introduce innovation or disturb the mosque's tranquility. The phrase 'al-mutaqaddim dhikruha aw ghayriha' includes even other nights not mentioned. This ruling preserves the Hanafi principle that individual devotion is preferred over formal congregational assemblies beyond the prescribed sunnah.

Key Terms
إحياء (ihya'): Spending the night in worship, including prayer, dhikr, and recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Recommended (mandub)
B) Disliked (makruh tanzihi)
C) Permissible (mubah)
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
Individual revival of specific nights is recommended, but gathering in mosques for such revivals is disliked to avoid innovation.

Reward and Ruling for Voluntary Prayer While Sitting
Ruling on voluntary prayer while sitting with reward and posture details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing nafl prayer while sitting, identify the reward reduction, and explain the conditions for equal reward.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer while sitting is permissible but reward is halved unless there is a valid excuse.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the fiqh of nafl prayer for a person who sits despite being able to stand. It distinguishes between voluntary and obligatory prayer, explains the preferred seated posture, and addresses the dispute about when sitting becomes disliked. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary guilt and highlights the role of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Nafl prayer while sitting is permissible (ja'iz) even if one can stand. The word 'nafl' includes all voluntary prayers, including sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Note the reward division
Without excuse: half the reward of standing. With valid excuse (illness, etc.): full reward by consensus. Gesture prayer for the excused is even better than a standing person's prayer.
3
Determine the seated posture
Sit like in tashahhud (iftirash): spread left foot, sit on it, erect right foot. This is the chosen view (al-mukhtar). Some recommend squatting (ihtiba).
4
Understand the ikhtilaf on completing while sitting
If one starts nafl standing and then sits without excuse, it is permissible without dislike according to the correct view. However, al-Hidayah considers it makruh if due to fatigue or laziness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز النفل قاعدا مع القدرة على القيام، لكن له نصف أجر القائم إلا من عذر، ويقعد كالمتشهد في المختار، وجاز إتمامه قاعدا بعد افتتاحه قائما بلا كراهة على الأصح. في صلاة النفل: إنما عبر به؛ ليشمل السنن المؤكدة وغيرها. إلا إلخ: أي إلا أنهم قالوا: هذا في حق القادر، أما العاجز من عذر فصلاته بالإيماء أفضل من صلاة القائم الراكع الساجد؛ لأنه جهد المقل، والإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة القاعد بعذر مساوية لصلاة القائم في الأجر. كالمتشهد إذا لم يكن به عذر فيفترش رجله اليسرى، ويجلس عليها، وينصب يمناه. وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يضع يمناه على يسراه تحت سرته، لكن صرح في كتاب "سياسة الدنيا والدين" بأنه يضع، وإليه يشير قولهم إن القعود كالقيام. في المختار ولكن ذكر شيخ الإسلام: الأفضل له أن يقعد في موضع القيام محتبئا. وجاز إلخ أي إن شرع الرجل في النفل وهو قائم، ثم قعد في الركعة الأولى أو الثانية جاز له على الأصح واختار صاحب "الهداية" الكراهة إذا كان كالإعياء والتعب. من غير عذر
It is permissible to perform nafl while sitting even when able to stand, but he has half the reward of the one standing unless there is an excuse. And he sits like in tashahhud according to the chosen view. And it is permissible to complete it while sitting after beginning it standing without dislike on the correct view. Regarding nafl prayer: he only expressed it thus to include the confirmed sunnah and others. 'Except' etc.: meaning except that they said: this applies to the one able; as for the one unable due to an excuse, his prayer with gestures is better than the prayer of the one standing, bowing, and prostrating because it is the effort of the poor, and consensus is established that the prayer of the one sitting due to an excuse equals the standing in reward. 'Like tashahhud' means if he has no excuse, he spreads his left foot, sits on it, and erects his right. There is indication that he does not place his right hand on his left below his navel, but the book 'Siyasat al-Dunya wa al-Din' states he does place them, and their saying that sitting is like standing points to it. In the chosen view, but Shaykh al-Islam mentioned: it is better for him to sit in the place of standing in a squatting position. 'And it is permissible' etc.: meaning if a man begins nafl standing, then sits in the first or second rak'ah, it is permissible on the correct view, but the author of al-Hidayah chose dislike if it is due to fatigue or tiredness. Without excuse.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi rulings on voluntary (nafl) prayer while sitting. The main ruling states that one may perform nafl sitting even if able to stand, but the reward is half that of standing. However, if there is a valid excuse (e.g., illness), the reward is equal. The commentary expands: for those with an excuse, praying with ishara (gestures) is superior to even a standing person's prayer because it shows utmost humility. The seated posture is like tashahhud (iftaresh) – left foot splayed, sitting on it, right foot upright. Some scholars differ on hand placement; the chosen view is not to place hands below navel, but some allow it. If one starts nafl standing and then sits with an excuse, it is allowed without dislike. But if sitting without excuse, the author of al-Hidayah considers it disliked due to laziness. The commentary also notes consensus that the reward for a seated person with excuse equals that of a standing person.

Key Terms
المتشهد (al-mutashahhad): The sitting posture for tashahhud: iftirash (spreading left foot and sitting on it, erecting right).
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred opinion within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half the reward of the standing person
C) No reward
D) Double the reward

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer sitting is permissible; reward is halved unless excused, and the posture is like tashahhud.

Istikhara and Salat al-Hajah: Two Recommended Prayers for Seeking Guidance and Fulfilling Needs
Rulings on two recommended prayers with their method and du'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istikhara and salat al-hajah, explain the purpose of istikhara (timing vs. act), and describe the method of both prayers including the prescribed du'a.

Core Idea
Istikhara guides timing, not decision; Salat al-Hajah is a dua wrapped in prayer.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents two important recommended prayers: Istikhara for seeking the best time for a good deed, and Salat al-Hajah for presenting one's needs to Allah. Both are grounded in the Sunnah and have specific etiquettes and supplications. Understanding these practices enriches one's worship and reliance on Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prayers and their rulings
Read the passage and note the two prayers: Istikhara and Salat al-Hajah. The text states they are understood for determining timing (istikhara) and for fulfilling needs (salat al-hajah). Both are recommended (sunnah muakkadah).
Istikhara is not for deciding between good and bad, but for timing a good deed.
2
Understand the unique Hanafi interpretation of istikhara
The Hanafi school holds that istikhara applies to all good deeds (like Hajj, jihad) but only to determine the time, not the act itself. The act is already known to be good; istikhara helps choose when to do it.
This distinguishes Hanafi view from some other schools that limit istikhara to specific matters.
3
Memorize the steps of Istikhara
The passage says: pray two rak'ahs (like any sunnah prayer), recite al-Kafirun in the first rak'ah and al-Ikhlas in the second, repeat the prayer seven times, then act according to what one's heart opens to.
Repeating seven times is recommended, not obligatory.
4
Analyze the hadith for Salat al-Hajah
The hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa prescribes: perform wudu well, pray two rak'ahs, praise Allah and send salawat on the Prophet, then recite the specific du'a that includes seeking mercy, forgiveness, all good, safety from sin, and fulfillment of needs.
The du'a is comprehensive and should be recited after the prayer.
5
Apply the general principle: both are sunnah muakkadah
The commands in the hadith (falyatawadda', thumma yusalli) indicate recommendation, not obligation. In Hanafi fiqh, such commands from ahad hadith are interpreted as mandub (recommended) unless there is a qarina for obligation.
Therefore, both prayers are recommended but not required; leaving them is not sinful but missing out on great reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاستخارة في الحج والجهاد وجميع أبواب الخير تحمل على تعيين الوقت لا نفس الفعل، وإذا استخار مضى لما ينشرح صدره، وينبغي أن يكررها سبع مرات، ويقرأ في الأولى بالكافرون، وفي الثانية بالإخلاص. وصلاة الحاجة: وهي ركعتان، عن عبد الله بن أبي أوفى قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "من كانت له حاجة إلى الله تعالى أو إلى أحد من بني آدم فليتوضأ وليحسن الوضوء، ثم يصلي ركعتين، ثم ليثن على الله، وليصل على النبي، ثم ليقل: لا إله إلا الله الحليم الكريم، سبحان الله رب العرش العظيم، الحمد لله رب العالمين، أسألك رحمتك، وعزائم مغفرتك، والغنيمة من كل بر، والسلامة من كل إثم لا تدع لي ذنبا إلا غفرته، ولا هما إلا فرجته، ولا حاجة لك فيها رضا إلا قضيتها يا أرحم الراحمين".
And istikhara regarding Hajj, jihad, and all gates of good is understood to determine the time, not the act itself. And when one performs istikhara, he proceeds with what his heart opens to, and he should repeat it seven times, and recite in the first rak'ah al-Kafirun, and in the second al-Ikhlas. And Salat al-Hajah: it is two rak'ahs. From 'Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever has a need from Allah or from any of the children of Adam, let him perform wudu' and do it well, then pray two rak'ahs, then praise Allah and send salawat upon the Prophet, then say: La ilaha illa Allah al-Halim al-Karim, Subhan Allah Rabbi al-'Arsh al-'Azim, al-Hamdu li-llahi Rabbi al-'Alamin, as'aluka rahmataka wa 'azaima maghfiratika wal-ghanimata min kulli birr wa al-salamata min kulli ithm, la tada' li dhanban illa ghafartahu wa la hamman illa farrajtahu wa la hajatan laka fiha rida illa qadaytaha ya arham al-rahimin."
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents two recommended prayers: Istikhara and Salat al-Hajah. For Istikhara, the ruling clarifies that it relates to determining the timing of an action (e.g., when to perform Hajj or jihad), not whether to do the act itself (since the act is already good and determined). One should pray two rak'ahs (like any sunnah prayer) and then recite specific surahs (al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas). The prayer should be repeated seven times, and the person acts according to the inclination of his heart. Salat al-Hajah is a two-rak'ah prayer followed by a lengthy du'a reported in a hadith from Ibn Abi Awfa. The du'a includes praise, salawat, and a comprehensive supplication for forgiveness, relief from worries, and fulfillment of needs. Both prayers are forms of nafl (voluntary worship) and are recommended for seeking guidance or divine assistance in worldly or religious matters.

Key Terms
الاستخارة (al-istikhara): A prayer seeking guidance from Allah to choose the best time for an action.
صلاة الحاجة (salat al-hajah): A two-rak'ah prayer followed by a specific du'a to fulfill a need from Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To determine whether the act itself is good
B) To determine the specific time to perform the act
C) To make the act obligatory
D) To guarantee success

Key Takeaway
Both Istikhara and Salat al-Hajah are sunnah muakkadah acts; Istikhara determines timing, not the act, and Salat al-Hajah is a dua after prayer.

Voluntary Prayer on a Mount: Complete Hanafi Rulings
Rulings on performing nafl prayer while riding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for voluntary prayer on a mount, including conditions, gestures, building rules, leaning, the najasah exception, and the invalidity of walking or swimming during prayer.

Core Idea
Nafl on a mount is recommended; najasah does not invalidate, but walking or swimming does.

This lesson covers the Hanafi fiqh on performing voluntary (nafl) prayer while riding an animal or mount. The text addresses the circumstances under which such prayer is permissible, the method of gesturing for bowing and prostration, and special rules for continuity when dismounting or mounting. It also clarifies that impurity on the mount does not break the prayer, while walking or swimming during prayer invalidates it entirely. These rulings reflect the school's accommodation for travelers and those in need, balancing ease with legal discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is voluntary (nafl) prayer performed while riding a mount. The ruling is mandub (recommended) or at least permissible (mubah). The text says 'يتنفل راكباً' meaning it is allowed, rather encouraged.
This is not for obligatory prayers; only nafl.
2
Specify the conditions for validity
The prayer must be performed outside the built-up area (outside the city or village), the rider makes gestures (ima') for ruku and sujud, and the direction is wherever the mount naturally faces. The condition of facing qibla is dropped.
If inside the city, facing the mount's direction is not allowed.
3
Apply the building rule on dismounting and mounting
If one starts the prayer while riding, then dismounts, he may continue (build) from where he left off. However, if he starts on the ground and then mounts, he cannot build; he must start a new prayer.
The difference is because the mount is the locus of concession; dismounting is a return to normal, so continuity is allowed.
4
Understand the ruling on leaning
Leaning on something during the prayer is permissible if the rider is tired. Without an excuse, it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it shows disrespect, but it does not invalidate.
This is according to the most apparent view (al-azhar).
5
Examine the najasah exception
Najasah (impurity) on the mount, even on the saddle or stirrups, does not invalidate the prayer according to the majority of Hanafi scholars. The text says 'على الأصح'. A minority (Muhammad bin Muqatil and Abu Hafs) restrict the exemption to less than a dirham's amount, but the relied-upon view is absolute permission.
Walking or swimming during prayer invalidates by consensus (ijma) of the Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتنفل راكبا خارج المصر مؤمياً إلى أي جهة توجهت دابته وبنى بنزوله لا بركوبه ولو كان بالنوافل الراتبة، وعن أبي حنيفة لله: أنه ينزل لسنة الفجر؛ لأنها أكد من غيرها، وجاز للمتطوع الاتكاء على شيء إن تعب بلا كراهة، وإن كان بغير عذر كره في الأظهر لإساءة الأدب، ولا يمنع صحة الصلاة على الدابة نجاسة عليها ولو كانت في السرج والركابين على الأصح، ولا تصح صلاة الماشي بالإجماع. وكذا السابح أي إجماع أئمتنا وهو قول أكثر مشايخنا في بعض. و يتنفل راكباً: أي جاز له التنفل بل ندب له. خارج المصر: يعني خارج العمران؛ ليشمل خارج القرية والأخبية بمحل إذا دخله مسافر قصر الفرض، وسواء كان مسافراً، أو الحاجة خرج النواحي. مؤميا إلخ فلو سجد على سرجه أو على شيء وضع عنده يكون عبثاً لا فائدة فيه، فيكره، ولا تفسد؛ لأنه إيماء وزيادة اللهم إلا أن يكون ذلك الشيء نجساً، فتفسد لاتصال النجاسة به. توجهت دابته إلخ أشار به إلى أنه إذا صلى إلى غير ما توجهت به دابته لا يجوز؛ لعدم الضرورة إلى ذلك. وفي توحيد الضمير في قوله: "مؤمياً" وقوله: "به" إشارة إلى أن الصلاة على الدابة لا تصح بالجماعة، فإن فعلوا فصلاة الإمام صحيحة، وصلاة القوم فاسدة. وبنى بنزوله إلخ أي إذا افتتح التطوع راكباً، ثم نزل يبني، ولا يبني بركوبه أي إذا افتتح نازلا ثم ركب. لا بركوبه: أي لا يجوز له البناء بعد ركوبه على ما مضى من صلاته نازلاً. بالنوافل الراتبة المؤكدة وغيرها حتى سنة الفجر. وإن كان بغير إلخ: أي وإن كان الاتكاء بغير عذر كره في الأظهر؛ لإساءة الأدب، بخلاف القعود بغير عذر بعد القيام؛ فإنه لا كراهة فيه على الأصح. ولا يمنع صحة إلخ : أي صلى رجل على دابة وعليها نجاسة قليلة كانت أو كثيرة، وسواء كانت في سرجها أو في ركابيها تصح صلاته ولا تمنع هذه النجاسة صحتها، قال في "العناية : لأن الركوع والسجود إذا سقط ركنين فلأن يسقط طهارة المكان وهو شرط ،أولى وفيه نظر؛ لأنه يستلزم جوازه بلا وضوء، ولا يلزم من سقوط الشيء إلى خلف سقوط ما لا خلف له فكان ما قال محمد بن مقاتل وأبو حفص الكبير : إذا كانت النجاسة في موضع الجلوس أو الركابين أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا يجوز الصلاة، وهو القياس اعتباراً للصلاة على الدابة بالصلاة على الأرض، وإن كان عامة المشايخ على الجواز للضرورة.
And he performs nafl while riding outside the city, making gestures towards whatever direction his mount faces, and he builds upon his prayer when dismounting but not when mounting, even if it is for the regular supererogatory prayers. And from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): that he dismounts for the sunnah of Fajr because it is stronger than others. And it is permissible for the volunteer to lean on something if tired without dislike; but if without excuse, it is disliked in the most apparent view due to bad manners. And najasah on the mount does not prevent the validity of the prayer, even if it is on the saddle or stirrups according to the correct view. And the prayer of a walking person is not valid by consensus. And likewise the swimming person, meaning by consensus of our imams, and it is the saying of most of our senior scholars in some [matters]. 'He performs nafl while riding': meaning it is permissible for him, rather recommended. 'Outside the city': meaning outside the built-up area; to include outside the village and tents in a place where a traveler would shorten the obligatory prayer, whether he is a traveler or has a need to go out to the outskirts. 'Making gestures' etc.: if he prostrates on his saddle or on something placed near him, it is futile and useless, so it is disliked, but it does not invalidate because it is gesture and addition; unless that thing is najis, then it invalidates due to contact with najasah. 'To whatever direction his mount faces' etc.: he indicated that if he prays to other than the direction his mount faces, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. And in the singular pronoun in his saying 'making gestures' and 'him' there is indication that prayer on a mount is not valid in congregation; if they do it, the prayer of the imam is valid, and the prayer of the people is invalid. 'And he builds upon his dismounting' etc.: if he begins the nafl riding, then dismounts, he builds; and he does not build upon his mounting, meaning if he begins dismounted then mounts. 'Not upon his mounting': meaning he is not allowed to build after mounting on what preceded of his prayer while dismounted. 'Even for the regular affirmed sunan' and others, including even the sunnah of Fajr. 'And if it is without' etc.: meaning if leaning is without an excuse, it is disliked in the most apparent view due to bad manners, unlike sitting without excuse after standing; there is no dislike in that on the correct view. 'And najasah does not prevent the validity' etc.: meaning if a man prays on a mount and there is najasah on it, little or much, whether on its saddle or its stirrups, his prayer is valid and this najasah does not prevent its validity. It is said in al-'Inayah: because if bowing and prostrating are dropped as two pillars, then dropping the condition of cleanliness of place is more appropriate. But there is consideration: because it entails its permissibility without wudu', and the dropping of a thing to the rear does not entail dropping of what has no rear. So what Muhammad bin Muqatil and Abu Hafs al-Kabir said: if the najasah is in the place of sitting or the stirrups more than a dirham's amount, the prayer is not valid. And this is the analogy considering the prayer on a mount like prayer on the ground. However, the majority of the mashayikh accept the permissibility due to necessity.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage covers the Hanafi rulings for voluntary prayer while riding an animal (or in a vehicle analogously). It is permissible (actually recommended) to perform nafl prayer while riding outside the city, making gestures (ima') for bowing and prostrating, facing any direction the mount goes. The prayer is valid even if the mount moves; one can continue the prayer when dismounting but not when mounting again (if one starts on ground, must complete there). The exception is the sunnah of Fajr: Abu Hanifa said one should dismount for it because it is more emphasized. Leaning on something while praying is allowed if tired, but disliked if without excuse due to disrespect. Najasah (impurity) on the animal, even on the saddle or stirrups, does not invalidate the prayer according to the relied-upon view, though some early scholars (Muhammad bin Muqatil, Abu Hafs al-Kabir) limited it to less than a dirham. Prayer while walking (mashi) or swimming (sabih) is invalid by consensus of the Hanafi imams because these involve excessive movement. The commentary also explains that congregational prayer on a mount is invalid for the followers, though the imam's prayer may be valid. The majority dispense najasah for necessity, but the strict qiyas would require purity.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head for bowing and prostration, performed by a rider or sick person.
البناء (al-bina'): Continuing the prayer from where it left off, allowed when dismounting but not when mounting.
النوافل الراتبة (al-nawafil al-ratibah): Regular confirmed supererogatory prayers associated with the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

The Hanafi school allows great flexibility for nafl prayer while riding, including gestures, facing any direction, and disregarding impurity on the mount, but walking or swimming invalidates it entirely.

Praying Nafl on a Mount with Gestures (Ima')
Ruling on voluntary prayer on a riding animal outside inhabited areas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid voluntary prayer on a riding animal and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the Fajr sunnah.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer on a mount is valid with head gestures, but you cannot continue if you start on ground and then mount.

This lesson covers the permissibility of performing voluntary (nafl) prayers while riding on an animal outside inhabited areas. We learn the conditions for validity, the use of gestures (ima') instead of full bowing and prostration, and the rule about continuing prayer when dismounting or mounting. A notable difference within the Hanafi school arises regarding the sunnah of Fajr.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its ruling
Identify the act: performing voluntary (nafl) prayer while riding an animal (dābba) outside the settlement (khārij al-miṣr). The ruling: it is permissible (jā'iz) and recommended (mandūb).
The prayer is performed with gestures (īmā') instead of full rukū' and sujūd.
2
List the conditions for validity
The rider must be outside the built-up area (miṣr), face the direction his mount turns (not intentionally turn away), and gesture with his head for bowing and prostrating. Prostration on the saddle is disliked (makrūh) but does not invalidate unless the object is impure.
If the rider is inside the city, he must dismount and pray normally.
3
Understand the building rule
If he begins the prayer while riding and then dismounts, he may continue (build) from where he left off. However, if he begins while dismounted and then mounts, he cannot continue; he must restart the prayer.
This applies only to voluntary prayers, not obligatory prayers.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Fajr sunnah
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that one should dismount for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it permissible to pray it while riding, like other sunan.
The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is that dismounting is preferable for Fajr sunnah, but praying while riding is permissible.
5
Identify what invalidates the prayer
The prayer is invalidated if the rider intentionally turns away from the mount's direction (unnecessary), or if he prostrates on an impure object, as contact with impurity (najāsah) nullifies the prayer.
Otherwise, the prayer remains valid despite disliked actions like prostrating on the saddle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٦] بالنوافل الراتبة المؤكدة وغيرها حتى سنة الفجر مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٦
And he may perform supererogatory prayer while riding outside the settlement, gesturing (ima') towards any direction his mount turns, and he may build [on his prayer] when he dismounts, not when he mounts. Even if it is among the regular sunan prayers. And from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: he dismounts for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. Commentary: "He may perform supererogatory prayer while riding": i.e., it is permissible for him, rather recommended. "Outside the settlement": meaning outside the built-up area; includes outside the village and tents, a place where if a traveler enters, he shortens the obligatory prayer. Whether he is traveling or has a need to go out. "Gesturing": if he prostrates on his saddle or on something placed near him, it is futile and disliked, but the prayer is not invalidated because it is ima' plus an addition. Unless that thing is impure, then it is invalidated due to contact with impurity. "To any direction his mount turns": indicates that if he prays facing other than where his mount goes, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity. And the unification of the pronoun in "gesturing" and "with it" indicates that prayer on an animal is not valid in congregation; if they do, the imam's prayer is valid and the followers' prayer is invalid. "And he may build when he dismounts": if he begins the voluntary prayer riding, then dismounts, he builds; he does not build when he mounts, i.e., if he begins dismounted then mounts, he may not build upon his previous prayer. "Regular sunan prayers": emphasized and others, even the sunnah of Fajr.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for performing nafl (voluntary) prayers while riding outside built-up areas (outside the city or village limits). The key points: (1) The rider may gesture (ima') with his head for ruku' and sujud rather than full prostration. (2) He may pray facing any direction his mount turns; intentionally turning away is not allowed. (3) If he begins the prayer while riding and then dismounts, he may continue from where he left off. Conversely, if he begins dismounted and then mounts, he cannot continue—he must restart. (4) This applies to all voluntary prayers, including the regular sunan (rawatib), except according to Abu Hanifa, for the sunnah of Fajr the rider should dismount because it is more emphasized. The commentary clarifies that 'outside the settlement' means outside the built-up area where travel rulings apply. Gesturing is valid; prostrating on the saddle is considered futile (abath) and disliked (makruh tanzihan), but does not invalidate unless the object is impure. Congregational prayer on an animal is not valid; only the imam's prayer is valid.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā'): Gesturing with the head as a substitute for bowing and prostrating in prayer, used when full bodily movement is not possible (e.g., on a riding animal).
الدابة (al-dābba): A riding animal (horse, mule, donkey, etc.) used for travel.
النافلة الراتبة (al-nāfila al-rātiba): The regularly performed supererogatory prayers associated with the five daily prayers (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Leaning During Voluntary Prayer (Nafl)
Ruling on leaning during nafl prayer with distinction between excuse and no excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaning (ittika') during voluntary prayer and distinguish between the cases with and without excuse.

Core Idea
Leaning without excuse is makruh tanzih; leaning with excuse is permissible without dislike.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on leaning on something for support during a voluntary (nafl) prayer. The text distinguishes between two scenarios: when the worshiper is genuinely tired and when he leans without excuse. Understanding this distinction helps protect the prayer's etiquette while accommodating human weakness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is leaning (ittika') during a voluntary prayer. Determine the reason for leaning: is there an excuse like tiredness?
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
With excuse (tired): permissible without dislike. Without excuse: disliked (makruh tanzih) due to poor etiquette.
The dislike is not prohibitive; the prayer remains valid.
3
Note the comparison with sitting after standing
The commentary says sitting without excuse after standing is not disliked, whereas leaning is. So the dislike is specific to leaning, not to all postural changes.
4
Understand the epistemological weight
The ruling is stated as 'in the apparent view' (fi al-azhar), indicating it is the relied-upon position from the school's core texts.
This is a strong transmission, not a weak opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاز للمتطوع الاتكاء على شيء إن تعب بلا كراهة، وإن كان بغير عذر كره في الأظهر لإساءة الأدب، وإن كان بغير إلخ: أي وإن كان الاتكاء بغير عذر كره في الأظهر؛ لإساءة الأدب، بخلاف القعود بغير عذر بعد القيام؛ فإنه لا كراهة فيه على الأصح [الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٧]

Commentary: "But if it is without excuse": i.e., if the leaning is without excuse, it is disliked in the apparent view due to poor etiquette, contrary to sitting without excuse after standing; there is no dislike in that according to the soundest view.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage rules on leaning (itika') during a voluntary prayer. If the worshiper is tired and needs support, it is permissible without any dislike (karahah). However, if he leans without a valid excuse (e.g., mere laziness), it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it shows poor etiquette (isā'at al-adab). The commentary distinguishes this from sitting after standing without excuse, which is not disliked. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that leaning without excuse is makruh tanzih, not makruh tahrimi, so the prayer remains valid but reward may be lessened.

Key Terms
الاتكاء (al-ittikā'): Leaning on something for support during prayer, typically on a wall or staff.
