Impurity on the Mount: Validity of Prayer
Ruling on impurity on the mount and its effect on prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on impurity on a riding animal and distinguish the majority view from the minority view based on necessity and qiyas.

Core Idea
Impurity on the mount does not invalidate prayer, even in large amounts, due to necessity.

This lesson examines the effect of impurity (najis) on a riding animal during prayer. The source presents the soundest view that impurity does not prevent validity, along with an intra-madhhab dispute. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the interplay between conditions, pillars, and the principle of necessity (darurah) that overrides analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the statement: impurity does not prevent the validity of prayer on a mount. Note the scope: any impurity, even on the saddle or stirrups, little or much.
This is the majority view, labeled 'al-ashah' (soundest).
2
Understand the reasoning from necessity
Read the quotation from al-Inayah: since ruku' and sujud (pillars) are dropped symbolically, the condition of purity of place is a fortiori dropped. Recognize that this is an istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity.
The reasoning is not accepted by all; the author notes a critique regarding wudu.
3
Identify the minority counter-argument
Muhammad bin Muqatil and Abu Hafs al-Kabir argued that if impurity exceeds a dirham, prayer is invalid. They applied qiyas, comparing prayer on a mount to prayer on the ground.
This view is based on strict analogy and is not the mufta bihi.
4
Recognize the tarjih (preference)
The text states 'amma al-mashayikh 'ala al-jawaz' (the majority of scholars are on permissibility). Thus the mufta bihi is the dispensatory view.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah supports permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يمنع صحة الصلاة على الدابة نجاسة عليها ولو كانت في السرج والركابين على الأصح، ولا تصح صلاة الماشي بالإجماع. وكذا السابح أي إجماع أئمتنا، ولا يمنع صحة إلخ : أي صلى رجل على دابة وعليها نجاسة قليلة كانت أو كثيرة، وسواء كانت في سرجها أو في ركابيها تصح صلاته ولا تمنع هذه النجاسة صحتها، قال في "العناية : لأن الركوع والسجود إذا سقط ركنين فلأن يسقط طهارة المكان وهو شرط أولى وفيه نظر؛ لأنه يستلزم جوازه بلا وضوء، ولا يلزم من سقوط الشيء إلى خلف سقوط ما لا خلف له فكان ما قال محمد بن مقاتل وأبو حفص الكبير : إذا كانت النجاسة في موضع الجلوس أو الركابين أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا يجوز الصلاة، وهو القياس اعتباراً للصلاة على الدابة بالصلاة على الأرض، وإن كان عامة المشايخ على الجواز للضرورة.
And impurity on the riding animal does not prevent the validity of prayer upon it, even if it is on the saddle and stirrups, according to the soundest view. And the prayer of one walking is not valid by consensus. Likewise, the one swimming [i.e., praying while moving] is by consensus of our imams. Commentary: "And impurity does not prevent validity": i.e., a man prays on an animal with impurity, little or much, whether on its saddle or stirrups, his prayer is valid and this impurity does not prevent its validity. He said in al-Inayah: "Because when ruku' and sujud fall as pillars, then the purity of place, which is a condition, falls even more so." But there is a critique: it would imply permissibility without wudu, and the falling of one thing does not necessitate the falling of that which has no substitute. So what Muhammad bin Muqatil and Abu Hafs al-Kabir said: if the impurity on the sitting place or stirrups exceeds a dirham's amount, the prayer is not permissible. That is the analogical reasoning (qiyas) considering prayer on an animal like prayer on the ground. However, the majority of scholars are on permissibility due to necessity.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage deals with the effect of impurity (najis) on the riding animal. The ruling states that impurity does not invalidate the prayer performed on the animal, even if the impurity is directly on the saddle or stirrups. This is the soundest (asah) view. The prayer of a person who is walking (mashi) or swimming (sabih) is invalid by consensus, because they cannot maintain stillness. The commentary from al-Inayah explains that since ruku' and sujud (pillars) are dropped entirely, the condition of purity of place is dropped a fortiori. However, a counterargument is given: this reasoning would justify prayer without wudu, which is not accepted. Therefore, Muhammad bin Muqatil and Abu Hafs al-Kabir held that if the impurity in the sitting area exceeds a dirham's size, the prayer is invalid. This latter view is based on qiyas, comparing prayer on an animal to prayer on the ground. Nevertheless, the majority of Hanafi scholars (jumhur al-mashayikh) prefer the ruling of permissibility due to necessity.

Key Terms
السرج (al-sarj): The saddle of the riding animal.
الركابين (al-rikābayn): The stirrups, where the feet rest.
القَياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning comparing prayer on an animal to prayer on the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The prayer must be repeated after purification.
D) Impurity on the saddle always invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Impurity on a riding animal does not invalidate prayer because necessity (darurah) overrides the normal condition of purity of place.

Obligatory Prayer on a Riding Animal: Conditions of Necessity
Ruling with conditions for permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that obligatory prayers are invalid on a mount, list the valid excuses that permit it, and explain the manner of prayer (facing qiblah, gestures) when such excuses exist.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayer on a mount is invalid except for genuine necessity — fear, mud, or a refractory animal.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes the general principle that fard and wajib prayers cannot be performed on a riding animal; they require standing on the ground facing the qiblah. However, Islam provides relief for genuine hardship. The text enumerates specific excuses (darurah) that make it permissible to pray on a mount, along with the proper method (gestures, facing qiblah if possible). Understanding these conditions is essential for maintaining prayer in difficult circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State clearly that the default ruling is: obligatory (fard) and wajib prayers (like witr, nadhr) are not valid on a riding animal. This includes funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah when the verse was recited on the ground.
The rule is absolute unless a specific excuse is present.
2
List the valid excuses
From the passage, enumerate the five causes of necessity that permit praying on a mount: fear of a thief or wild beast, excessive mud that would soil the face/dress, a refractory animal that may bolt, and inability to find help to mount (due to weakness).
Mere dampness (naudah) is not a valid excuse.
3
Understand the manner of prayer
If an excuse exists, the rider should stop the animal if possible, face the qiblah, and pray with gestures (ima) for ruku and sujud. If the animal cannot be stopped, he prays in the direction it faces, even if it turns away from the qiblah.
If placed in a mahmil with a board touching the ground, it is like the ground and one must stand fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة الفرض والواجب على الدابة لا يصح على الدابة صلاة الفرائض والواجبات كالوتر والمنذور، وما شرع فيه نفض فأفسده، ولا صلاة الجنازة وسجدة تليت آيتها على الأرض إلا لضرورة كخوف لص على نفسه أو دابته أو ثيابه لو نزل، وخوف سبع، وطين المكان، وجموح الدابة، وعدم وجدان من يركبه لعجزه، والصلاة في المحمل على الدابة كالصلاة عليها، سواء كانت سائرة أو واقفة ولو جعل تحت المحمل خشبة حتى بقي قراره إلى الأرض كان بمنزلة الأرض، فتصح الفريضة فيه قائماً. وما شرع فيه نفل إلخ الكلام على حذف مضاف، أي ولا يصح قضاء نفل أفسده بعد ما شرع فيه. تليت آيتها أي لا يصح أداء سجدة تليت آيتها حال كون التالي على الأرض، ثم ركب الدابة، احترز به عما إذا تليت آية السجدة حال كون التالي على الدابة، فإنها تصح عليها. لضرورة قال في "الخلاصة : أما صلاة الفرض على الدابة بالعذر فجائزة، فيقف عليها أي مستقبل القبلة، ويصلي بالإيماء إن أمكنه إيقاف الدابة، فإن لم يمكنه صلى أينما توجهت ولو مستدبر القبلة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٠٧] وطين أي كوجود طين في المكان يغيب فيه الوجه أو يلطخه أو يتلف ما يبسط عليه، أما مجرد ندوة فلا يبيح ذلك، والذي لا دابة له يصلي قائماً في الطين بالإيماء. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٧] وجموح الدابة: أي إذا خاف الراكب جموح الدابة إن نزل عنها، ولم يجد من يركبه عليها جاز له الصلاة عليها بالاتفاق ولا تلزمه الإعادة بزوال العذر وعدم وجدان إلخ أي إذا لم يجد الراكب على الدابة من يركبه على دابته إن نزل منها، ونفسه عاجزة عن الركوب عليها من غير إعانة أحد، فله أداء ما ذكر من من صلاة الفرض والواجبات وغيرها كالصلاة في التفاصيل التي عرفتها آنفا. قائما: فإن لم يمكنه القيام، ولا النزول صلى قاعدا.
Section on obligatory and wajib prayer on a riding animal. It is not valid to perform on a riding animal the obligatory prayers and duties like witr and vows, and what he began as nafl and then ruined, nor funeral prayer nor a prostration of recitation whose verse was recited on the ground, except due to necessity: such as fear of a thief for himself or his animal or his clothes if he dismounts, fear of a wild beast, mud on the ground, a refractory animal, and inability to find someone to mount him due to his inability. And prayer in a litter (mahmil) on the animal is like prayer on it, whether moving or stationary. And if a board is placed under the litter so that its base remains to the ground, it is like the ground, so the obligatory prayer in it while standing is valid. Commentary: "What he began as nafl etc.": the speech is elliptical; i.e., it is not valid to make up a nafl that he spoiled after beginning it. "Verse recited on the ground": i.e., it is not valid to perform a prostration of a verse that was recited while the reciter was on the ground, then he mounts; distinguished from if the verse was recited while on the animal, then it is valid. "Due to necessity": he said in al-Khulasah: "As for obligatory prayer on an animal with an excuse, it is permissible. He stands on it, facing the qiblah, and prays with gestures if he can stop the animal. If not, he prays whatever direction it faces, even backwards." "Mud": i.e., mud that would cover the face or soil it or damage what he spreads. Mere dampness does not permit it. He who has no animal prays standing in mud with gestures. "Refractory animal": if the rider fears the animal will bolt if he dismounts, and cannot find someone to mount him, it is permissible for him to pray on it by agreement, and he is not required to repeat after the excuse passes. "Inability to find": i.e., if the rider on the animal does not find someone to mount him if he dismounts, and he is himself unable to mount without help, then he may perform the mentioned prayers (obligatory etc.) with the details already known. "Standing": if he cannot stand or dismount, he prays sitting.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This section covers obligatory (fard) and wajib prayers on a riding animal. The general rule is that such prayers cannot be performed on a mount; they require standing on the ground, facing qiblah, with full ruku' and sujud. However, exceptions are made for genuine necessity (darurah). The text lists causes: fear of a thief or wild beast, excessive mud that would soil the face, a rebellious animal, and inability to mount/dismount due to weakness. In such cases, the rider may pray on the animal, stopping if possible, facing qiblah, and using gestures (ima). If the animal cannot be stopped, he prays facing its direction. The prayer in a litter (mahmil) is treated like prayer on the animal unless a board makes it level with the ground, in which case he can stand. The commentary further clarifies: (1) A spoiled nafl prayer cannot be made up on an animal; (2) Sajdah tilawah must be performed while on the ground if the verse was recited there; (3) Mud must be excessive (covering face); (4) For a refractory animal, permission is agreed upon; (5) One unable to stand or dismount may pray sitting.

Key Terms
الضرورة (al-darūra): Necessity that justifies performing obligatory prayer on a mount, such as fear or mud.
المحمل (al-mahmil): A litter or howdah carried by the animal, in which the rider can sit or stand.
الجموح (al-jumūḥ): A refractory or bolting animal that cannot be controlled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for performing obligatory prayer on a riding animal?
A) Fear of a thief.
B) Light dampness on the ground (naudah).
C) A refractory animal that may bolt.
D) Inability to find someone to help mount the animal.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayer on a riding animal is only valid when a genuine necessity prevents dismounting; otherwise it is invalid and must be repeated.

Ruling on Prayer in a Ship and the Invalidity of Making Up a Spoiled Nafl
Partial ruling on nafl compensation in ship prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing obligatory prayer on a moving ship and explain why a spoiled nafl prayer cannot be compensated.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayer on a moving ship is valid; a spoiled nafl cannot be made up.

This lesson clarifies a brief but important point from the Nur al-Idah: while obligatory (fard) and wajib prayers are fully valid on a moving ship, a supererogatory (nafl) prayer that is spoiled after commencement cannot be made up later. This distinction underscores that nafl prayers, unlike obligatory ones, do not require compensation when invalidated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses prayer (salat) on a ship (safinah). The general Hanafi ruling is that obligatory and wajib prayers are valid on a moving ship if one faces the qiblah and performs the actions normally.
This is assumed from the context; the full conditions are not detailed here.
2
Understand the exception: spoiled nafl
The text explicitly states that it is not valid to make up (qada) a nafl prayer that one has spoiled after beginning it. This means the reward is lost, and there is no obligation to repeat it.
Spoiled nafl includes cases where wudu breaks or the prayer is invalidated for any reason.
3
Derive the underlying principle
Nafl prayers are not wajib; they are voluntary. Once invalidated, they cannot be 'made up' because there was no original obligation to begin with. In contrast, obligatory prayers must be repeated if invalidated.
This is consistent with the Hanafi view that qada is only for fard and wajib acts.
4
Apply to practical scenarios
If a person starts a sunnah prayer on a ship and his wudu breaks, he cannot simply continue later. He must restart if he wishes, but the original sunnah is forfeited. For fard prayers, he must repeat them if invalidated.
The ship's movement does not affect this ruling.

Section on prayer in a ship: the obligatory prayer in it while it is moving, and the wajib, and what he began as nafl, etc. The speech is elliptical: i.e., it is not valid to make up a nafl that he spoiled after beginning it.

This brief passage addresses prayer in a ship (safinah). The main rule alluded to is that obligatory and wajib prayers can be performed on a moving ship, presumably standing and facing qiblah if possible. The text only provides a commentary clarification: that a spoiled nafl prayer cannot be made up later (e.g., if one begins nafl on the ship and then invalidates it, he cannot simply continue). The full details of ship prayer—such as the requirement of facing qiblah, standing, etc.—are not elaborated here. The passage likely assumes the earlier rulings for prayer on a mount apply analogously, but the ship is generally considered like land if one can stand and face qiblah.

Key Terms
السفينة (al-safīna): A ship or boat on water.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer.
قضاء (qada’): Making up a missed or invalidated prayer after its time.

Key Takeaway
A spoiled nafl prayer on a ship (or anywhere) cannot be made up; only obligatory prayers require compensation.

Obligatory Prayers on an Animal: Necessity Conditions
Ruling on obligatory prayers on an animal with necessity conditions and howdah rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which obligatory prayers on an animal are valid and apply the exceptions for necessity.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayer on an animal is invalid unless a valid necessity excuses descent.

Prayer normally requires facing the qibla and standing on firm ground. This lesson explains the exceptional case where a person may pray obligatory prayers while riding, due to a genuine necessity such as fear or incapacity. The Hanafi school outlines specific conditions that make such prayers valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its normal ruling
Obligatory prayers (fard and wajib) must normally be performed standing on the ground, facing the qibla.
This is the default rule.
2
Recognize the exceptional ruling
The text states that obligatory prayers on an animal are valid (sahih) under certain conditions. This is an exception to the norm.
The exception is based on necessity (darurah).
3
List the specific necessities that permit this
The text lists: fear of a thief, predator; muddy ground; restiveness of the animal; inability to find help to mount. Each is a valid excuse.
These are the only valid excuses; general travel is not sufficient.
4
Note the exceptions to the exception
Funeral prayer (janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajda tilawah) if the verse was recited on the ground are not permitted even with necessity.
These must be performed on the ground regardless.
5
Understand the howdah ruling
Prayer in a howdah (mahmal) on an animal follows the same ruling as on the animal itself. If a plank is placed so it rests on the ground, it is like the ground and requires standing.
The whether moving or stationary does not change the ruling.

Source Text

yصح على الدابة صلاة الفرائض والواجبات كالوتر والمنذور، وما شرع فيه نفلا والعيدين موصولة فأفسده، ولا صلاة الجنازة وسجدة تليت آيتها على الأرض إلا لضرورة كخوف لص على نفسه أو دابته أو ثيابه لو نزل، وخوف سبع، وطين المكان، وجموح الدابة، وعدم وجدان من يركبه لعجزه، والصلاة في المحمل على الدابة كالصلاة عليها، سواء كانت سائرة أو واقفة ولو جعل تحت المحمل خشبة حتى بقي قراره إلى الأرض كان بمنزلة الأرض، فتصح الفريضة فيه قائماً.
وما شرع فيه نفلا إلخ الكلام على حذف مضاف، أي ولا يصح قضاء نفل أفسده بعد ما شرع فيه. تليت آيتها أي لا يصح أداء سجدة تليت آيتها حال كون التالي على الأرض، ثم ركب الدابة، احترز به عما إذا تليت آية السجدة حال كون التالي على الدابة، فإنها تصح عليها. لضرورة قال في "الخلاصة : أما صلاة الفرض على الدابة بالعذر فجائزة، فيقف عليها أي مستقبل القبلة، ويصلي بالإيماء إن أمكنه إيقاف الدابة، فإن لم يمكنه صلى أينما توجهت ولو مستدبر القبلة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٧] وجموح الدابة: أي إذا خاف الراكب جموح الدابة إن نزل عنها، ولم يجد من يركبه عليها جاز له الصلاة عليها بالاتفاق ولا تلزمه الإعادة بزوال العذر وعدم وجدان إلخ أي إذا لم يجد الراكب على الدابة من يركبه على دابته إن نزل منها، ونفسه عاجزة عن الركوب عليها من غير إعانة أحد، فله أداء ما ذكر من صلاة الفرض والواجبات وغيرها كالصلاة في التفاصيل التي عرفتها آنفا. قائما: فإن لم يمكنه القيام، ولا النزول صلى قاعدا.

Section on the prayer of obligation and necessity on an animal and howdah. It is valid on an animal to perform obligatory prayers and necessary ones like witr and vowed, and what one began as supererogatory, and the two Eid prayers are connected, so if he spoiled it, and not the funeral prayer and a prostration of recitation if its verse was recited on the ground except for necessity, such as fear of a thief for himself or his animal or his clothes if he descends, and fear of a predator, and mud of the place, and restiveness of the animal, and not finding someone to ride it due to his incapacity. And prayer in the howdah on the animal is like prayer on it, whether it is moving or stationary. And if he places a plank under the howdah so that its base remains on the ground, it is like the ground, so the obligatory prayer in it is valid while standing. (Then commentary explaining each term.)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah states the permissibility of performing obligatory and necessary prayers on an animal for a person who has a valid excuse. The ruling covers all obligatory prayers (fara'id) and wajib prayers such as witr and nadhr, as well as supererogatory prayers that one has already commenced. However, the two Eid prayers, if connected, and funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation are not valid on an animal unless there is a dire necessity. The necessity includes fear of a thief endangering himself, his animal, or his clothes if he descends; fear of a predator; muddy ground that would soil his clothes or prevent proper prostration; the animal being uncontrollable; and inability to find someone to assist him in mounting due to his own incapacity. The prayer in a howdah (mahmal) on an animal follows the same rulings as praying directly on the animal. If a plank is placed under the howdah so it rests on the ground, it is like praying on the ground, and one must stand for the obligatory prayer. The commentary from al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah expands on these conditions, including that if one cannot stand or dismount, he may pray sitting.

Key Terms
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits performing obligatory prayer on an animal, such as fear, mud, or restiveness of the animal.
جموح (jammūḥ): Restiveness of the animal, meaning it is uncontrollable and dangerous to dismount.
محمل (mahmal): A howdah or saddle enclosure on the animal where one can sit and pray.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Prayer in a Moving Ship: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sitting Without Excuse
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on sitting without excuse in a moving ship and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Sitting without excuse in a moving ship: Abu Hanifa says valid, but Sahibayn's view prevails as al-azhar.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses the validity of obligatory prayer in a moving ship while sitting without a valid excuse. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), and then resolves it by preferring the Sahibayn's view. Understanding this dispute illustrates how the Hanafi school sometimes adopts the position of the Sahibayn over that of Abu Hanifa when it is deemed more apparent or stronger in evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is performing obligatory prayer (salat al-fard) while sitting in a moving ship (sā'irah). Note that the worshipper is able to perform ruku' and sujud normally.
The passage also distinguishes between moving ships and those tied at the shore or in deep water.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa rules that sitting without excuse in a moving ship is valid (ṣaḥīḥah), provided the worshipper performs bowing and prostration normally.
He does not consider the motion of the ship as a hindrance to standing if one is able.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that sitting is not valid (lā taṣiḥḥ) without a valid excuse (ʿudhr). A valid excuse includes dizziness (dawarān al-ra's) or inability to exit the ship.
They require standing if possible, analogous to prayer on land.
4
Identify the tarjih mechanism
The text says 'wa huwa al-aẓhar' (and that is the more apparent), indicating preference for the Sahibayn's view. This becomes the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position for fatwa.
Later Hanafi works consistently adopt the Sahibayn's view in this issue.
5
Distinguish additional scenarios
The passage also covers: a ship tied in deep water and moved strongly by wind (like a moving ship), a ship tied at the shore (like land requiring standing if part rests on ground), and the obligation to face qibla at the start and adjust as the ship turns.
These rules are consistent with the principle that prayer conditions are determined by the ability of the worshipper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصلاة في السفينة
صلاة الفرض فيها وهي جارية والواجب
قاعدا بلا عذر صحيحة عند أبي حنيفة بالركوع والسجود ، وقالا : لا تصح إلا من عذر، وهو الأظهر، والعذر كدوران الرأس، وعدم القدرة على الخروج، ولا تجوز فيها بالإيماء اتفاقا والمربوطة في لجة البحر وتحركها الريح شديدا كالسائرة، وإلا فكالواقفة على الأصح، وإن كانت مربوطة بالشط لا تجوز صلاته قاعدا بالإجماع مع قدرته على القيام فإن صلى قائما وكان شيء من السَّفينة على قرار الأرض صحت الصلاة، وإلا فلا تصح على المختار إلا إذا لم يمكنه الخروج، ويتوجه المصلي فيها إلى القبلة عند افتتاح الصلاة، وكلما استدارت عنها يتوجه إليها في خلال الصلاة حتى يتمها مستقبلاً.
قاعدا أي حال كون المصلي قاعدا بلا عذر ولو كان قادرا على الخروج منها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٨] فيها: لمن يقدر على الركوع والسجود. [مراقي الفلاح ٤۰۹ والمربوطة أي السفينة التي ربطت في لحج البحر بالمراسي والحبال، ومع ذلك تحركها الريح تحريكا شديداً كالسفينة السائرة فيما عرفته الحكم والخلاف وإلا فكالواقفة أي وإن لم تحرك السفينة المربوطة الريح تحريكا شديداً فهي كالسفينة الواقفة بالشط، وحكم الواقفة كما بينه بعده. فإن صلى قائما إلخ أي فإن صلى في السفينة المربوطة بالشط قائماً، وكان شيء من السفينة على قرار الأرض صحت الصلاة بمنزلة الصلاة على السرير مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٩] وإلا فلا تصح: أي وإن لم يستقر منها شيء على الأرض، فلا تصح الصلاة فيها مراقي الفلاح (٤٠٩] على المختار: وظاهر "الهداية" و"النهاية" جواز الصلاة في المربوطة بالشط قائماً مطلقاً، أي سواء استقرت أو لا. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٩] يتوجه إليها وإن عجز عن الاستقبال يمسك عن الصلاة مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٠]
Section on prayer in a ship. Obligatory prayer in it while it is moving, and the necessary. Sitting without excuse is valid according to Abu Hanifa with bowing and prostration, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not valid except with excuse, and that is the more apparent. The excuse is like dizziness of the head, inability to exit. And it is not permissible in it with gestures by agreement. And the (ship) tied in the deep sea and moved strongly by the wind is like the moving one, otherwise it is like the stationary on the correct view. And if it is tied at the shore, it is not permissible for him to pray sitting with consensus while able to stand. Then if he prays standing and part of the ship is on the ground, the prayer is valid; otherwise, it is not valid on the chosen view, unless he cannot exit. And the worshipper faces the qibla at the opening of the prayer, and whenever it turns away, he turns toward it during the prayer until he completes it facing (the qibla). (Further commentary on these points.)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage addresses the rules of prayer in a ship. The matn states that obligatory and necessary prayers are valid in a moving ship. The commentary explains that praying sitting without excuse is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, provided one performs ruku' and sujud normally. However, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad hold that sitting is not valid without an excuse, and their view is considered the more apparent (al-azhar) and thus the relied-upon position. An excuse may be dizziness or inability to leave the ship. All agree that prayer with gestures (īmā') is not allowed on a ship; one must perform full ruku' and sujud if possible. The rules for a ship tied in deep water and rocked by strong wind are like those of a moving ship. If the ship is tied at the shore, it is like land: one must stand if able. If part of the ship rests on the ground, prayer standing is valid; otherwise, it is not valid on the chosen view. One must face the qibla at the beginning and turn whenever the ship turns to maintain facing it throughout the prayer.

Key Terms
سائرة (sā'irah): A moving ship, as opposed to one tied or stationary.
مربوطة (marbūṭah): A ship tied to the shore or by anchors, stationary.
لجة (lujjah): Deep water; the main body of the sea.
إيماء (īmā'): Gestures, used for bowing and prostration when unable to perform them normally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In a moving ship, the relied-upon Hanafi view is that sitting without a valid excuse invalidates the obligatory prayer; one must have an excuse or stand.

Definition and Ruling of Tarawih Prayer
Definition of tarawih prayer and its sunnah status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tarawih prayer, state its ruling (sunnah mu'akkadah), and explain why it is performed in congregation.

Core Idea
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah distinguished by congregational performance and rests between rak'ahs.

This passage introduces tarawih prayer and explains why it is treated separately from other sunnah prayers. The commentary clarifies that tarawih has many detailed branches and a unique ruling: performance in congregation. Understanding the definition and classification helps appreciate the Hanafi position on this important Ramadan practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being defined
The passage defines 'tarawih' as a specific night prayer performed during Ramadan after 'isha. Note that it is not listed with other sunnah prayers because of its distinct features.
The act is the tarawih prayer, not any supererogatory prayer.
2
Note its ruling category
From the hanafi_position_box, tarawih is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). This means it is highly recommended but not obligatory.
It is not fard or wajib.
3
Understand the etymology
The term 'tarawih' is the plural of 'tarwiha', which means a rest. It is so named because the Companions used to rest after every four rak'ahs. This rest is part of the sunnah.
The rest (tarwiha) is a defining characteristic.
4
Recognize the distinctive feature
The passage states that tarawih is distinguished by being performed in congregation. This sets it apart from other sunnah and supererogatory prayers.
Congregation is the key distinguishing ruling.

Prayer on a Ship: Sitting Without Excuse - Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on prayer on a ship with intra-Hanafi dispute and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on sitting prayer on a ship and apply the preferred view (al-azhar) and conditions to determine validity.

Core Idea
Sitting without excuse in fard prayer on a ship is invalid according to the preferred Hanafi view, unless there is a valid excuse.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses the ruling on praying sitting without excuse on a ship, presenting an intra-Hanafi dispute. While Imam Abu Hanifa holds it valid, his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) consider it invalid except with an excuse. The text then explains the preferred view and clarifies conditions for standing prayer on tied versus moving ships, as well as ships at the bank versus in deep sea.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
Determine the precise legal act: praying sitting (qāʿidan) without a valid excuse while able to stand, on a ship, in a fard prayer with ruku' and sujud.
The dispute centers on whether standing is an absolute obligation or relaxable on a ship.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, sitting without excuse is valid as long as ruku' and sujud are performed. This is based on a broader view of permissibility in non-nafl contexts.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that sitting is invalid without a valid excuse (e.g., dizziness, inability to exit). They emphasize the obligation of standing in fard prayer.
This position is stated as 'wa huwa al-azhar' (the more apparent) in the text, indicating its preference.
4
Apply the Preferred View (Tarjih)
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Sahibayn view: sitting without excuse invalidates the prayer and must be repeated.
This is the position for fatwa, as indicated by 'al-azhar'.
5
Analyze Ancillary Conditions
Examine the distinctions: tied ship in deep sea (marbutah fi lujjah) vs. tied at bank (shatt); moving vs. stationary; and conditions for standing prayer (part of ship on ground).
These nuances determine when standing is required and when sitting may be excused.

Source Text

قاعدا بلا عذر صحيحة عند أبي حنيفة بالركوع والسجود ، وقالا : لا تصح إلا من عذر، وهو الأظهر، والعذر كدوران الرأس، وعدم القدرة على الخروج، ولا تجوز فيها بالإيماء اتفاقا والمربوطة في لجة البحر وتحركها الريح شديدا كالسائرة، وإلا فكالواقفة على الأصح، وإن كانت مربوطة بالشط لا تجوز صلاته قاعدا بالإجماع، مع قدرته على القيام فإن صلى قائما وكان شيء من السَّفينة على قرار الأرض صحت الصلاة، وإلا فلا تصح على المختار إلا إذا لم يمكنه الخروج، ويتوجه المصلي فيها إلى القبلة عند افتتاح الصلاة، وكلما استدارت عنها يتوجه إليها في خلال الصلاة حتى يتمها مستقبلاً. آنفاً من قاعدا أي حال كون المصلي قاعدا بلا عذر ولو كان قادرا على الخروج منها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٨] فيها: لمن يقدر على الركوع والسجود. [مراقي الفلاح ٤۰۹ والمربوطة أي السفينة التي ربطت في لجة البحر بالمراسي والحبال، ومع ذلك تحركها الريح تحريكا شديداً كالسفينة السائرة فيما عرفته الحكم والخلاف وإلا فكالواقفة أي وإن لم تحرك السفينة المربوطة الريح تحريكا شديداً فهي كالسفينة الواقفة بالشط، وحكم الواقفة كما بينه بعده. فإن صلى قائما إلخ أي فإن صلى في السفينة المربوطة بالشط قائماً، وكان شيء من السفينة على قرار الأرض صحت الصلاة بمنزلة الصلاة على السرير [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٩] وإلا فلا تصح: أي وإن لم يستقر منها شيء على الأرض، فلا تصح الصلاة فيها [مراقي الفلاح (٤٠٩] على المختار: وظاهر "الهداية" و"النهاية" جواز الصلاة في المربوطة بالشط قائماً مطلقاً، أي سواء استقرت أو لا. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٠٩] يتوجه إليها وإن عجز عن الاستقبال يمسك عن الصلاة [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٠]
Sitting without excuse is valid according to Abu Hanifa with bowing and prostration, but they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not valid except for an excuse, and that is the more apparent. The excuse is like dizziness of the head and inability to exit. And it is not permissible by gesture (ima) by agreement. And a ship tied in the deep sea, if the wind moves it violently, it is like a moving ship; otherwise it is like a stationary ship according to the soundest view. And if it is tied at the bank, his prayer sitting is not valid by consensus, while he is able to stand. If he prays standing and some part of the ship is on solid ground, the prayer is valid; otherwise it is not valid according to the chosen view, unless he cannot exit. And the worshipper faces the qibla at the beginning of the prayer, and every time the ship turns away from it, he faces it during the prayer until he completes it facing the qibla. Recently, from 'sitting' meaning the condition of the worshipper sitting without excuse even if he is able to exit from it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 408] Therein: for one who is able to bow and prostrate. [Maraqi al-Falah 409] And 'the tied ship' means the ship that is tied in the deep sea with anchors and ropes, and despite that the wind moves it violently, it is like a moving ship concerning the ruling and the difference; otherwise it is like a stationary ship. That is, if the tied ship is not moved violently by the wind, it is like a stationary ship at the bank, and the ruling of the stationary ship is as explained after it. 'If he prays standing, etc.' means if he prays standing in a ship tied at the bank, and some part of the ship is on solid ground, the prayer is valid, analogous to prayer on a bed. [Maraqi al-Falah: 409] 'Otherwise it is not valid' means if none of it is settled on the ground, prayer in it is not valid. [Maraqi al-Falah (409] 'According to the chosen view' and apparent from al-Hidayah and al-Nihayah is the permissibility of prayer standing in a ship tied at the bank absolutely, whether it is settled or not. [Maraqi al-Falah: 409] He faces it, and if unable to face the qibla he refrains from prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 410]
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on praying on a ship. The base text (matn) states that praying sitting without excuse is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, saying it is valid only with an excuse. The preferred view (al-azhar) is that of the Sahibayn. The excuse includes physical inability like dizziness. Next, the text distinguishes between a ship tied in deep sea (marbutah fi lujjah) and one tied at the bank (shatt). If the ship is tied in deep sea and the wind moves it violently, it is treated like a moving ship (sa'irah); otherwise it is like a stationary ship (waqifah) at the bank. Prayer sitting without excuse on a ship tied at the bank is invalid by consensus if the person can stand. If he stands and part of the ship is on solid ground, prayer is valid; otherwise it is invalid on the chosen view (al-mukhtar), unless he cannot leave the ship. The worshipper must face the qibla at the beginning and adjust during prayer as the ship turns. The commentary clarifies each part, explaining that 'sitting without excuse' means even if he can leave. It also notes that al-Hidayah and al-Nihayah permit standing absolutely in a ship tied at the bank.

Key Terms
قاعدا (Qāʿidan): In the context of prayer, sitting without a valid excuse, while able to stand.
المربوطة (al-Marbūṭah): A ship tied to a fixed point (e.g., at a riverbank or anchored in deep sea).
لجة (Lujjah): Deep water, the main body of the sea.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (al-azhar) in this passage, what is the ruling on praying sitting without excuse on a ship tied in deep sea (lujjah) that is moved violently by wind?
A) Valid according to Abu Hanifa, regardless of the ship's movement.
B) Invalid, because it is treated like a moving ship and sitting without excuse is invalid.
C) Valid because the ship is tied, so it is like land.
D) Invalid only if the ship is tied at the bank.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is that sitting without excuse invalidates fard prayer on a ship, and the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.

Salah — Prayer

Tarawih Prayer: Ruling, Time, and Congregation
Comprehensive rulings on tarawih prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tarawih, explain its time and number of rak'ats, and distinguish the three opinions on congregation, identifying the preferred view.

Core Idea
Tarawih is sunnah for every Muslim; its congregation is a communal sunnah, not an individual obligation.

Tarawih is a special night prayer of Ramadan, distinguished from other supererogatory prayers by its prescribed congregation and fixed number of rak'ats. This lesson unpacks its legal status, time, and the internal Hanafi discussion on whether praying in congregation is obligatory on each person or a communal responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tarawih is identified as a prayer that is sunnah for both men and women. Note that the author states 'sunnah' explicitly.
The ruling is distinguished from mustahabb; the text later reconciles a statement by al-Quduri.
2
Determine the time and structure
The time is after isha prayer; the prayer is 20 rak'ats with salam after every two rak'ats. Also note the flexibility to pray witr before or after.
The preferred view allows delaying to the last third of the night without dislike.
3
Analyze the congregation dispute
The text presents three opinions: sunnah 'ayn (individual), mustahabb at home (except for scholars), and sunnah kifayah (communal). Identify which is preferred.
The text states 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' or similar for the preferred view? Actually it says 'the correct view' is sunnah kifayah.
4
Evaluate the practical consequences
For each opinion, determine the consequence of praying alone or missing the congregation. This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.
E.g., according to sunnah 'ayn, one is sinful; according to sunnah kifayah, no sin if others attend.
5
Note the manner of performing rak'ats
Salam after every two rak'ats is recommended. Connecting four without salam is disliked but valid, and counts as two rak'ats.
This affects the validity and reward; the sound view upholds validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التراويح. فصل إلخ بيان لصلاة التراويح، وإنما لم يذكرها مع السنن المؤكدة قبل النوافل المطلقة؛ لكثرة شعبها، ولاختصاصها بحكم من بين سائر السنن والنوافل، وهو الأداء بجماعة البحر الرائق: ۱۱٦/٢] :التراويح جمع ترويحة، هي في الأصل مصدر بمعنى الاستراحة، سميت به الأربع ركعات المخصوصة؛ لاستلزامها استراحة بعدها كما هو السنة فيها. [البحر الرائق: ١١٦/٢] سنة للرجال والنساء، وصلاتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية ووقتها بعد صلاة العشاء، ويصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح وتأخيره عنها، ويستحب تأخير التراويح إلى ثلث الليل أو نصفه، ولا يكره تأخيرها إلى ما بعده على الصحيح، وهي عشرون ركعة بعشر تسلیمات سنة للرجال إلخ فإن قلت صرح الشيخ بسنية التراويح، وذهب القدوري إلى استحبابه، فكيف التوفيق؟ قلت : قال القدوري: يستحب أن يجتمع الناس وهو يدل على أن الاجتماع مستحب، وليس فيه دلالة على أن التراويح مستحبة، وإلى هذا ذهب بعضهم فقال : التراويح سنة، والاجتماع مستحب. بالجماعة: أطلق المصنف له في الجماعة، ولم يقيدها بالمسجد لما في "الكافي"، والصحيح أن للجماعة في بيته فضيلة، وللجماعة في المسجد فضيلة أخرى، فهو حاز إحدى الفضيلتين وترك الفضيلة الأخرى. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] كفاية: اعلم أن فيها ثلاثة أقوال الأول: أنه سنة على الأعيان حتى أن من صلى التراويح منفرداً فقد أساء؛ لتركه السنة وإن صليت في المساجد، و به كان يفتي ظهير الدين المرغيناني والثاني: أنه يستحب أن يصلي التراويح في بيته إلا أن يكون فقيهاً عظيماً يقتدى به، فيكون في حضوره ترغيب لغيره، وفي امتناعه تقليل الجماعة، والثالث: أن إقامتها بالجماعة سنة على الكفاية، حتى لو ترك أهل المسجد كلهم الجماعة فقد أساؤوا وأثموا، وإن أقيمت التراويح بالجماعة في المسجد، وتخلف عنها أفراد الناس، وصلى في بيته لم يكن مسيئاً. [البحر الرائق ملخصا: ١١٩/٢] بعد صلاة العشاء: اعلم أن في وقتها ثلاثة أقوال الأول: أن الليل كله وقت لها قبل العشاء وبعده، وقبل الوتر وبعده الثاني: أن وقتها ما بين العشاء إلى الوتر الثالث ما اختاره المصنف. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما لو صلاها قبل العشاء فعلى القول الأول هي صلاة التراويح، وعلى الأخيرين ،لا، وفيما إذا صلاها بعد الوتر فعلى الثاني لا، وعلى الثالث نعم هي صلاة التراويح، وتظهر فيما إذا فاتته ترويحة أو ترويحتان، ولو اشتغل بها يفوته الوتر بالجماعة، فعلى الأول يشتغل بالوتر، ثم يصلي ما فاته من التراويح وعلى الثاني يشتغل بالترويحة الفائتة، وينبغي أن يكون الثالث كالثاني. [البحر الرائق: ١١٨/٢] على الصحيح وقال بعضهم: يكره؛ لأنها تبع للعشاء، فصارت كسنة العشاء. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٣] عشرون ركعة: بإجماع الصحابة .. مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٤] الحكمة في تقديرها بهذا العدد مساواة المكمل، وهي السنن للمكمل وهي الفرائض الاعتقادية والعملية [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٤] بعشر تسليمات: يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين، فإذا وصلها وجلس على كل شفع، فالأصح أنه إن تعمد كره وصحت وأجزأته عن كلها، وإذا لم يجلس إلا في آخر أربع نابت عن تسليمة، فتكون بمنزلة ركعتين في الصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٤]
Chapter on Tarawih. The chapter, etc., is an explanation of the tarawih prayer. He did not mention it with the confirmed sunnahs before the absolute supererogatory prayers because of the multiplicity of its branches and because it is distinguished from other sunnahs and nawafil by a ruling, namely performing it in congregation. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:116] Tarawih is the plural of tarwiha, originally a verbal noun meaning rest; it is named for the four specific rak'ats because they necessitate a rest after them as is sunnah. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:116] It is sunnah for men and women, and praying it in congregation is sunnah kifayah. Its time is after the isha prayer. It is permissible to offer witr before tarawih or delay it. It is recommended to delay tarawih until the last third of the night or half, and it is not disliked to delay it beyond that according to the correct view. It is twenty rak'ats with ten salams. 'Sunnah for men, etc.' If you say: The author explicitly stated that tarawih is sunnah, but al-Quduri said it is mustahabb (recommended), so how to reconcile? I say: al-Quduri said: It is mustahabb for people to gather; this indicates that the gathering is mustahabb, not that tarawih itself is mustahabb. Some held this view: tarawih is sunnah, the gathering is mustahabb. 'In congregation': The author made it absolute regarding congregation and did not restrict it to the mosque because of what is in al-Kafi. The correct view is that congregation in one's home has virtue, and congregation in the mosque has another virtue; thus one attains one virtue and leaves the other. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:120] 'Kifayah': Know that there are three opinions: First, it is sunnah 'ayn (individual obligation) such that one who prays tarawih alone has acted badly for leaving the sunnah, even if it is performed in mosques; this was the fatwa of Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. Second, it is mustahabb to pray tarawih at home unless one is a great scholar to be followed, so his presence encourages others and his absence reduces the congregation. Third, performing it in congregation is sunnah kifayah, such that if all the people of a mosque abandon the congregation they have acted badly and sinned, but if tarawih is performed in congregation in the mosque and individuals stay away and pray at home, they are not blameworthy. [Summarized from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:119] 'After isha prayer': Know that regarding its time there are three opinions: First, the entire night is its time, before isha and after it, before witr and after it. Second, its time is between isha and witr. Third, what the author chose. The practical consequence appears if one prays it before isha: according to the first opinion it is tarawih, according to the latter two it is not. If one prays it after witr: according to the second it is not, according to the third it is tarawih. Also appears if one misses one or two tarwihas and engaging in them would cause him to miss witr in congregation: according to the first he engages in witr first, then prays what he missed of tarawih; according to the second he engages in the missed tarwiha; the third should be like the second. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:118] 'According to the correct view': Some said it is disliked because tarawih is appended to isha, thus becomes like its sunnah. [Maraqi al-Falah: 413] 'Twenty rak'ats': By consensus of the Companions. [Maraqi al-Falah: 414] The wisdom in estimating this number is to equalize the complement (the sunnah) with the complemented (the beliefs and practical obligations). [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 414] 'With ten salams': He gives salam at the end of every two rak'ats. If he connects them and sits after every pair, the soundest view is that if he does it deliberately it is disliked but valid and suffices for all. If he does not sit except at the end of four, it substitutes for one salam, and it is like two rak'ats according to the sound view. [Maraqi al-Falah: 414]
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of tarawih prayer. It begins by defining tarawih linguistically (plural of tarwiha meaning rest) and technically (the specific night prayers of Ramadan). The text states that tarawih is sunnah for both men and women, and performing it in congregation is sunnah kifayah (a communal sunnah). The time is after isha prayer until dawn. It is permissible to pray witr before or after tarawih, but it is better to delay tarawih to the last third or half of the night; delaying beyond that is not disliked on the correct view. The number of rak'ats is twenty, based on the consensus of the Companions, and it is prayed in units of two with a salam after each pair. The commentary then addresses several points: (1) reconciling the statement that tarawih is sunnah with al-Quduri's view that it is mustahabb – the answer is that al-Quduri meant the congregation is mustahabb, not the prayer itself. (2) The ruling on congregation: it is sunnah kifayah; there are three opinions within the Hanafi school: sunnah 'ayn (individual), mustahabb at home (except for scholars), and sunnah kifayah. The preferred view is the third. (3) The time: three opinions on whether it can be prayed before isha or after witr; the practical consequences are explained. (4) The number of rak'ats is confirmed by ijma of the Companions, and the wisdom is to balance sunnah with obligatory acts. (5) The manner of salam: salam after every two rak'ats; if one connects four with only one salam at the end, it is disliked but valid, and the four count as two rak'ats in the sound view.

Key Terms
سنة كفاية (Sunnah Kifāyah): A sunnah that is obligatory on the community as a whole; if some fulfill it, the rest are absolved, but if all abandon it, all are sinful.
تراويح (Tarāwīḥ): Plural of tarwiha, meaning rest; the night prayers of Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ats with salams every 2 rak'ats.
تسليمة (Taslīmah): The salutation ending the prayer; here it refers to each pair of rak'ats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is the ruling on performing tarawih in congregation?
A) Fard 'ayn on every individual.
B) Mustahabb but not sunnah.
C) Sunnah kifayah – a communal sunnah.
D) Makruh because it should be done at home.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a sunnah prayer of 20 rak'ats in Ramadan; its congregation is a sunnah kifayah, not an individual obligation.

The Ruling of Tarawih Prayer: Sunnah, Congregation, Time, and Number
Defines Tarawih's ruling, congregation, time, and number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih prayer, identify its proof (Ijma of the Companions), and apply the mufta bihi positions on congregation and time.

Core Idea
Tarawih is 20 rak'at Sunnah Mu'akkadah with congregation Sunnah Kifayah, proven by Ijma.

Tarawih is the special night prayer of Ramadan. In this passage, Imam al-Shurunbulali lays out the core Hanafi rulings: its status as a highly recommended Sunnah, the communal nature of its congregation, the time window, and the definitive number of 20 rak'at. He also reconciles differing opinions within the school and provides practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hukm of Tarawih
The passage begins by stating that Tarawih is Sunnah for men and women. Note that al-Quduri called it mustahabb; the author reconciles by saying the prayer itself is Sunnah but the congregation is mustahabb.
The hukm level is Sunnah Mu'akkadah.
2
Analyze the Congregational Ruling
The congregation is described as Sunnah Kifayah. Three intra-Hanafi views are presented: individual Sunnah, recommended at home for scholars, and the mufta bihi of Sunnah Kifayah.
Understand the practical difference: if congregation is established, praying alone is not blameworthy.
3
Determine the Time of Tarawih
The mufta bihi is after Isha until Fajr, with best in last third or half. Three views on the exact window; the author chooses after Isha. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: praying before Isha counts only on one view.
Delaying beyond half is not disliked per the correct position.
4
Confirm the Number of Rak'at and Proof
The number is 20 rak'at with ten taslims, proven by Ijma of the Companions. The wisdom is to match the number of obligatory acts.
This is a qat'i proof; other numbers are rejected.
5
Apply the Practical Consequences
The passage gives scenarios: missing Tarawih and Witr, preference for grouping. Use the mufta bihi to resolve.
If Witr in congregation is at stake, pray Witr first per the first view; the third view is like the second.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
صلاة التراويح
سنة للرجال والنساء، وصلاتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية ووقتها بعد صلاة العشاء، ويصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح وتأخيره عنها، ويستحب تأخير التراويح إلى ثلث الليل أو نصفه، ولا يكره تأخيرها إلى ما بعده على الصحيح، وهي عشرون ركعة بعشر تسلیمات
سنة للرجال إلخ فإن قلت صرح الشيخ بسنية التراويح، وذهب القدوري إلى استحبابه، فكيف التوفيق؟ قلت : قال القدوري: يستحب أن يجتمع الناس وهو يدل على أن الاجتماع مستحب، وليس فيه دلالة على أن التراويح مستحبة، وإلى هذا ذهب بعضهم فقال : التراويح سنة، والاجتماع مستحب. بالجماعة: أطلق المصنف له في الجماعة، ولم يقيدها بالمسجد لما في "الكافي"، والصحيح أن للجماعة في بيته فضيلة، وللجماعة في المسجد فضيلة أخرى، فهو حاز إحدى الفضيلتين وترك الفضيلة الأخرى. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] كفاية: اعلم أن فيها ثلاثة أقوال الأول: أنه سنة على الأعيان حتى أن من صلى التراويح منفرداً فقد أساء؛ لتركه السنة وإن صليت في المساجد، و به كان يفتي ظهير الدين المرغيناني والثاني: أنه يستحب أن يصلي التراويح في بيته إلا أن يكون فقيهاً عظيماً يقتدى به، فيكون في حضوره ترغيب لغيره، وفي امتناعه تقليل الجماعة، والثالث: أن إقامتها بالجماعة سنة على الكفاية، حتى لو ترك أهل المسجد كلهم الجماعة فقد أساؤوا وأثموا، وإن أقيمت التراويح بالجماعة في المسجد، وتخلف عنها أفراد الناس، وصلى في بيته لم يكن مسيئاً. [البحر الرائق ملخصا: ١١٩/٢] بعد صلاة العشاء: اعلم أن في وقتها ثلاثة أقوال الأول: أن الليل كله وقت لها قبل العشاء وبعده، وقبل الوتر وبعده الثاني: أن وقتها ما بين العشاء إلى الوتر الثالث ما اختاره المصنف. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما لو صلاها قبل العشاء فعلى القول الأول هي صلاة التراويح، وعلى الأخيرين ،لا، وفيما إذا صلاها بعد الوتر فعلى الثاني لا، وعلى الثالث نعم هي صلاة التراويح، وتظهر فيما إذا فاتته ترويحة أو ترويحتان، ولو اشتغل بها يفوته الوتر بالجماعة، فعلى الأول يشتغل بالوتر، ثم يصلي ما فاته من التراويح وعلى الثاني يشتغل بالترويحة الفائتة، وينبغي أن يكون الثالث كالثاني. [البحر الرائق: ١١٨/٢] على الصحيح وقال بعضهم: يكره؛ لأنها تبع للعشاء، فصارت كسنة العشاء. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٣] عشرون ركعة: بإجماع الصحابة .. مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٤] الحكمة في تقديرها بهذا العدد مساواة المكمل، وهي السنن للمكمل وهي الفرائض الاعتقادية والعملية [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٤] بعشر تسليمات: يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين، فإذا وصلها وجلس على كل شفع، فالأصح أنه إن تعمد كره وصحت وأجزأته عن كلها، وإذا لم يجلس إلا في آخر أربع نابت عن تسليمة، فتكون بمنزلة ركعتين في الصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٤]
Book of Prayer. Tarawih Prayer: It is Sunnah for men and women. Praying it in congregation is Sunnah Kifayah. Its time is after Isha prayer. It is permissible to perform Witr before Tarawih and to delay it after it. It is recommended to delay Tarawih to the last third of the night or its midpoint. It is not disliked to delay it beyond that according to the correct position. It is twenty rak'at with ten taslims. 'Sunnah for men etc.': If you say the Shaykh explicitly stated it is Sunnah, while al-Quduri held it is recommended, how to reconcile? I say: al-Quduri said it is recommended for people to gather, which indicates the gathering is recommended, not that Tarawih itself is recommended. Some held: Tarawih is Sunnah, gathering is recommended. 'In congregation': The author did not restrict it to the mosque according to al-Kafi. The correct view is that congregation at home has one virtue and congregation in the mosque has another virtue; one attains one virtue and leaves the other. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/120] 'Kifayah': Know that there are three views: First: it is Sunnah upon individuals, so one who prays alone is blameworthy for abandoning Sunnah even if prayed in mosques. This was the fatwa of Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. Second: it is recommended to pray Tarawih at home unless one is a great scholar followed by others, for his presence encourages others and his absence reduces the congregation. Third: performing it in congregation is Sunnah Kifayah, so if all the people of a mosque abandon the congregation they are blameworthy and sinful, but if the congregation is held and some individuals stay away and pray at home they are not blameworthy. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/119 summarised] 'After Isha prayer': Know that there are three views on its time: First: the whole night is its time, before and after Isha, before and after Witr. Second: its time is between Isha and Witr. Third: what the author chose. The practical consequence appears if one prays it before Isha: according to the first it is valid Tarawih, according to the others no. If after Witr: according to the second no, according to the third yes. It also appears if one misses one or two Tarwihas and by engaging in them one misses Witr in congregation: according to the first, one performs Witr then prays the missed Tarawih; according to the second, one engages in the missed Tarwiha. The third should be like the second. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/118] 'According to the correct position': Some said it is disliked because it follows Isha and thus becomes like its Sunnah. [Maraqi al-Falah 413] 'Twenty rak'at': by consensus of the Companions. [Maraqi al-Falah 414] The wisdom in this number is to equal the complement (the completed) i.e. the Sunnah with the complement (the completed) which are the creedal and practical obligatory acts. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 414] 'With ten taslims': One gives salutation after every two rak'at. If one prays them connected and sits after every pair, the correct view is that if he does so intentionally it is disliked but valid and suffices for all. If he does not sit except in the last four, it substitutes for one taslim and is considered like two rak'at according to the correct view. [Maraqi al-Falah 414]
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that defines the basic ruling of Tarawih prayer, its congregation status, time, and number of rak'at. The author begins by stating that Tarawih is Sunnah for both men and women. A scholar notes that al-Quduri called it 'mustahabb' (recommended), but the text reconciles this by clarifying that the gathering is mustahabb, not the prayer itself—the prayer remains Sunnah. The congregation is 'Sunnah Kifayah', meaning if no one in a locality performs it in congregation, all are blameworthy, but if some do, the rest are absolved. Three intra-Hanafi views on congregating are presented: one considers it Sunnah on each individual, another prefers home prayer except for leading scholars, and the third is the relied-upon view of Sunnah Kifayah. The time for Tarawih is after Isha until Fajr, with the best being the last third or half of the night. Delaying beyond that is not disliked according to the correct opinion. Three views on the exact time window are given: whole night, between Isha and Witr, or after Isha as chosen by the author; practical consequences of each are illustrated. The number of rak'at is established as twenty, based on Consensus of the Companions (Ijma as-Sahabah), which is a strong proof. The wisdom is to equal the total number of obligatory acts in belief and practice. Each two rak'at are separated by a taslim (salutation). If one intentionally connects all without sitting between pairs, it is disliked but valid.

Key Terms
تراويح (Tarawih): The sunnah night prayers performed during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'at with ten taslims.
سنة كفاية (Sunnah Kifayah): A communal Sunnah: if some people perform it in congregation, the obligation is lifted from the rest. If all abandon it, they are sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many rak'at does Tarawih prayer consist of, and what is the proof for this number?
A) 8 rak'at based on the practice of the Prophet
B) 20 rak'at based on consensus of the Companions
C) 36 rak'at based on the practice of Umar
D) 12 rak'at based on analogy with the daily Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is 20 rak'at of highly recommended Sunnah, prayed after Isha, with congregation as Sunnah Kifayah, proven by Ijma of the Sahaba.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Additional Practices in Tarawih: Sitting, Recitation, and Qada
Lists sunan of Tarawih: sitting between sets, Qur'an recitation, and ruling on qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (sunan) specific to Tarawih prayer according to the Hanafi school, and explain rulings on sitting, recitation length, and qada.

Core Idea
Tarawih is rooted in rest; sitting after every four rak'at fulfills its meaning, and missed Tarawih is never made up.

This lesson explores the unique sunan of Tarawih, including sitting between sets, recitation length, and the ruling on making up missed prayers. Unlike obligatory prayers, Tarawih is time-bound and cannot be qada. The passage also emphasizes adapting recitation to avoid boredom while preserving essential sunan like salawat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each practice
List the recommended acts (sitting, khatm, recitation length, salawat, tasbih) and the ruling for qada. Determine whether each is mustahabb, sunnah, or not permitted.
Sitting after every four rak'at is mustahabb; completing Qur'an is sunnah; recitation adaptation is permissible; qada is not valid.
2
Locate the evidence
The main evidence for sitting is the practice of the Sahabah and the linguistic derivation of Tarawih from rest. For other points, the text cites later Hanafi works.
Hadith from al-Bayhaqi and the practice of Makkah/Madinah.
3
Understand the principle behind qada
Tarawih is time-specific; its Sunnah is linked to the month of Ramadan and the congregation. Missing it does not carry a makeup obligation.
This distinguishes it from fard prayers.
4
Resolve the ikhtilaf on recitation length
Two views: reciting ten verses per rak'ah (to complete Qur'an once) vs. three short verses (to avoid boredom). The mufta bihi is to adapt based on congregation.
The later fatwa favors shorter recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب الجلوس بعد كل أربع بقدرها، وكذا بين الترويحة الخامسة والوتر، وسن ختم القرآن فيها مرة في الشهر على الصحيح، وإن ملّ به القوم قرأ بقدر ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفيرهم في المختار ولا يترك الصلاة على النبي الله في كل تشهد منها ولو ملّ القوم على المختار ولا يترك الثناء وتسبيح الركوع والسجود، ولا يأتي بالدعاء إن مل القوم، ولا تقضى التراويح بفواتها منفردا ولا بجماعة.
أحداً
أي الطويل
من التنفل ما شاء، وإنما
الجلوس إلخ قيل: ينبغي أن يقول: والمستحب الانتظار بين الترويحتين؛ لأنه استدل بعادة أهل الحرمين وأهل المدينة، كانوا يصلون بدل ذلك أربع ركعات فرادى، وأهل مكة يطوفون بينهما أسبوعاً، ويصلون ركعتي الطواف، إلا أنه روى البيهقي بإسناد صحيح أنهم كانوا يقومون على عهد عمر طويله، ونحن لا نمنع الكلام في القدر المستحب بجماعة، وأهل كل بلدة بالخيار يسبحون أو يهللون أو ينتظرون سكوتاً أو يصلون أربعاً فرادى، وإنما استحب الانتظار؛ لأن التراويح مأخوذ من الراحة، فيفعل ذلك تحقيقاً لمعنى الاسم، وكذا هو متوارث. فتح القدير ٤٠٨/١] وكذا إلخ أي وكذا يستحب الجلوس بقدرها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٤] مرة الخ: اعلم أن الجمهور على أن السنة الختم ،مرة، فلا يترك لكسل القوم، ويختم في الليلة السابع والعشرين؛ لكثرة الأخبار أنها ليلة القدر ومرتين فضيلة وفي كل عشر مرة أفضل [البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] بقدر ما لا يؤدي إلخ وفي "مختارات النوازل" أنه يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن السنة فيها الختم؛ لأن جميع عدد الركعات في جميع الشهر ست مائة ركعة، وجميع آيات القرآن ستة آلاف. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] في المختار وفي "المجتبى" : والمتأخرون كانوا يفتون في زماننا بثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة حتى لا يمل القوم، ولا يلزم تعطيلها وهذا حسن؛ فإن الحسن روى عن أبي حنيفة : أنه إن قرأ في المكتوبة بعد الفاتحة ثلاث آيات فقد أحسن ولم يسئ، هذا في المكتوبة فما ظنك غيرها. البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] ولا يترك الصلاة إلخ لأن الصلاة على النبي سنة مؤكدة عندنا، وفرض على قول بعض المجتهدين، بدونها، ويحذر من الهدرمة وترك الترتيل وترك تعديل الأركان وغيرهما كما يفعله من لا خشية له. مراقي الفلاح: (٤١٥] ولا يترك إلخ إماما كان أو مقتديا أو منفرداً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٦]
فلا
يصح
It is recommended to sit after every four rak'at for the duration of them, and similarly between the fifth Tarwiha and Witr. It is Sunnah to complete the Qur'an in it once a month according to the correct view. If the congregation becomes bored, he should recite as much as does not cause aversion in the chosen view. He should not leave sending salutations on the Prophet in every Tashahhud of it, even if the congregation becomes bored according to the chosen view. He should not leave the praise and the glorifications of bowing and prostrating. He should not perform supplication if the congregation becomes bored. Missed Tarawih is not made up individually or in congregation. ... 'Sitting etc.': It is said that he should say 'recommended to wait between two Tarwihas' because he deduces from the practice of the people of the Two Harams and the people of Madinah; they used to pray four rak'at individually instead, and the people of Makkah used to perform Tawaf between them and pray two rak'at of Tawaf. However, al-Bayhaqi narrated with a sound chain that they used to stand long during the time of Umar. We do not forbid speech during the recommended amount in congregation, and the people of each town have the choice: they may glorify, proclaim tahlil, wait silently, or pray four individually. Waiting is recommended because Tarawih is derived from rest, so doing that actualizes the meaning of the name, and so it is inherited. [Fath al-Qadir 1/408] 'Similarly etc.': meaning similarly it is recommended to sit for its duration. [Maraqi al-Falah 414] 'Once etc.': Know that the majority hold that the Sunnah is to complete it once; so it should not be abandoned due to the laziness of the people. He completes it on the 27th night because many reports indicate it is Laylat al-Qadr. Completing twice is virtuous, and completing in every ten days is better. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/120] 'As much as does not cause aversion etc.': In Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: He recites ten verses in every rak'ah, which is correct because the Sunnah is to complete it; all the rak'at in the whole month are six hundred, and all the verses of the Qur'an are six thousand. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/120] 'In the chosen view': In al-Mujtaba: The later scholars gave fatwa in our time to recite three short verses or one long verse so that the congregation does not become bored, and it is not necessary to abandon it. This is good, for al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if he recites three verses after the Fatiha in the obligatory prayer, he has done well and not wrong. This is in the obligatory prayer, so what do you think of other prayers? [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/120] 'Should not leave salutations etc.': Because sending salutations on the Prophet is a confirmed Sunnah in our school, and it is obligatory according to some jurists. He should beware of mumbling, leaving proper recitation, leaving proper posture of the pillars, and other things done by those without fear. [Maraqi al-Falah 415] 'Should not leave etc.': Whether one is an imam, follower, or praying alone. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 416] So it is not valid [to leave it].
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage details the recommended acts (sunan) and rulings specific to the performance of Tarawih prayer. The author begins by stating that it is recommended (mustahabb) to sit after every four rak'at for a period equal to the prayer, and similarly between the fifth Tarwiha and Witr. The commentary explains that the wisdom behind waiting (انتظار) is derived from the root of Tarawih meaning rest. It cites the practice of the people of Makkah and Madinah, and a hadith from al-Bayhaqi. It is Sunnah to complete the entire Qur'an at least once during the month of Ramadan in Tarawih. If the congregation becomes bored, the imam should shorten his recitation to maintain their engagement. The relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that he should not abandon sending salawat upon the Prophet in every tashahhud, nor the praise (thana) and the tasbih of ruku and sujud, but he may omit the supplication (dua) if the congregation is bored. Importantly, Tarawih is not made up (qada) if missed, whether individually or in congregation; it is a time-specific prayer. The commentary cautions against improper recitation and postures.

Key Terms
ترويحة (Tarwiha): A unit of two rak'at in Tarawih, after which a taslim is performed. Five Tarwihas make ten rak'at.
ختم القرآن (Khatm al-Qur'an): The act of reciting the entire Qur'an from beginning to end during Tarawih prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It must be made up individually before the next Fajr
B) It must be made up in congregation the next night
C) It is not made up at all
D) It can be made up anytime during Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Missed Tarawih is not made up; it is time-specific. Other sunan include sitting, completing Qur'an once, adapting recitation, and preserving salawat.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Rulings on Salat al-Tarawih and Its Recommended Acts
Rulings with proof on Tarawih performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah mu'akkadah ruling of Tarawih, apply the Hanafi rule on adjusting recitation to avoid boredom, and explain why missed Tarawih is not made up.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah; recitation may be shortened to keep the congregation engaged, and it is never made up if missed.

Tarawih prayer occupies a special place in Ramadan nights. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings on its performance, the recommended acts, and the critical principle that whatever is recited must not drive the congregation away. We will also explore the internal Hanafi difference on recitation length and why qada' is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the sunnah acts mentioned in the matn: sitting after every four rak'ahs, completing the Quran once, reciting salawat, tasbih, thana', and adjusting recitation to avoid boring the congregation.
These acts enhance the prayer but are not obligatory.
2
Locate the proof
The commentary cites the hadith of Bayhaqi with a sound chain about the practice during Umar's reign where they stood for long prayers. This is the basis for the sunnah of Tarawih.
The proof is a hadith (zanni al-thubut), thus the ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
3
Analyse the recitation adjustment
The text presents two positions: the early view of ten ayat per rak'ah to complete the Quran, and the later fatwa of three short ayat or one long ayah to prevent boredom. The later is mufta bihi.
The adjustment is based on Abu Hanifa's statement about fard prayer: reciting three ayat after Fatiha is sufficient.
4
Examine the obligation of salawat and tasbih
The matn explicitly says not to omit sending blessings on the Prophet and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud, even if the congregation becomes bored. The commentary emphasises they are sunnah mu'akkadah.
These are considered wajib in regular prayer but here they are sunnah; omitting them is disliked (makruh).
5
State the rule on qada'
The passage concludes: 'ولا تقضى التراويح بفواتها منفردا ولا بجماعة' – Tarawih is not made up after its time passes, whether individually or in congregation.
Because it is a sunnah tied to a specific time (Ramadan nights), it cannot be performed after the month ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلاة التراويح
ويستحب الجلوس بعد كل أربع بقدرها، وكذا بين الترويحة الخامسة والوتر، وسن
ختم القرآن فيها مرة في الشهر على الصحيح، وإن ملّ به القوم قرأ بقدر ما لا يؤدي
إلى تنفيرهم في المختار ولا يترك الصلاة على النبي الله في كل تشهد منها ولو ملّ القوم على المختار ولا يترك الثناء وتسبيح الركوع والسجود، ولا يأتي بالدعاء إن مل القوم، ولا تقضى التراويح بفواتها منفردا ولا بجماعة.
أحداً
أي الطويل
من التنفل ما شاء، وإنما
الجلوس إلخ قيل: ينبغي أن يقول: والمستحب الانتظار بين الترويحتين؛ لأنه استدل بعادة أهل الحرمين وأهل المدينة، كانوا يصلون بدل ذلك أربع ركعات فرادى، وأهل مكة يطوفون بينهما أسبوعاً، ويصلون ركعتي الطواف، إلا أنه روى البيهقي بإسناد صحيح أنهم كانوا يقومون على عهد عمر طويله، ونحن لا نمنع الكلام في القدر المستحب بجماعة، وأهل كل بلدة بالخيار يسبحون أو يهللون أو ينتظرون سكوتاً أو يصلون أربعاً فرادى، وإنما استحب الانتظار؛ لأن التراويح مأخوذ من الراحة، فيفعل ذلك تحقيقاً لمعنى الاسم، وكذا هو متوارث. فتح القدير ٤٠٨/١] وكذا إلخ أي وكذا يستحب الجلوس بقدرها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٤] مرة الخ: اعلم أن الجمهور على أن السنة الختم ،مرة، فلا يترك لكسل القوم، ويختم في الليلة السابع والعشرين؛ لكثرة الأخبار أنها ليلة القدر ومرتين فضيلة وفي كل عشر مرة أفضل [البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢]
بقدر ما لا يؤدي إلخ وفي "مختارات النوازل" أنه يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن السنة فيها الختم؛ لأن جميع عدد الركعات في جميع الشهر ست مائة ركعة، وجميع آيات القرآن ستة آلاف. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] في المختار وفي "المجتبى" : والمتأخرون كانوا يفتون في زماننا بثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة حتى لا يمل القوم، ولا يلزم تعطيلها وهذا حسن؛ فإن الحسن روى عن أبي حنيفة : أنه إن قرأ في المكتوبة بعد الفاتحة ثلاث آيات فقد أحسن ولم يسئ، هذا في المكتوبة فما ظنك غيرها. البحر الرائق: ١٢٠/٢] ولا يترك الصلاة إلخ لأن الصلاة على النبي سنة مؤكدة عندنا، وفرض على قول بعض المجتهدين، بدونها، ويحذر من الهدرمة وترك الترتيل وترك تعديل الأركان وغيرهما كما يفعله من لا خشية له. مراقي الفلاح: (٤١٥] ولا يترك إلخ إماما كان أو مقتديا أو منفرداً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٦]
فلا
يصح
The Book of Prayer: 136. Salat al-Tarawih. It is recommended to sit after every four [rak'ahs] for an amount equal to them, and likewise between the fifth tarwiha and witr. It is sunnah to complete the Quran in it once per month according to the correct view. And if the congregation becomes bored with him, he recites to an extent that does not lead to their aversion according to the chosen view. He should not omit sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) in every tashahhud of it, even if the congregation becomes bored according to the chosen view. And he should not omit the praise (thana') and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud. And he should not supplicate if the congregation becomes bored. And tarawih is not made up after its time passes, whether individually or in congregation. ... (commentary follows) ... The hadith of Bayhaqi with a sound chain that they used to stand for a long time in the era of Umar. ... And it is said that it is recommended to wait between tarwihas because tarawih is derived from rest. ... And know that the majority [of scholars] hold that the sunnah is to complete [the Quran] once, so it is not abandoned due to laziness of the congregation. ... And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that if one recites three ayat after the Fatiha in the fard prayer, he has done well and not wronged. ... So it is not valid.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage from the matn and its commentary discusses the rulings related to Salat al-Tarawih. It begins by stating the recommended actions: sitting after every four rak'ahs, the sunnah of completing the Quran once per month, and adjusting recitation length based on the congregation's engagement. It then addresses the obligation of sending salawat and the prohibition of omitting the tasbih and thana'. The commentary then expands on the recommendation of waiting between tarwihas, citing the practice of the people of the Two Holy Sanctuaries and a hadith from Bayhaqi. It explains that the term 'tarawih' is derived from 'rest' (raha), so waiting embodies the meaning of the name. The commentary also discusses the amount of recitation, noting that the correct view is ten ayat per rak'ah to enable completion of the Quran over the month, but later fatwas allowed short verses to avoid boredom, as supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa about reciting three ayat in fard. The passage concludes that tarawih is not to be made up if missed, whether individually or in congregation.

Key Terms
تراويح (tarawih): The special night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs, derived from 'raha' (rest).
ختم القرآن (khatm al-Qur'an): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran in the tarawih prayer over the month of Ramadan.
تسبيح الركوع والسجود (tasbih al-ruku' wa al-sujud): The glorification of Allah recited in the bowing and prostration postures, e.g., 'Subhana rabbiyal-'azim' and 'Subhana rabbiyal-a'la'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on making up missed tarawih prayers?
A) They must be made up individually.
B) They must be made up in congregation.
C) They are not made up at all.
D) They are made up in the daytime.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah with flexibility in recitation to suit the congregation, and it is not to be made up if missed.

Salah — Prayer

Prayer in the Ka'bah and Following the Imam
Rulings on prayer in/on Ka'bah and following an imam inside or outside

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah, and identify the conditions for validly following an imam who is inside the Ka'bah while you are outside.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid for fard and nafl; on top is valid but makruh; following an imam inside requires open door and proper positioning.

The Ka'bah is the qibla for all Muslims, but what about praying inside it? The Hanafi school provides clear rulings on the validity of prayer both inside and on top of the Ka'bah, as well as the intricate rules for following an imam when the imam is inside the Ka'bah and the follower is outside. This lesson unpacks these rulings from the matn and its commentary, explaining the conditions and the reasoning behind the makruh classification for praying on the roof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Prayer inside the Ka'bah (fard and nafl) and on top. State the hukm: sahih (valid) for inside, sahih but makruh tanzih for top.
Makruh here is tanzihi (slight dislike) due to showing superiority over the Ka'bah.
2
Understand the reason for makruh
The text says 'li isa'at al-adab' – poor manners of showing superiority over the Ka'bah. This is a tanzihi dislike, not prohibitive.
The commentary emphasizes it is makruh tanzih.
3
Analyze conditions for following an imam inside
When imam is inside Ka'bah and follower outside, the door must be open (or the follower can hear the takbir). Also, the follower must not be closer to the Ka'bah than the imam in the imam's direction.
The commentary clarifies that hearing the takbir suffices even if door is closed.
4
Examine the seven possible relative positions
Inside or on top, if the follower places his back to the imam's face, the followership is invalid. In seven other relative positions (back to imam's other side, side to face, etc.) it is valid, but facing the imam directly without a barrier is makruh.
The commentary lists seven valid scenarios and one invalid (back to face).
5
Apply the rules to multiple followers around the Ka'bah
If people form a circle around the Ka'bah with the imam outside, all are valid except the one who is in the imam's direction and closer to the Ka'bah than the imam.
The text gives an example with distances from the Ka'bah.

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٧] ومن جعل إلخ: أي ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه، أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه متوجها إلى غير جهته أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه صح اقتداؤه في هذه الصور السبع، إلا أنه يكره إذا قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٧] وإن جعل ظهره إلخ تصريح بما علم التزاما من السابق لإيضاح الحكم، وذلك لتقدمه على إمامه.
