صلاته
Chapter: Prayer in the Ka'bah. The prayer of the person praying is valid (sahih) for fard and nafl inside it, likewise on top of it even if he does not take a sutra, but it is makruh; due to poor manners in showing superiority over it. And whoever places his back to other than the face of his imam inside it or on top of it, it is valid. And if he places his back to the face of his imam, it is not valid. And following [an imam] from outside while the imam is inside and the door is open is valid. And if they gather around it and the imam is outside, it is valid except for the one who is closer to it [the Ka'bah] than the imam in his direction. (Commentary follows explaining the seven cases of facing directions inside, and the condition of the door being open, and the exception for those closer.)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage from the matn and its commentary deals with the rulings of praying inside the Ka'bah and following an imam. The matn states that it is valid to pray fard or nafl inside the Ka'bah and on its roof, although praying on the roof is makruh due to lack of respect. It then discusses the validity of following an imam inside when the follower is outside: it is valid if the door is open. If the follower is closer to the Ka'bah than the imam in the direction of the imam, his prayer is not valid. The commentary elaborates on the seven possible relative positions inside the Ka'bah (facing front, back, side, etc.) and clarifies that it is valid in seven of them except when facing the imam's face directly without a barrier, which is makruh. It also explains that the door is considered open by custom; even if closed but the follower hears the takbir, it is still valid. Finally, it gives an example of people around the Ka'bah: all are valid except one who is in the imam's direction and closer to the Ka'bah than the imam.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred house of Allah in Makkah, the qibla for Muslims.
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer, specifically when follower is outside and imam inside Ka'bah.
السترة (al-sutrah): An object placed in front of the praying person to prevent passersby from crossing in front of him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following relative positions between a follower and imam inside the Ka'bah invalidates the followership?
A) The follower's face is toward the imam's back.
B) The follower's back is toward the imam's face.
C) The follower's side is toward the imam's side.
D) The follower's face is toward the imam's face with a barrier.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid for both fard and nafl, praying on top is valid but makruh tanzih, and following an imam inside requires the follower to hear the takbir (door open or not) and not be closer to the Ka'bah than the imam in the imam's direction.

Validity of Prayer Inside and on Top of the Kaaba
Ruling on prayer in/on Kaaba with dislike explanation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer inside and on top of the Kaaba and identify the reason for dislike.

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid; above it is valid but disliked due to physical superiority over the House.

This lesson covers the unique case of performing salah inside or on top of the Kaaba. The Hanafi school affirms the validity of such prayer while noting an etiquette concern. Dislike is tanzihi (non-prohibitory) because the act itself is not sinful but shows disrespect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing salah (fard or nafil) inside or on top of the Kaaba. The ruling is sahih (valid).
The text says 'المصلي صح فرض ونفل فيها، وكذا فوقها'.
2
Note the exception for on top
Prayer on top is valid but makruh tanzihi due to bad manners (isaa'at al-adab) from being above the House.
The dislike is not prohibitory; the prayer is still valid.
3
Understand the lack of sutra requirement
No sutra (barrier in front) is needed because the Kaaba itself serves as the qibla direction.
The text states 'وإن لم يتخذ سترة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلاة في الكعبة
المصلي صح فرض ونفل فيها، وكذا فوقها وإن لم يتخذ سترة، لكنه مكروه؛ لإساءة الأدب باستعلائه عليها، ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها صح، وإن جعل ظهره إلى وجه إمامه لا يصح، وصح الاقتداء خارجها بإمام فيها والباب مفتوح، وإن تحلقوا حولها والإمام خارجها صح إلا لمن كان أقرب إليها في جهة إمامه.
من إمامه
لإساءة الأدب يفيد أن الكراهة للتنزيه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٧] ومن جعل إلخ: أي ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه، أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه متوجها إلى غير جهته أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه صح اقتداؤه في هذه الصور السبع، إلا أنه يكره إذا قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٧] وإن جعل ظهره إلخ تصريح بما علم التزاما من السابق لإيضاح الحكم، وذلك لتقدمه على إمامه.
[مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٨] فيها : أي في جوفها، سواء كان معه جماعة فيها أو لم تكن. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٨] والباب مفتوح: القيد بفتح الباب اتفاقي، فإذا سمع التبليغ والباب مغلق لا مانع من صحة الاقتداء. مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٨] إلا لمن كان إلخ أي صلى قوم صلاة حول الكعبة، وتحلقوا حولها، والإمام في جانب من جوانبها صح صلواتهم كلهم، ولكن لا يصح صلاة من كان في جهة إمامه وهو أقرب إليها من إمامه، مثلاً كان القوم مختلفين في البعد من الكعبة بحيث كان الإمام بقدر ذراعين من الكعبة، وبعضهم بقدر ذراعين وبعضهم بقدر ذراع واحد وبعضهم بقدر ثلاثة أذرع فصاعداً مثلاً، صلواتهم جميعاً، لكن لا يصح صلاة من كان بقدر ذراع وهو في جهة الإمام.
Chapter of Prayer in the Kaaba. The worshipper: obligatory and supererogatory prayer are valid in it, and likewise above it even if he does not take a sutra, but it is disliked due to bad manners from being above it. Whoever faces his back to other than the face of his imam in it or above it, it is valid. And if he faces his back to the face of his imam, it is not valid. And following [an imam] outside [the Kaaba] with an imam inside it is valid while the door is open. And if they form a circle around it with the imam outside, it is valid except for the one who is closer to it [the Kaaba] in the direction of his imam. From his imam: 'due to bad manners' indicates the dislike is tanzihi [non-prohibitory]. And 'Whoever faces his back' etc.: meaning whoever faces his back to other than the face of his imam in it or above it, such that his face is to the back of his imam, or his back is to the side of his imam, or his back is to the back of his imam, or his side is to the face of his imam, or his side is to the side of his imam facing other than his direction, or his face is to the face of his imam – his following is valid in these seven forms, except that it is disliked when he faces his face to the face of his imam with no barrier between them. [Muraqi al-Falah: 417] And 'If he faces his back' etc. is a clear statement of what was implicitly understood from the previous to clarify the ruling, because he is ahead of his imam. [Muraqi al-Falah: 418] 'In it': i.e., in its interior, whether there is a congregation with him in it or not. [Muraqi al-Falah: 418] 'And the door is open': the condition of the door being open is incidental; if he hears the relay and the door is closed, there is no obstacle to the validity of following. [Muraqi al-Falah: 418] 'Except for the one who is' etc.: meaning a group prayed around the Kaaba, forming a circle around it, with the imam on one of its sides – all their prayers are valid, but the prayer of the one who is in the direction of his imam and closer to it than his imam is not valid. For example, if the people differ in distance from the Kaaba such that the imam is two cubits from the Kaaba, some of them are two cubits, some one cubit, some three cubits and upwards, all their prayers are valid, but the prayer of the one who is one cubit and in the direction of the imam is not valid.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the validity of prayer inside or on top of the Kaaba. The author states that both obligatory and supererogatory prayers are valid in these locations, and it is not required to take a sutra (an object in front of the worshipper) because the Kaaba itself serves as a qibla. However, performing prayer on top of the Kaaba is considered makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked) because it shows disrespect by being physically above the sacred house. The passage then details the conditions for following an imam in prayer when the imam is inside the Kaaba and the follower is outside, or when the imam is outside and the followers form a circle around the Kaaba. The key point is that the follower must not face his back directly towards the imam's face; if he does, the prayer is invalid. Seven permissible configurations are enumerated, but facing the imam directly without a barrier is disliked. The commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Muraqi al-Falah clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (non-prohibitory) and that the condition of the door being open is not essential; hearing the takbir suffices. The exception regarding proximity: if a follower is closer to the Kaaba than the imam in the direction the imam is facing, his prayer is invalid because he would be ahead of the imam.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): In this passage, makruh refers to makruh tanzihi (non-prohibitory dislike) due to bad manners.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer; the validity conditions are specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which best describes the Hanafi ruling for praying on top of the Kaaba?
A) Valid and recommended.
B) Valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
C) Invalid because of lack of sutra.
D) Invalid because it is disrespectful.

Key Takeaway
The Kaaba's sanctity does not invalidate prayer inside it or on top, but respect requires avoiding being above it.

Conditions for Following an Imam Inside the Kaaba
Conditions for iqtida with imam inside Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for valid iqtida when the imam is inside the Kaaba and the follower is outside.

Core Idea
A follower outside the Kaaba can validly follow an imam inside, provided he does not face his back directly to the imam's face.

This lesson examines the specific rules for congregational prayer when the imam prays inside the Kaaba and the followers are outside. The Hanafi school allows this with precise conditions regarding the follower's orientation relative to the imam. The key is to avoid placing one's back directly opposite the imam's face.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic ruling
Iqtida is valid if the follower does not place his back directly opposite the imam's face. The passage lists seven permissible configurations.
The text says 'ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها صح'.
2
List the seven valid configurations
The commentary enumerates seven ways: face to back of imam, back to side, back to back, side to face, side to side (facing different direction), and face to face (but disliked).
These are all valid except the specific case of back to face.
3
Identify the invalid case
If the follower faces his back to the imam's face, the prayer is invalid ('لا يصح').
Also if the follower is ahead of the imam, as clarified later.
4
Consider the door condition
The door being open is incidental; what matters is hearing the takbir or seeing movements.
The commentary says 'والباب مفتوح: القيد بفتح الباب اتفاقي'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلاة في الكعبة
المصلي صح فرض ونفل فيها، وكذا فوقها وإن لم يتخذ سترة، لكنه مكروه؛ لإساءة الأدب باستعلائه عليها، ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها صح، وإن جعل ظهره إلى وجه إمامه لا يصح، وصح الاقتداء خارجها بإمام فيها والباب مفتوح، وإن تحلقوا حولها والإمام خارجها صح إلا لمن كان أقرب إليها في جهة إمامه.
من إمامه
لإساءة الأدب يفيد أن الكراهة للتنزيه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤١٧] ومن جعل إلخ: أي ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه، أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه، أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه متوجها إلى غير جهته أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه صح اقتداؤه في هذه الصور السبع، إلا أنه يكره إذا قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٧] وإن جعل ظهره إلخ تصريح بما علم التزاما من السابق لإيضاح الحكم، وذلك لتقدمه على إمامه.
[مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٨] فيها : أي في جوفها، سواء كان معه جماعة فيها أو لم تكن. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٨] والباب مفتوح: القيد بفتح الباب اتفاقي، فإذا سمع التبليغ والباب مغلق لا مانع من صحة الاقتداء. مراقي الفلاح: ٤١٨] إلا لمن كان إلخ أي صلى قوم صلاة حول الكعبة، وتحلقوا حولها، والإمام في جانب من جوانبها صح صلواتهم كلهم، ولكن لا يصح صلاة من كان في جهة إمامه وهو أقرب إليها من إمامه، مثلاً كان القوم مختلفين في البعد من الكعبة بحيث كان الإمام بقدر ذراعين من الكعبة، وبعضهم بقدر ذراعين وبعضهم بقدر ذراع واحد وبعضهم بقدر ثلاثة أذرع فصاعداً مثلاً، صلواتهم جميعاً، لكن لا يصح صلاة من كان بقدر ذراع وهو في جهة الإمام.
Chapter of Prayer in the Kaaba. The worshipper: obligatory and supererogatory prayer are valid in it, and likewise above it even if he does not take a sutra, but it is disliked due to bad manners from being above it. Whoever faces his back to other than the face of his imam in it or above it, it is valid. And if he faces his back to the face of his imam, it is not valid. And following [an imam] outside [the Kaaba] with an imam inside it is valid while the door is open. And if they form a circle around it with the imam outside, it is valid except for the one who is closer to it [the Kaaba] in the direction of his imam. From his imam: 'due to bad manners' indicates the dislike is tanzihi [non-prohibitory]. And 'Whoever faces his back' etc.: meaning whoever faces his back to other than the face of his imam in it or above it, such that his face is to the back of his imam, or his back is to the side of his imam, or his back is to the back of his imam, or his side is to the face of his imam, or his side is to the side of his imam facing other than his direction, or his face is to the face of his imam – his following is valid in these seven forms, except that it is disliked when he faces his face to the face of his imam with no barrier between them. [Muraqi al-Falah: 417] And 'If he faces his back' etc. is a clear statement of what was implicitly understood from the previous to clarify the ruling, because he is ahead of his imam. [Muraqi al-Falah: 418] 'In it': i.e., in its interior, whether there is a congregation with him in it or not. [Muraqi al-Falah: 418] 'And the door is open': the condition of the door being open is incidental; if he hears the relay and the door is closed, there is no obstacle to the validity of following. [Muraqi al-Falah: 418] 'Except for the one who is' etc.: meaning a group prayed around the Kaaba, forming a circle around it, with the imam on one of its sides – all their prayers are valid, but the prayer of the one who is in the direction of his imam and closer to it than his imam is not valid. For example, if the people differ in distance from the Kaaba such that the imam is two cubits from the Kaaba, some of them are two cubits, some one cubit, some three cubits and upwards, all their prayers are valid, but the prayer of the one who is one cubit and in the direction of the imam is not valid.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the validity of prayer inside or on top of the Kaaba. The author states that both obligatory and supererogatory prayers are valid in these locations, and it is not required to take a sutra (an object in front of the worshipper) because the Kaaba itself serves as a qibla. However, performing prayer on top of the Kaaba is considered makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked) because it shows disrespect by being physically above the sacred house. The passage then details the conditions for following an imam in prayer when the imam is inside the Kaaba and the follower is outside, or when the imam is outside and the followers form a circle around the Kaaba. The key point is that the follower must not face his back directly towards the imam's face; if he does, the prayer is invalid. Seven permissible configurations are enumerated, but facing the imam directly without a barrier is disliked. The commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Muraqi al-Falah clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (non-prohibitory) and that the condition of the door being open is not essential; hearing the takbir suffices. The exception regarding proximity: if a follower is closer to the Kaaba than the imam in the direction the imam is facing, his prayer is invalid because he would be ahead of the imam.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in congregational prayer; the validity conditions are specified.
حائل (ha'il): Barrier; the commentary mentions that face-to-face without a barrier is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for valid iqtida when the imam is inside the Kaaba and the follower outside?
A) The door of the Kaaba must be open.
B) The follower must not face his back to the imam's face.
C) The follower must be able to see the imam.
D) The follower must be closer to the Kaaba than the imam.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following an imam inside the Kaaba depends on orientation: avoid placing your back directly opposite the imam's face.

Circle Prayer Around the Kaaba and the Proximity Exception
Exception for circle prayer around Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a follower's prayer around the Kaaba is invalid due to being closer to the Kaaba than the imam in the same direction.

Core Idea
A follower must not be physically ahead of the imam; being closer to the Kaaba than the imam in the imam's facing direction invalidates the prayer.

This lesson examines a specific ruling for congregational prayer when worshippers form a circle around the Kaaba with the imam outside. All are valid except one: the follower who is in the same direction as the imam's face and closer to the Kaaba than the imam. This is because he is effectively ahead of the imam, which invalidates the iqtida.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
When worshippers form a circle around the Kaaba with the imam outside, all their prayers are valid generally.
The text says 'صح صلواتهم كلهم'.
2
Identify the exception
The prayer of the person who is in the direction of the imam's face and closer to the Kaaba than the imam is not valid.
The text says 'لا يصح صلاة من كان في جهة إمامه وهو أقرب إليها من إمامه'.
3
Understand the reason
This follower is ahead of the imam, which violates the condition that followers must not be ahead of the imam.
The commentary says 'لتقدمه على إمامه'.
4
Apply to an example
If imam is 2 cubits from Kaaba, and a follower in his direction is 1 cubit, that follower's prayer is invalid.
The passage gives this example.

Source Text

باب الصلاة في الكعبة

Checkpoint
When worshippers form a circle around the Kaaba with the imam outside, which follower's prayer is invalid?
A) Any follower who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam.
B) A follower who is closer to the Kaaba than the imam and in the imam's direction.
C) A follower who is in the imam's direction regardless of distance.
D) A follower who is not in the circle.

Key Takeaway
In circle prayer around the Kaaba, a follower must not be both in the imam's direction and closer to the Kaaba than the imam.

Definition and Types of Travel for Prayer Concessions
Definition of travel distance and types for concessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of travel that triggers concessions, classify travel into three types, and explain why sinful travel grants concessions in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The minimum travel for concessions is three days' moderate pace; even sinful travel qualifies in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Nur al-Idah defines the threshold for travel that changes legal rulings, such as shortening prayer and breaking fast. It also classifies travel into three categories and addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether sinful travel grants these concessions. By understanding this, you will grasp how the Hanafi school applies the general cause of travel without moral qualification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi minimum travel distance
Extract the definition: travel of three days' moderate pace including rest stops. Note that this is measured by duration, not distance, and that moderate pace is the average of camel and foot speed.
The estimation uses the shortest days of the year.
2
Classify the three types of travel
List travel of obedience (Hajj, jihad), permissible (trade), and sinful (highway robbery). Recognize that the first two are agreed upon as causes for concession.
The classification is based on the intention and nature of the journey.
3
Contrast the Hanafi position on sinful travel
Hanafi holds that sinful travel also grants concessions. The opposing schools (Malik, Shafi'i, Hanbali) deny this. Understand the basis: Hanafi applies the concession because the legal cause (travel hardship) is present regardless of sin.
The text does not provide the full opposing proof, but the principle is clear.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi, a bandit can shorten prayer; in other schools, he must pray full. This affects the validity of his salah.
Concessions are rukhsas, not obligations; the dispute is about their availability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المسافر
أقل سفر تتغير به الأحكام مسيرة ثلاثة أيام من أقصر أيام السنة بسير وسط مع الاستراحات، والوسط سير الإبل ومشي الأقدام في البر وفي الجبل بما يناسبه، وفي البحر اعتدال الريح،
أي إبل القافلة
المسافر: اعلم أنّ السفر على ثلاثة أقسام سفر طاعة كالحج والجهاد وسفر مباح كالتجارة، وسفر معصية: كقطع الطريق والأولان سببان للرخصة اتفاقاً، وأما الأخير فكذلك عندنا، خلافاً لمالك والشافعي وأحمد، فإنهم قالوا : سفر المعصية لا يفيد الرخصة. [ حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف وزيادة: ٤١٩]
ثلاثة هذا التقدير للسفر الذي تقصر فيه الصلاة، ويباح فيه الفطر، ويمسح فيه أكثر من يوم وليلة، وتسقط به الأضحية، وأما المبيح لترك الجمعة والعيدين والجماعة والمبيح للتنفل على الدابة وللتيمم، ولاستحباب القرعة بين نسائه، فلا يقدر بهذه المدة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤۲۱ أيام قدر بالأيام دون المراحل والفراسخ، وهو الأصح. مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١] بسير وسط : فلو أسرع بريده فقطع ما يقطع بالسير الوسط في ثلاثة أيام في أقل منها قصر، وكما إذا سار فيها سيراً خارقا للعادة، وصرح في "التبيين": أنه يكتفى في تقدير المسافة بالمدة المذكورة بغلبة الظن، ولا يشترط اليقين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢١] مع الاستراحات فينزل المسافر فيه للأكل والشرب وقضاء الضرورة ،والصلاة، ولأكثر النهار حكم كله، قاصداً محلاً، وبكر في اليوم الأول وسار إلى وقت الزوال حتى بلغ المرحلة، فنزل بها للاستراحة وبات بها، ثم بكر في اليوم الثاني وسار إلى ما بعد الزوال ونزل، ثم بكّر في الثالث وسار إلى الزوال فبلغ المقصد، قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : الصحيح أنه مسافر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١]
وفي الجبل إلخ أي ويعتبر السير الوسط في الجبل بما يناسبه؛ لأنه يكون صعوداً وهبوطا ومضيقاً ووعرا، فيكون مشي الإبل والأقدام فيه دون سيرهما في السهل، فإذا قطع بذلك السير مسافة ليست ببعيدة . من ابتداء اليوم ونزل بعد الزوال، احتسب به على نحو ما قدمناه يوماً، فإذا بات ثم أصبح وفعل كذلك إلى ما بعد الزوال ثم نزل، كان يوماً ثانياً، ولا يعتبر أعجل السير، وهو سير البريد، ولا أبطأ السير، وهو مشي العجلة التي تجرها الدواب، فإن الأمور أوساطها، وهو هنا سير الإبل والأقدام [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١]
وفي البحر أي وفي البحر يعتبر اعتدال الريح على المفتى به فينظر إلى السفينة كم تسير في ثلاثة أيام ولياليها عند استواء الريح بحيث لم تكن عاصفة ولا هادئة فيجعل ذلك أصلاً، فإذا سار أكثر اليوم به كان ككله وإن كانت المسافة دون ما في السهل حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١)
Chapter of the Traveler's Prayer. The minimum travel by which rulings change is a journey of three days of the shortest days of the year with moderate pace including rest stops. The moderate pace is the speed of camels and walking on foot on land, and in the mountain what suits it, and at sea moderate wind. i.e., camels of the caravan. The traveler: Know that travel is of three types: travel of obedience like Hajj and jihad, permissible travel like trade, and sinful travel like highway robbery. The first two are causes for concession by consensus. As for the last, likewise according to us, contrary to Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, for they said: sinful travel does not grant concession. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with omission and addition: 419] 'Three days': This estimation for travel in which prayer is shortened, breaking the fast is permitted, wiping over socks for more than a day and night is allowed, and the udhiyah sacrifice is waived. As for what permits leaving Friday, Eid prayers, congregation, and permits voluntary prayer on a riding animal and tayammum, and the recommendation of drawing lots among his wives, these are not estimated by this duration. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 421] 'Days' were estimated by days, not by stages or leagues, and that is the most correct. [Muraqi al-Falah: 421] 'With moderate pace': If he hastens his post-horse and covers what is covered by moderate pace in three days in less than that, he shortens, and likewise if he travels in it with extraordinary speed. It is stated in al-Tabyin that in estimating the distance by the mentioned duration, predominant probability suffices, certainty is not required. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 421] 'With rest stops': So the traveler alights for eating, drinking, relieving nature, and prayer, and the majority of the day has the ruling of the whole day, intending a place. He set out early on the first day and traveled until noon until he reached the stage, then alighted there for rest and stayed the night, then set out early on the second day and traveled until after noon and alighted, then set out early on the third and traveled until noon and reached the destination. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: Correct that he is a traveler. [Muraqi al-Falah: 421] 'And in the mountain' etc.: i.e., moderate pace in the mountain is considered what suits it, because it involves ascent and descent, narrowness and ruggedness, so the walking of camels and feet there is less than their walking on plain ground. If one covers by that pace a distance not far from the start of the day and alights after noon, it is counted as a day according to what we mentioned. Then if he stays the night and then does likewise until after noon and then alights, it is a second day. The fastest pace, which is the post-horse speed, is not considered, nor the slowest pace, which is the walking of a cart pulled by animals, for the best of things are their middles, and here it is the pace of camels and feet. [Muraqi al-Falah: 421] 'And at sea': i.e., at sea moderate wind is considered according to the mufta bihi. One looks at how far the ship sails in three days and nights when the wind is steady, neither stormy nor calm, and makes that the basis. If it sails more than a day by that, it counts as the whole, even if the distance is less than on land. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Muraqi al-Falah: 421]
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage defines the travel distance that triggers legal concessions (rukhsas) such as shortening prayer, breaking fast in Ramadan, wiping over socks for three days, and waiving the udhiyah sacrifice. The minimum distance is measured by a three-day journey using a moderate pace (sabil al-wasat) including rest stops. The moderate pace is defined as the average speed of camels and walking on land, adapted for mountainous terrain, and at sea, a moderate wind speed. The passage then classifies travel into three types: obedient, permissible, and sinful. According to the Hanafi school, all three types grant concessions, contrary to Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad who hold that sinful travel does not. The estimation by days is preferred over stages or leagues. The commentary clarifies that if one travels faster and covers the distance in less than three days, the concession still applies. The intention to travel and the practical schedule of rest stops are important; the traveler must intend a specific destination. Scholars like Sarakhsi confirm that even if the journey takes less than three days due to speed, the traveler status is established. The method of counting days is also explained: starting early and traveling until noon each day, with overnight stops. The passage concludes with sea travel: the moderate wind speed determines the distance equivalent to three days' journey, and if the ship sails for most of the day, it counts as a full day.

Key Terms
سفر (safar): Travel of three days' moderate pace that changes legal rulings.
رخصة (rukhsah): Legal concession granted due to hardship of travel, e.g., shortening prayer, breaking fast.
سير وسط (sayr wasat): Moderate pace of travel, specifically camel's pace and walking on foot, not extreme fast or slow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which types of travel grant legal concessions (rukhsas)?
A) Only travel for Hajj and Jihad.
B) Only permissible travel like trade.
C) Both obedient and permissible travel, but not sinful travel.
D) All types of travel, including sinful travel.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines travel for concessions by a three-day moderate journey and applies the concession to all travel, including sinful, based on the general cause of hardship.
